*** HIGH-STAKES THINKING BOX (v7.13 — MANDATORY) ***

After each street-by-street replay, include a "High-Stakes
Thinking" box. This goes beyond the single hand Hero showed
up with — it forces range-based analysis.

REQUIRED CONTENT:

  **High-Stakes Thinking**

  Villain's range at each decision point:
    PREFLOP (action X): [Named combos — value, bluff, flat candidates.
                         Don't say "a wide range" — list the hands.]
    FLOP (action Y):    [After the flop action, what narrows from the
                         preflop range? Which hands got to this action?]
    TURN (action Z):    [Same for turn.]
    RIVER (action W):   [Range at showdown / final decision.]

  How the optimal line changes across villain's full range:
    vs Value slice ([specific combos]): [what's correct — bet/check/
                                          fold-size/call-size]
    vs Bluff slice ([specific combos]): [what's correct]
    vs Medium slice ([specific combos]): [what's correct]
    The "correct" single action is the one that performs best
    AGGREGATED across this mix — not the one that happened to beat
    the hand villain showed.

  Population tendency this play exploits or fails to exploit:
    [Which specific population leak applies here? E.g., "Villains
    at this stake under-bluff rivers after calling turn — so checking
    behind thin value is OK, but folding to a river bet is too tight."]

  Aggressor vs Reactor:
    [Was Hero the Aggressor or the Reactor on this hand?
    How would the EV change if Hero had taken the opposite role?]

Plus: Top 5 Errors (punts + mistakes), 5 Discipline Spots.

For each leak, include AT MINIMUM:
  - Caller IP Flop Agg: show hands where Hero checked a draw
    IP as caller, with the draw type and what bet would have
    been correct
  - Missed C-Bet: show the board, Hero's hand, IP/OOP, why
    a c-bet was correct (with sizing)
  - Missed River Value: show the full 5-street action to see
    HOW Hero ended up with 0-1 streets of value
  - Fold-to-3Bet: show hands where Hero folded to 3-bet that
    should have continued (with stack/range context)
  - Missed Steals: show the hand + table context

PREFLOP DEVIATION EXAMPLES (v7.2 — NEW):
For each deviation type with CLEAR flags, include 2-3 examples:

  - Wide Open: show the hand, position, depth, what the OPEN
    chart says for that position/depth, and outcome. Note:
    "Won this time ≠ correct. Range file says fold from HJ."
  - Missed Rejam: show Hero's flat vs the REJAM chart. Include
    opener position, Hero's stack, and why jamming was better
    (fold equity + equity when called > flatting EV).
  - Missed Defend/3-Bet: show what Hero folded, the FLAT3B
    chart that says continue, and whether a flat or 3-bet was
    the intended action.
  - Wide BB Defend: show what Hero called with from BB, the
    BB_DEF chart for that opener width, and the postflop result.
    Pattern: calling wide from BB then losing postflop = leak.
  - Missed Call-Rejam / Wide Call-Rejam: show the jam spot,
    CALLRJ chart, and whether Hero's call/fold was correct.

For preflop-only hands, the Hand Replay Template simplifies:
  HAND: TM### (Tournament Name, Date)
  HERO: [Cards] | [Position] | [Stack]BB | [Format]
  PREFLOP: [Full action sequence]

*** DRILL THREE-QUESTION FRAMEWORK (v7.13 — MANDATORY) ***

Every drill hand in Del 7 MUST require three answers from Hero
BEFORE revealing the result. Do not accept single-street answers.
If Hero only gives a flop action, ask "and what's your turn and
river plan?"

The three questions (all required, in order):

  1. RANGE MAPPING
     "Map villain's range — what hands are they taking this line
     with? Value hands, bluffs, made draws, blockers — list them.
     Don't say 'a strong hand' — name the combos."

  2. STREET-BY-STREET PLAN (ALL remaining streets + abort cards)
     "What's your plan for ALL remaining streets? For each street:
      - Which cards continue the aggression?
      - Which cards abort (check/fold)?
      - Which sizing on each planned bet?
      - What's the response if villain raises?
     Single-street answers are not accepted."

  3. POPULATION EXPLOIT
     "What population tendency are you exploiting here? Name the
     specific leak: under-bluffs rivers? Over-cbets? Over-folds
     to small river bets? Under-3bets?"

OUTPUT FORMAT FOR DRILL HAND:

  ## Drill Hand [N]
  **Situation:** [brief spot description]
  **Board:** [if postflop]
  **Hero's hand:** [cards]
  **Stack/Position:** [BB and position]

  **Q1: Map villain's range.**
  [Wait for answer. Don't proceed.]

  **Q2: Plan all remaining streets.**
  [Wait for answer. Probe for abort cards if missing.]

  **Q3: What population tendency are you exploiting?**
  [Wait for answer.]

  --- after all 3 answered ---
  **Result/Coaching:** [full analysis]

DELIVERABLE 9 — DEEP RUN & RECOVERY TRACKER
========================================================

| Tournament | Format | Hands | Levels | Start | Low | Peak (after low) | Final |

CRITICAL: "Peak" column must show the max stack AFTER the low
point, NOT the overall tournament peak. If Hero peaked at 200BB
then crashed to 3BB then recovered to 15BB, the survival story
is "3BB → 15BB", not "3BB → 200BB." The 200BB was before the
crash and is irrelevant to the recovery narrative.

Calculation: Find the index of the minimum stack. Then take
max(stacks[min_index:]) as the recovery peak.

Flag SURVIVAL STORY if Hero hit <5BB and recovered to >3x that
low point (using max-after-low, not overall max).
Flag DEEP RUN (20+ levels).
Describe key comeback hands for survival stories.

the highest-pressure, highest-ICM spots in the session.

For each of the last 10 hands, output:

Then for any hand with postflop action, provide:

  FLOP: Board texture, Hero's action, sizing check, coaching rule
  TURN: Card, equity shift?, Hero's action, sizing check
  RIVER: Card, Hero's action, was value/bluff correct?, missed value?

Focus on:
  - Bust-out hands: Was the bust decision correct for the stack/ICM?
  - Bubble hands: Did Hero tighten appropriately or too much?
  - Final table hands: Stack-aware decisions, pay jump awareness
  - Short-stack hands: Push/fold compliance, limp strategy (App H)
  - Any hand where Hero folded — was it a correct fold or a missed
    spot given the stack/position/ICM pressure?

This is the most coach-like section of the report. Write it as
if reviewing with Amit or Dave — specific, actionable, no padding.

========================================================
NON-NEGOTIABLE PARSING RULES
========================================================

EFFECTIVE STACK RULE:
All analysis uses EFFECTIVE stack (min of Hero + relevant villain).
"Deep All-In >40BB" = 40BB effective. "Panic Punt >20BB" = 20BB eff.
SB jams vs short BB = evaluate at BB's stack.

PUNT vs MISTAKE CLASSIFICATION (v7.0):

PUNT = Reckless, emotionally driven play. Chips go in badly
with little strategic merit. Active error — Hero DID something
destructive. Punts correlate with tilt.
  Examples: Shoving 77 into a multiway pot at 60BB.
  Escalating after villain resistance. Panic jam with air.
  Over-jamming after getting check-raised. 3-bet bluff-shoving
  a hand with no equity. Calling off a stack with bottom pair.

MISTAKE = Passive error or missed opportunity. Systemic/habitual
leak. Hero DIDN'T do something they should have. Mistakes
correlate with habit and incomplete internalization of rules.
  Examples: Folding a steal hand first-in. Not c-betting HU
  as PFR. Missing river value. Not opening from BTN with a
  hand that's clearly in range. Checking monotone board IP
  when IP PFR on monotone should c-bet (J14).

This distinction matters for mental game tracking:
  - Punts → tilt analysis (which of the 7 types?)
  - Mistakes → L3→L4 mastery gap (knows the rule, hasn't
    automated it yet)
  - A session with 0 punts and 8 mistakes = clean mental game,
    systemic leaks to drill.
  - A session with 5 punts and 2 mistakes = tilt problem.

Track separately: Punts/100 AND Mistakes/100.
Won punts still count toward Punts/100 but NOT BB Lost.

FORMAT-AWARE ERROR DETECTION:
Check bounty/freezeout/satellite before classifying squeezes/jams.
Bounty + Hero covers = wider ranges correct.
Freezeout/satellite = stricter ranges.

BOARD TEXTURE:
Connected-Middling = 3 unpaired cards in 5-J range, ≤2 gaps.
Paired boards are NEVER connected-middling.

SB SIZING: Exclude open-jams from avg. Flag Min-Raise <2.5BB.

MISSED STEAL: Only when Hero folds without raising. Fold-to-3bet
is separate. Don't count fold-to-3bet in open %.

ICM CONTEXT: Note tournament phase. Early = no ICM excuse.
Late = tighter folds may be correct. Bounty = softer ICM.

CO OPEN RANGE (40+BB):
No offsuit lower <9 (except Aces, not A7o/A6o). K7o NOT standard.
Any suited broadway, suited connector, pocket pair = open.
T7o/76o NOT opens or jams from CO at 15BB.

RANGE VERIFICATION (v6.9):
Before classifying ANY preflop action as a punt or missed play,
search Poker_Ranges_Text.txt for the relevant chart. This is
mandatory for: missed steals, wide opens, push/fold violations,
3-bet evaluations, BB defense evaluations, and rejam decisions.
If the hand is NOT in the range file AND NOT in a coaching rule
exception, it's a stronger punt classification. If it IS in the
range file but violates a coaching rule, note the conflict.

STRATEGIC RULES (confirmed):
- Sub-12BB = push/fold only. 12-15BB = min-raise OK.
- QJs ~35BB vs squeeze = shove/fold, not call.
- SPR ~1 = don't shove, lure over streets.
- 77 facing jam with players behind = fold.
- Paired boards = bet high frequency (but see Appendix A for
  nuance: 88x/77x = heavy check, 22x/33x = bet more freely,
  always small sizing on paired boards).
- After check-check on flop = attack turn.
- Monotone boards = check air, bet strong made hands.
- Trips on 3-flush + villain raises = fold.
- 3-bet pots = PFR c-bets at higher frequency.
- BB check-raise preferred over donking as non-PFR.
- Escalating commitment after resistance = confirmed leak.
- Jam Question (>20BB): What calls that I beat? What folds that
  has equity? 4-flush or 3-flush with one pair?

*** CALL VILLAIN JAM (CVJ) CLASSIFICATION (v7.10 — NEW) ***

When villain_jammed=True AND Hero calls (pf_action='call'):
  1. Determine villain's EFFECTIVE POSITION (use eff_pos for table size)
  2. Determine villain's stack in BB (jam size)
  3. Evaluate Hero's hand vs estimated jam range:
     - VS EP JAM (<15BB): call with 88+, ATs+, AJo+, KQs
     - VS EP JAM (15-25BB): call with TT+, AQs+, AKo
     - VS MP JAM: slightly wider than EP
     - VS LP JAM (<15BB): call with 66+, A9s+, ATo+, KQs, KJs
     - VS LP JAM (15-25BB): call with 88+, ATs+, AJo+
  4. If Hero's hand is BELOW threshold → flag as CLEAR CVJ Mistake
  5. If Hero's hand is borderline → flag as MARGINAL CVJ
  6. Include villain position + stack in flag output

  Example: A8o calling UTG 8.6BB jam from SB = CLEAR CVJ mistake
  (A8o not in 88+/ATs+/AJo+ range for EP jam call)

  Session 19 miss: TM5803303634 (Ah8s calling UTG jam, -2.47EV per GTO)

*** ISO-JAM EVALUATOR (v7.10 — NEW) ***

When Hero raises over a villain's all-in (Hero 3-bets/raises and
villain was already all-in):
  1. Same position + stack evaluation as CVJ
  2. TIGHTER thresholds (players behind can wake up with premiums):
     - VS EP JAM: iso with TT+, AQs+, AKo
     - VS MP JAM: iso with 99+, AJs+, AQo+
     - VS LP JAM: iso with 77+, ATs+, AJo+, KQs
  3. If Hero's hand is below threshold → flag as CLEAR Iso-Jam Mistake

  Example: QTo iso-jamming over EP 7.8BB jam = CLEAR mistake
  (QTo not in TT+/AQs+/AKo range)

  Session 19 miss: TM5803173488 (QdTc iso over EP jam)

*** ICM PRESSURE FLAG (v7.10 — NEW) ***

When the tournament is in a pressure zone (FT bubble, FT, HU bubble):
  Detect via: n_players relative to format's payout structure.
  Heuristic: if n_players <= 2× FT size (e.g., <=16 for 8-max FT),
  or if tournament name contains "Bounty King" and n_players is
  small, apply ICM modifiers:

  At >30BB with ICM pressure:
  - 3-bet jamming with 88-TT = MARGINAL (standard at 25BB, too deep at 35BB+)
  - 3-bet jamming with 99 at 37BB near bubble = flag for review
  - Opening ranges unchanged, but jam ranges contract

  Session 19 miss: TM5803509744 (99 SB 37BB jam near bubble)

  NOTE: Parser cannot detect exact players remaining in tournament.
  Use heuristic: if level >= 20 and stack > 30BB, apply ICM caution
  flag to medium-pair jams.

*** FT FLAT ALERT (v7.10 — Dave) ***

At Final Table (n_players ≤ 9 at 9-max, ≤ 8 at 8-max, or detected
via late levels + small table size):
  - Flatting an EP open = raise ALERT
  - Correct action at FT: raise/fold, not flat
  - Exception: deep-stacked (>80BB) with speculative hand and good
    implied odds

  Session 19 example: TM5803086037 (A3s flatting UTG open from HJ
  at 31BB, FT of Bounty King). Should have folded or 3-bet.

  RULE: At FT, if Hero flats an EP/MP open, flag as "FT Flat Alert"
  in the mistakes section with note "FT raise/fold preferred."

*** EXPECTED VALUES IN ALL TABLES (v7.10 — NEW) ***

EVERY table in the report that shows a count, rate, or percentage
MUST include an "Expected" or "Target" column and color coding:
  🟢 = within target range or better
  🟡 = borderline (within 10% of target boundary)
  🔴 = outside target range, needs attention

This applies to:
  - EAI tables (always show Expected win% column)
  - Positional open rates (show target range per position)
  - C-bet rates (show 60-65% HU, 30-40% MW targets)
  - Bluff profile (show 55-65% value, 20-30% semi, 10-20% pure)
  - Caller IP aggression (show 30-40% target)
  - SD Aggressor (show >40% target)
  - WWSF (show 42-48% target)
  - Non-SD Win (show 25-35% target)
  - F2-3B (show 55-65% target)
  - SB BvB (show ~80% limp / ~10% raise / ~10% fold)
  - Stack depth tiers (show appropriate targets per tier)
  - Facing bets fold% by street (show reasonable ranges)
  - River audit (show expected distribution)

A table without expected/target context is INCOMPLETE.

*** MISSED STEAL STACK CONTEXT (v7.10 — NEW) ***

When flagging a missed steal, the parser MUST also report:
  - Stacks of players behind Hero (BTN, SB, BB)
  - Flag if any player behind has a reshove stack (<15BB)
  - If reshove stack behind: downgrade CLEAR → MARGINAL for
    marginal hands (e.g., JTo CO with 5.6BB BTN = MARGINAL)
  - If all stacks behind are >25BB: standard steal evaluation applies

*** GGPOKER REVERSE CHRONOLOGICAL ORDER (v7.11 — FIX) ***

GGPoker hand history files store hands in REVERSE chronological
order — the most recent hand is FIRST in the file. The parser
reads in file order, so hands[0] = newest, hands[-1] = oldest.

IMPACT: Deep run stack trajectories must REVERSE the hand list
before computing start/peak/low/final. Without reversal, start
and final are swapped.

The parser now reverses per-tournament hand lists in the deep
run tracker. All other analysis (session-wide stats) is
unaffected since aggregate stats don't depend on order.

*** SURVIVAL STORY FORMAT (v7.11 — NEW) ***

Every deep run with survival=True (low < start×0.3 AND
recovery > low×2) gets a narrative paragraph in the report.

FORMAT RULES:
  1. Written in FIRST PERSON (as if Hero wrote it)
  2. Chronological order (reverse the file order)
  3. Card quality woven into the narrative (explains the bleed)
  4. Key hands with full context (position, stack, action, board)
  5. Tournament-specific EAI at the end (actual vs expected)
  6. NO TABLES — text-message friendly (can be copy-pasted)
  7. Don't say "champion" — say what it actually took
     (e.g., "all it needed was 6/6 flips and 5/6 when behind")
  8. Note ICM context for bubble folds (don't call them mistakes
     if ITM bubble explains the tightening)
  9. Multiway all-ins are highlights — always mention them

*** GTO WIZARD EXPORT FORMAT (v7.11 — NEW) ***

The GTO Review file MUST be in native GGPoker hand history
format — raw hand text extracted from the input files, NOT
hand IDs or summaries. The file must be directly importable
into GTO Wizard without conversion.

CONTENTS: Include ALL of the following hand categories:
  - GTO Review Shortlist (interesting spots for review)
  - All CLEAR mistakes (missed steals, missed pushes, CVJ, etc.)
  - All MARGINAL mistakes
  - All CVJ / Iso-Jam / ICM Pressure Flag hands
  - All FT Flat Alert hands
  - Missed river value hands
  - Missed probe hands

METHOD: Extract raw hand text from input files by matching
Poker Hand #TM{id} and copying the full hand block.

*** <8BB PUSH/FOLD METRIC (v7.11 — NEW) ***

Tracked separately from missed steals. Appears in report as:
  "Missed Push/Reshove <8BB: X (Y clear)"

This captures the systematic ultra-short-stack leak where Hero
folds hands that should be pushed at <8BB. Different from missed
steals (which use open-raise ranges) because push/fold ranges at
<8BB are MUCH wider than open ranges.

Parser tracks: push_fold_lt8bb_misses, push_fold_lt8bb_clear.
Per-tournament counts appear in deep run data.

*** FT DETECTION LIMITATIONS (v7.11 — NOTE) ***

FT Flat Alert requires TWO conditions:
  1. n_players < table_size (seats have emptied)
  2. level >= 15 (not early tournament)

This is HEURISTIC — it can fire at short-handed tables that
aren't actual final tables (e.g., after rebalance, or in
sit-and-go formats). The flag includes requires_confirmation=True.

The report MUST note "confirm FT" on every FT Flat Alert.
User should verify whether the hand was actually at a final
table before treating it as a mistake.

ITM BUBBLE: Cannot be estimated from GGPoker hand histories.
Files don't include total field size or remaining players.
Use level + stack compression + table emptying as proxies,
but always note uncertainty.

PARSING RULES:
- Hole cards from "Dealt to" or "Shows" lines only.
- Always state suits explicitly.
- ITM% by Bullets, not tournaments.
- SB standard = 3.0BB. Min-raise <2.5BB = leak.
- Process 100% of hands. No sampling.
- Batch if needed. Never output final tables until ALL batches done.

PARSER TRACKING — v6.9 ADDITIONS:
- BET SIZING: For every Hero bet/raise, record size as % of pot.
  Tag by: street, spot type (PFR cbet/probe/donk/barrel/value/bluff),
  IP vs OOP. Aggregate into sizing profile tables.
- FACING BET: For every villain bet Hero faces, record villain's
  size as % of pot and Hero's response (fold/call/raise).
  Aggregate by street and sizing bucket (small/med/large).
- BOARD TEXTURE: Classify every flop as: Paired, Monotone,
  Connected-Middling, Dry-A-high, Dynamic, Low-dry.
  Track Hero's c-bet frequency and win rate per board type.
- RIVER ACTIONS: Track Hero's river action (value/bluff/check-SDV/
  check-giveup when checked to; fold/call/raise when facing bet).
  Track showdown results for river calls.
- PREFLOP DEVIATIONS: For every hand, compare Hero's preflop
  action against Poker_Ranges_Text.txt. Log mismatches with
  hand ID. Output full deviation list + top 10 summary.
- LAST 10 HANDS: For each tournament, extract the final 10 hands
  with full action sequences for street-by-street review.

GOOGLE SHEETS EXPORT ROW:
Date, Batch ID, Hands, BB/100, VPIP, PFR, 3Bet, <12BB Errors, Top Leak


========================================================
APPENDIX A — JAKA COACHING FRAMEWORK
(Postflop Evaluation Rules)
========================================================
Source: Jaka coaching curriculum (WSOP Prep series + study materials)
Note: Dave may have different opinions on specific spots.
When Dave-specific rules conflict, they take precedence for
punt evaluation. Jaka framework is the baseline.


A. C-BET AS PFR (IP) vs BB — BOARD CATEGORIZATION
--------------------------------------------------------

FREQUENCY DECISION TREE:
| Category     | Freq  | Board Profile                                      | Sizing               |
| Bet Range    | ~100% | A/K high. Q/J/T high where other 2 cards NOT both  | Small (1/3) unless   |
|              |       | connected BB cards (8 and below)                    | double str8 draws    |
| Heavy Bet    | ~66%  | Q/J/T high + 2 connected BB cards (8-4) at 40bb.   | Polar: big or check  |
|              |       | OR no face card + BB has offsuit 2-pair combos      |                      |
| Heavy Check  | ~50%  | All cards ≤8 + BB has most offsuit 2-pair combos.   | Small only when bet  |
|              |       | OR paired boards 88 and below                       |                      |

SIZING RULES:
- Paired boards: ALWAYS small sizing (1/3 pot). Lower pair = less
  worried (33x/22x bet more freely than 77x/88x).
- A high paired (e.g., A88): Bet range small.
- Double straight draws: Size UP. More possible straights = bigger bet.
- Single str8 draw (Q82): Normal. Double str8 draw (Q84, J76): Bigger.
- Range bet + no straight draws: Can size DOWN to 25%.
- Simplification: Mostly 66% + some 33% → use 60%. Mostly 33% + some
  66% → use 40-50%.

HAND SELECTION:
- Heavy check boards: Check AA/KK (less protection). Bet 99-JJ (need
  protection from overcards). Check AK/AQ/KQ (SDV). Bet J9s/Q9s/A3s
  (less SDV, board connectivity).
- Paired boards ≤8: Check AA/KK, mix QQ. Bet 77-JJ for protection.
- Flush draw equity: Check back hands WITH the flush draw suit (don't
  waste equity if CR'd). Bet hands WITHOUT it. EXCEPTION at deep stacks:
  reverse — x/r with FD when deep (need equity for big pot).

STACK DEPTH:
- Ax boards at 30bb: C-bet freq drops from ~85% to ~35% (IP flats A9s+
  at 30bb, dominating OOP's Ax).
- Paired boards: Deeper = more checking (reverse implied odds vs trips).

BOARD QUIZ REFERENCE:
872=Heavy Bet. 875=Heavy Check. 654=Heavy Check. J78=Heavy Bet.
T65=Heavy Bet. K63=Range Bet. QT3=Range Bet. Q85=Heavy Bet (polar).
J88=Heavy Check. A88=Bet Range. Q33=Bet Range. K66=Heavy Check.
88x/77x/66x/55x/44x = HEAVY CHECK (exception: A high).

BLANKS FOR BB AFTER CALLING C-BET:
K87 → blanks: A, 2, 3 (cards 4-T hit BB range).
A96 → blanks: 2, 3, 4 (cards 5-T hit BB range).
KT7 → blanks: 2-5.


B. C-BET AS PFR (OOP)
--------------------------------------------------------

EP vs CO:
- Turn when 2 draws complete (str8 + flush): Very small ~15% pot, bet wide.
- Rainbow boards OOP: Big betting on lower flops when opp has overs + BDFDs.
- Monotone: More small betting. Can simplify to checking some boards.
- Pot-size on rainbow: Low + str8 draws = more checking. Low + no str8 =
  increase freq, 75-100% pot.
- Paired boards OOP: Pair they don't have (22-44) = more pot-sizing.
  Higher pairs (55-77) = less pot-sizing, 60% sizing OK on rainbow.
  Medium paired two-tone (775, 774) = 60% OK. Low paired two-tone
  (332, 223) = no big betting.
- Summary: More str8 draws w/ low cards = less big betting. Pair they
  don't have = more pot-sizing. Rainbow > two-tone. Broadway + pair = bigger.

CO vs BU (key differences):
- Wider ranges → less big betting, more balancing needed.
- K high boards: Heavy checking at both depths (Kxs flatted heavily by BU).
  Exploit: If villains don't flat Kxs enough → increase c-bet freq.
- 1BB bets: On K/Qx + broadway boards from range advantage.
- 30bb: Bet more on 3 mid/low boards (IP not flatting suited connectors).
- Population: Can bet more overall — people don't raise OOP c-bets enough.


C. CHECK-RAISING FROM THE BB
--------------------------------------------------------

BLUFF SELECTION:
1. Gutshots ± backdoor flush draws.
2. Flush draws with backdoor straight draws (combo draws preferred).
3. Overcard flush draw BLOCKERS — very powerful. e.g., Ks4x on Js5s2x.
   Ace of flush draw suit = strongest CR blocker.
4. Cards wrapping around top card with backdoor flush draws.

CHECK-RAISING TOP PAIR:
- Always CR: TPTK.
- Usually CR: Top pair 2nd kicker.
- Conditional CR: TPMK if IP c-bets range or many underpairs on board.

CHECK-RAISING FOR PROTECTION:
- Bottom/2nd pair qualifies IF: pair ≤6 AND backdoor str8 draw.
- SHALLOW: x/c WITH BDFD (don't get shoved off equity). x/r WITHOUT BDFD.
- DEEP: x/r WITH BDFD (need equity for big pot). Don't x/r without BDFD
  when deep (reverse implied odds).

WHAT NOT TO CR:
- Unders to top pair (A8 on A97): Not enough equity unless fully unblocking
  folds from 88/99. Prefer 56s/76s type hands.

SIZING:
- Standard: ~2.5x (need ~1/3 folds to profit).
- Deep/polarized: 3x-3.5x (uncommon).
- After CR, flush completes on turn: ALWAYS 1/3 sizing (wider value range
  including 2-pair/sets, cheap bluffs).
- Most turns after CR: Small sizings.

CR vs CHECK-SHOVE:
- Only check-SHOVE if remaining stack after calling ≤ pot size.

TURN AFTER CR:
- Broadway turns favor IP → lower bet freq.
- Small blank turns favor OOP → higher bet freq.

IP RESPONSE (POPULATION LEAK):
- Population doesn't CR enough AND overfolds to CRs. Our CR bluffs print.


D. RAISING C-BETS (MULTIWAY)
--------------------------------------------------------

- A-high low boards (A32 fd) MW: PFR c-bets only ~7% at 1/3 pot. Mostly
  AJ+ flush draws, gutshots like K5s/K4s.
- BTN almost never raises MW on A-high boards.
- BB CR range MW: Obvious str8/flush draws (43s, 5xss, 2xss). Non-obvious
  bluffs: bottom/middle low pair UNBLOCKING big card folds (73s, Q2s, 72s
  no BDFD).
- After CR, offsuit 5x/4x turn: Bet range. Shove 73s/72s w/o flush draw
  specifically — folds out tons of flush draws.
- T22r MW: PFR checks ~39%. CO bets 66% when checked to. BB barely calls,
  must CR at high frequency.
- After getting CR'd: Check back medium Qx on turn to keep strong hands
  mixed with protection-raised pairs.


E. PROBE BETS & DONK BETS FROM BB
--------------------------------------------------------

TURN PROBE TRIGGERS (after PFR checks back flop):
- Board favorable for BB (all low, connected middling, middling board pairs)
  AND Hero has draws/improvement.
- Made hand needing protection.
- Opponent capped + turn unlikely to help.
- Very favorable: Consider leading entire range (e.g., 4568).

TURN CARD PROBE FREQUENCY:
- 2-8: Highest (favor BB range).
- 9/T/J: Neutral, moderate frequency.
- A/K/Q: Very infrequent (favor opponent's range).

PROBE SIZING:
- Large % of range wants to bet → small/medium.
- Small % → large/overpot.
- Strongest hands → larger. Paired turns favoring BB → large.
- Rarely overpot multiway.

TURN DONK BET TRIGGERS (after CALLING a flop c-bet):
- Turn swings equity in BB's favor AND Hero has improvement outs.
- Middle/bottom card on flop pairs on turn.
- Top card pairs IF it's a BB card (6, 7, 8 — not A, K, Q).
- Turn completes draws BB is more likely to have.

WHY DONK:
- Prevents IP positional exploitation. Generates cheap folds.
- Builds pots when turn improves us AND opponent would check back.
- Sets up river bluffs on favorable boards.


F. PLAYING VS CAPPED RANGES
--------------------------------------------------------

IDENTIFYING CAPPED:
1. IP checks flop as PFR (strongest signal).
2. IP checks back turn after c-betting (especially on dynamic boards).
3. Player checked multiple streets.
4. Harder to identify multiway (strong hands may be checked MW).

TURN vs CAPPED:
- Strong draws + top pair+: Large sizes aggressively, especially dynamic boards.
- Mediocre (2nd/3rd pair): Small block bets.
- Weak SDV (ace high no draws, bottom pair no draws): Keep checking.
- BB-favorable boards: Play aggressively.

RIVER vs CAPPED:
- Strong: Bet for value, size for their calling range.
- Mediocre SDV: Check, hope to win showdown.
- No SDV: Evaluate as bluff. Size for max folds.
- Marginal SDV unlikely to win → turn into bluff-raise when villain bets
  capped and we block their calling range.


G. OVERBETTING
--------------------------------------------------------

AS PFR — TURN OVERBETS:
- Flop has lots of BB draws + turn is blank for those draws → big bet.
  If blank is undercard → overbet.

AS BB — TURN OVERBETS VS CAPPED PFR:
- PFR checks back flop (capped) → overbet turn, especially with
  lots of draws/bluffs available.
- Flop check-check, turn is big card hitting check-back range (King):
  Go BIG. Saying "I have better than TPGK."

SET OVERBETTING BY BOARD HEIGHT:
- A/Q high + low cards (A456, Q456): Overbet sets. Opponent's check-back
  has pairs, overcards dead to your set — can't call overbet.
- J high: Starts to overbet a little.
- T high and below (T456): Don't overbet sets. Opponent has overcards
  you WANT to keep in.

OVERBET BLUFF SELECTION:
- Must have EQUITY backing it up: str8 flush draws, bottom pair + FD.
- Suit matters: K4hh/K4dd (with FD) overbets. K4cc/K4ss (no draw) doesn't.
- When overbetting as bluff: Know what you're folding out, what equity
  you deny, what rivers let you continue.


H. MAX VALUE — TURN & RIVER
--------------------------------------------------------

TURN SIZING FOR VALUE:
- After flop c-bet with strong hand: Size turn to create ~1:1 SPR on river
  (generally 60-110% pot depending on texture).
- Dynamic boards: Frontload value on turn. River card often makes
  extraction harder with strong made hands.
- Use raises on turn with strong hands to decrease SPR.

RIVER SIZING:
- Missed draws everywhere → large.
- OOP with mediocre-but-likely-best → small.
- Target specific calling hands. Size for THAT range, not generic "big."
- Vs aggressive + capped: Size to induce bluffs, especially with blockers.
- Call river raises/shoves when opponent's represented range is unlikely
  based on all prior action.

RIVER VALUE BET RULE (reinforced):
- Only got one street of value by river + safe river + blocks helping
  hands → MUST bet. Don't check back overpair with one bet extracted.


APPLICATION TO GEM REPORTS
--------------------------------------------------------

1. C-BET DECISIONS: Classify board (Bet Range / Heavy Bet / Heavy Check)
   per Section A. Grade Hero's decision + sizing. Flag deviations.

2. CHECK-RAISE DECISIONS: When Hero in BB facing c-bet, evaluate per
   Section C. Was this a valid CR candidate? Sizing correct? Flag missed
   CRs with strong candidates.

3. PROBE/DONK DECISIONS: After PFR checks back or after calling c-bet,
   evaluate per Sections D and E. Flag missed probes on favorable turns.

4. OVERBET SPOTS: Flag missed overbets per Section G — especially when
   PFR checked back (capped) and turn is blank/undercard.

5. CAPPED RANGE EXPLOITATION: When villain checks back flop or turn,
   note capped range and evaluate exploitation per Section F.

6. VALUE EXTRACTION: Grade river sizing per Section H. Flag under-betting
   and "Too Much River Respect" using SPR planning framework.

NEW METRICS TO CONSIDER TRACKING:
- Missed overbet opportunities
- Donk bet frequency on equity-shifting turns
- C-bet accuracy by board category
- Check-raise bluff quality (required characteristics present?)

========================================================
APPENDIX B — JAKA COACHING FRAMEWORK
(Preflop: 4-Bet, BB Defence, BvB SRP)
========================================================
Source: Jaka coaching curriculum (4b Opportunity Group, BB Defence,
BvB SRP by Thomas Boivin). Same precedence rules as Appendix A.


I. 4-BET / COLD 4-BET FRAMEWORK
--------------------------------------------------------

AKo ALL-IN CALL-OFF THRESHOLDS:
- vs EP action: ~60BB
- vs MP action: ~75BB
- vs LP action: ~100BB

NEVER COLD CALL A 3-BET. Only exception: possibly BU at 100bb+ depth.

OOP FACING 3-BET WITH AQo/AJo DEEP:
- 4b-fold candidates, NOT flats. Flatting OOP = massive reverse implied
  odds (stacked when they have AK; if they 5b-jam, they had you
  dominated anyway).

AKo AT 50-60BB OOP: Just jam. AKs can use NAI (non-all-in) 4b sizing
because it plays well postflop.

NAI 4-BET RANGE MUST INCLUDE BLUFFS. If never 4b-bluffing, leaving
a powerful tool unused.

4-BET BLUFF SELECTION:
- Want 2 blockers to their value range, not just 1. Single T blocker
  not enough — villains don't always 3-bet TT.
- ATo NOT a good 4b bluff from EP/MP — blocks their 3b bluffs (KTs,
  QTs, JTs are Tx-heavy). From LP where 3-bettor is wider → ATo OK.
- AQo has 2 blockers but doesn't work deep — need postflop playability
  → prefer KJs, AJs instead.
- A5s is an exception — plays great vs flatting range, str8 outs unblocked.
- Cold 4b bluffs = generally 2 big suited cards.

WHEN IP GETS SQUEEZED:
- Can't flat → jam most of continue range. Mix in KK/AA traps + some
  4b-folds with blockers to balance.

OOP FACING 3-BET (SPECIFIC HANDS):
- 4b-fold: TT, KJs, AJs, AQo, AQs (at typical depths)
- Jam: AKo
- TT if 4b: mostly fold to 5b (call only vs confirmed maniac)
- JJ+ = continue. TT only if villains super wide.
- QQ+ getting in if jammed on. AKs also getting in vs 5b.

NO FLATTING 3-BETS WITH SHALLOW STACKS + PLAYERS BEHIND.
COLD CALLING 3-BET THEN FOLDING TO 4-BET = DISASTER.
Only have a flatting range as exploit vs players very unlikely to 4b.


II. BB DEFENCE FRAMEWORK
--------------------------------------------------------

FLATTING RANGE FUNDAMENTALS:
- Good price from BB (1BB already invested). Don't need to win often.
- Tighten up one notch vs bigger raise sizes.
- HU and 3-way: flat almost any 2 suited cards (except when entire
  flat range must be very tight).

STACK SIZE → SHALLOWER = WIDER FLATS:
- 15-20BB: Wider flats. Equity realization easier via check/shove.
- 100BB: Tighter flats. Get barreled off equity over multiple streets.
- Deep stacks: Specifically tighten hands with reverse implied odds.

POSITIONAL ADJUSTMENTS:
- Earlier the open → tighter we flat. Especially dominated hands.

MULTIWAY ADJUSTMENTS FROM BB:
- Offsuit: Fold dominated hands as players increase. 3-way connected
  and 1-gappers still OK. 4-way only LOW connected/1-gappers.
  5-way fold everything except top broadway.
- Suited: HU & 3-way = call almost any 2 suited. 4-way = fold junky
  suited. 5-way = continue tightening.

3-BETTING FROM BB — BLUFF SELECTION:
- Use blockers with kickers just BELOW hands you want them to fold.
  "1 pip under the opening range" for villain.
- Use hands you don't mind wasting (low equity realization if called).
- Adjust bluff range: EP opener = tighter bluffs, LP = wider.

ICM ADJUSTMENTS TO BB DEFENCE:
- Estimate risk premium from chip distribution + laddering chances.
- Fold significantly more when risk premium is high.
- Light reshoves: Axs + hands that unblock raise-folds.
- High risk premium = postflop equity realization tough → rejam more
  linearly (raw equity over speculative hands).


III. BvB SRP — THEORY & SIMPLIFIED STRATEGIES
(Thomas Boivin / Jaka Group)
--------------------------------------------------------

SB C-BET BY BOARD TEXTURE (60BB DEFAULT):

Paired boards:
- Paired 7+ high → c-bet range 15-25%
- Paired 6- high → check + bet 30-40% (polar)

Monotone boards:
- C-bet range 12-15% on almost all monotones
- EXCEPT A-high monotones (AK5m, AJ6m) and connected monotones
  (875m) → check range

Straight-draw boards:
- Check + c-bet polar. Sizing by texture:
  - 1 possible straight → size UP
  - 2-3 possible straights → size DOWN
  - Rainbow → size UP. Two-tone → size DOWN.
  - Examples: 876s=b40. 876r=b70. 875s/r=b100. 874r=b133.

High card boards (most need checking range):
- T high and lower → check + b2e (geometric 2 streets)
- HHM/HMM/MMM (KQ8, Q97, T75) AND AKx/AQx → check + b2e
- Others (A93, K82, Q73, J52) → check + b40 (or CbetR20 vs non-elite)
- HHL rainbow (AJ4r, KJ2r, QT5r, JT5r) → c-bet range 20%

GEOMETRIC SIZING:
- b2e = same % of pot on 2 remaining streets to end all-in
- b3e = same % on 3 streets to end all-in

STACK DEPTH ADJUSTMENTS (BvB):
40BB vs 60BB: Check ~5% less overall. A-high → c-bet much more.
20BB vs 40BB: Check ~6% less overall. A-high/K-high → c-bet much more.

BB STAB STRATEGY (vs SB check):
- Dry/disconnected (A72, K82, T52) → stab SMALL 25%. Merged.
- Mid-low connected (876, 754) → stab MEDIUM 40%. Polar on wet.
- Polar value range boards (AK7, KQ8, Q87s, T95) → stab BIG 60-100%.


IV. BvB SRP — POPULATION EXPLOITS
(Thomas Boivin / Jaka Group)
--------------------------------------------------------

EXPLOIT: BB OVERFOLDS vs SMALL C-BET (FLOP):
- SB: C-bet range very small on dry + HHL boards.

EXPLOIT: BB TOO PASSIVE vs BIG C-BET:
- SB: Extend big c-bet range by adding bluffs.

EXPLOIT: BB NITTY vs ALL SIZES:
- Replace checks with 20-25% bets (bluffs). Keep big bets but NEVER
  bet big with 2-pair+ (those go in small bet).

EXPLOIT: SB OVER-CBETS — RIVER CONSEQUENCES:
- After range c-bet, OOP should check more on river.

EXPLOIT: BB STABS TOO MUCH vs CHECK:
- Counter to over-stabbing is ALWAYS check-raising.


APPLICATION OF APPENDIX B TO GEM REPORTS
--------------------------------------------------------

1. 4-BET DECISIONS: Evaluate Hero's 4b range vs Section I. Flag
   cold-calling 3-bets (should be 4b-fold or fold). Flag ATo 4b-bluffs
   from EP/MP. Check blocker quality on 4b-bluffs.

2. BB DEFENCE: Grade flatting range width vs stack depth and opener
   position per Section II. Flag too-tight BB defence at shallow stacks.
   Flag reverse implied odds hands flatted deep.

3. BvB C-BET: When Hero is SB in BvB SRP, classify board per
   Section III and grade c-bet decision + sizing.

4. BvB EXPLOITS: When villain exhibits population tendencies, evaluate
   whether Hero exploited per Section IV.

5. BB STAB: When SB checks to Hero in BB, grade stab decision per
   Section III BB stab strategy (small/medium/big by board type).


========================================================
APPENDIX C — BvB LIMP/CHECK + 3-BET CONSTRUCTION +
             DOUBLE BARREL & RIVER RAISE SIZING
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-03 (v6.2)
Sources: Thomas Boivin (BvB Limp/Check, JAKA Lvl 4),
         JAKA Coaching (3-Bet Ranges, Double Barrel Opp)

--------------------------------------------------------
C1. BvB LIMP/CHECK POSTFLOP STRATEGY (Boivin)
--------------------------------------------------------

CORE PRINCIPLE: After SB limps and BB checks, the DEFAULT
action for BOTH players is CHECK. Deviations are specific.

SB STRATEGY BY STACK DEPTH:

  60BB:
  - CHECK RANGE: XLL boards (A43, K42, Q52, J43), 9-high
    and below, all monotone boards.
  - BET ~1BB: HHX boards (KT6, QJ5, JT4) — most textures.
  - PAIRED: Check low paired. Bet high paired. Mix middle.
  - HHH (AQJ, KQT): Check, then bet pot+ as delayed play.

  30BB: CHECK even MORE than 60BB. Check range on most textures.

  15BB: Similar to 60BB. NEW: Bet-to-end-it (jam) on dynamic
  flops: A65, K87, J75, T95. With strong draws and pairs+.

BOARD TEXTURE KEY:
  HHX = Two high + one low. XLL = One high + two low.
  HHH = Three high. Monotone = Check range.

BB STAB STRATEGY (after SB limp then check):
  - GTO stab frequency: 30-60%.
  - Default sizing: ~1bb (small). Low boards: b50-b70.
  - High boards (HHH): b100 (pot). Very polar.

GEM INTEGRATION — BvB LIMP/CHECK:
  1. Do NOT flag SB checks in BvB limp pots as "missed probes."
  2. Only flag SB bets as errors on: XLL, monotone, 9-high boards.
  3. Track BB stab rate in BvB limp pots separately.
  4. At 15BB, jam on dynamic boards with strong draws/pairs+ is correct.


--------------------------------------------------------
C2. CONSTRUCTING 3-BET RANGES (JAKA Coaching)
--------------------------------------------------------

THE 3-BET FRAMEWORK:
  - VALUE 3-bet: Top of range. Getting worse hands to call/jam.
  - CALL (flat): Middle of range. Keep worse hands in.
  - BLUFF 3-bet: Bottom of continue range. Getting better hands
    to fold. Must have: (a) borderline to call, AND (b) good
    blocker qualities (Ace or King preferred).

  CRITICAL CHECK: Before every 3-bet, ask "Am I 3-betting for
  value or as a bluff?" If neither → the hand is a CALL or FOLD.

STACK DEPTH ADJUSTMENTS:
  Shallow (<40BB): Lean toward blockers (Ax, Kx offsuit).
    NEVER 3-bet 76s type hands below 40BB.
  Medium (40-70BB): Mix blockers and suited hands.
  Deep (70BB+): Suited hands dominate bluff range.

POSITION-SPECIFIC 3-BET STRATEGY:
  BB 3-Betting — POLARIZED: Value + bluff, skipping the middle.
  SB 3-Betting — LINEAR: Continuous range from top down.
  OOP EXCEPTION (EP vs EP): 3-bet AQo/AJo/KQo even though
  folding to 4-bet "wastes" a hand.

RESHOVE RANGES FROM BLINDS:
  - vs CO/BTN open: reshove any pair up to 30BB effective.
  - vs HJ open: reshove any pair up to 25BB effective.
  - Top broadways (KQs) in BB vs BTN = reshove, not flat.

BB FLATTING RANGE RULES:
  1. Earlier raiser → tighter BB flat.
  2. Deeper effective → tighter with big-card/bad-kicker.
  3. Trashy suited/connected remain playable deep.
  4. Shallower stacks → wider calls.
  5. Multiway: tighten significantly.

REFERENCE OPEN PERCENTAGES (first-in):
  BTN: 45%  CO: 35%  HJ: 30%  LJ/MP: 25%  UTG+1: 22%  UTG: 15%

GEM INTEGRATION — 3-BET CONSTRUCTION:
  1. For each 3-bet, verify it classifies as value OR bluff.
  2. Flag 76s-type 3-bets at <40BB as stack-depth errors.
  3. Track missed reshoves: Hero flats from blinds at ≤30BB
     vs LP open with a hand that should jam.
  4. Dave: flat more vs EP opens from BTN/CO = confirmed.
     Amit: T9s prefer flat over 3-bet = confirmed.


--------------------------------------------------------
C3. DOUBLE BARREL & RIVER RAISE SIZING (JAKA Coaching)
--------------------------------------------------------

TURN BARREL SELECTION (after flop c-bet called):
  - Do NOT barrel hands with too much equity that can't call
    a shove. Example: J9 or 97 with pair + straight draw.
  - Instead: barrel gutshots and low-equity bluffs that you're
    happy to bet-fold.
  - RULE: If your hand has >25% equity but can't profitably
    call a raise, it's too good to bluff with on the turn.

RIVER RAISE SIZING vs BLOCK BETS:
  Step 1: Identify target hands villain likely has.
  Step 2: Choose size that makes target hands indifferent.
  Step 3: Adjust for read (Kx in range → SIZE UP).
  Step 4: Adjust for hand strength (strong → LARGER raise).

  GEM FLAG: When Hero faces a block bet on the river and just
  calls with a strong hand (trips+), flag as potential
  "Missed River Raise."

========================================================
END OF APPENDIX C
========================================================


========================================================
APPENDIX D — ICM PREFLOP (SHORT/MID STACKS) +
             MULTIWAY POTS + OPEN LIMPING STRATEGY
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-03 (v6.2)
Sources: JAKA Coaching (ICM Preflop, Multiway Lesson,
         Open Limping Strategy)

--------------------------------------------------------
D1. ICM PREFLOP — FINAL TABLE HEURISTICS
--------------------------------------------------------

GENERAL FT RANGE PRINCIPLES:
  - Opening ranges are BLOCKER ORIENTED. Suited connectors LOSE value.
  - Open-jamming rare above 15BB (unless LP and covered).
  - 3-bet NAI is viable at ANY stack depth, even 15BB.
  - Flat-calling very limited with short/mid stacks.
  - When in doubt: TIGHT IS RIGHT.

SHORT STACK RULES (≤20BB at FT):
  - ZERO flats as short stack (except BB). Play 3-bet or fold.
  - No jams at 15BB from HJ. Start having jams from CO.
  - Facing 3-bet from big stack OOP: NO calling. 4-bet or fold.
  - 3-betting from LP vs big stack: Don't flat offsuit hands.

MID STACK RULES (25-40BB at FT):
  - Can have tight flatting ranges in LP and in the blinds.
  - Attack wide opening ranges from big stacks.
  - BB Defence vs Big Stack: very wide defence with heavy jam range.

GEM INTEGRATION — ICM PREFLOP:
  1. Apply ICM evaluation overlay at FTs. Don't use ChipEV logic.
  2. Flag flat-calls from short stacks at FTs as potential errors.
  3. Flag open-jams above 15BB from EP/MP at FTs.
  4. Don't flag tight FT opens as "Nit Button."
  5. FT ranges vary by stack distribution. Context matters.


--------------------------------------------------------
D2. MULTIWAY POT STRATEGY (JAKA Coaching)
--------------------------------------------------------

CORE RULES:
  - C-BETTING OOP MULTIWAY: CHECK at high frequency.
  - Two broadway card boards: can bet at higher frequency.
  - Monotone boards OOP multiway: CHECK RANGE. No exceptions.
  - SIZING: Do NOT bet bigger multiway. Use MORE small bets.

GEM INTEGRATION — MULTIWAY:
  1. MW check frequency should be HIGHER than HU thresholds.
  2. Flag pure bluff c-bets into 3+ players.
  3. Flag oversized MW c-bets. MW sizing same or SMALLER than HU.
  4. Monotone + OOP + multiway = pure check range.
  5. Overpairs, TPTK, sets, strong draws = bet MW.
     Marginal pairs, pure air = check back MW.


--------------------------------------------------------
D3. OPEN LIMPING STRATEGY (JAKA Coaching)
--------------------------------------------------------

HEADS-UP LIMPED POTS (as IP limper):
  - A-high through T-high: BET RANGE (unless paired). Default: 1bb.
  - 9-high: first boards with a check range (10-30%).
  - 8-high through 4-high: check ~40% of the time.
  - Monotone: bet range 1bb heads-up.
  - Straight draws in BB's range: use 2/3 sizing.

3-WAY LIMPED POTS (HJ limp, both blinds call, 15BB eff):
  - Dry high-card boards (AKJ rainbow): 100% c-bet, mix 1bb/2bb.
  - High paired (KKT rainbow): 70% c-bet, all 1bb.
  - Mid paired (T22r, 833r): 64-74% c-bet, all 1bb.
  - Connected low (567r): only 50% c-bet. CHECK MORE.
  - Connected high (T98s): 94% c-bet, all 1bb (T+ cards).
  - RULE: Connected boards → check more ONLY when ALL THREE
    cards are below 9.

GEM INTEGRATION — OPEN LIMPING:
  1. In limped pots, do NOT apply standard c-bet targets.
  2. Track limped pot betting separately from RFI c-bets.
  3. Flag oversized bets in limped pots (1bb is default).
  4. When Hero is IP in limped pot and checks T-high+ board:
     flag as missed bet.

========================================================
END OF APPENDIX D
========================================================


========================================================
APPENDIX E — 3-BET POT C-BETTING BY BOARD TYPE +
             BIG STACK FINAL TABLE PLAY
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-03 (v6.3)
Sources: JAKA Coaching (Ace/King/Low Boards After 3-Betting,
         Playing the Big Stack on Final Tables)

--------------------------------------------------------
E1. 3-BET POT C-BETTING: ACE-HIGH BOARDS
--------------------------------------------------------

DEFAULT: Very little checking on A-high boards in 3-bet pots.
Simplified rule: bet range 25% pot.

POSITION CONTEXT — 3-BET RANGES BY DEPTH:
  30BB: 3-bet range is Ax-focused → Loves A-high boards.
  60BB: 3-bet range has more broadways/Kxs → Loves K-high boards.

CHECK BACK RANGE — BU vs CO at 60BB ONLY:
  Check ~40% on: Ax + BW + mid/low, Ax + 2 connected mid/low
  (A87, A54, A53, A42, A98), Broadway paired (AQQ, AJJ).

BIG BETS (60% pot) — BU vs CO ONLY: AKx boards. 3 cards 9+.

10% SIZING — MP vs EP: When IP has >60% equity advantage.
  NEVER use 10% when equities are closer.

MP vs EP: ALWAYS bet range on A-high. Never check. Never bet big.


--------------------------------------------------------
E2. 3-BET POT C-BETTING: KING-HIGH BOARDS
--------------------------------------------------------

BU vs CO at 30BB — MORE CHECKING on K-high (Ax bluffs want free card).
BU vs CO at 60BB — LESS CHECKING on K-high (range connects well).
MP vs EP: Still bet range on K-high.


--------------------------------------------------------
E3. 3-BET POT C-BETTING: LOW BOARDS
--------------------------------------------------------

DEFAULT: c-bet 25% sizing on most low boards in 3-bet pots.
CHECK MORE on: Low straight boards (567, 678), Jxx-9xx boards.
PAIRED LOW BOARDS: High bet frequency (75-89%). Always bet.
BIG BETS (60%): Less common. Primarily at 60BB on Tx + 2 mid/low.


--------------------------------------------------------
E4. BIG STACK FINAL TABLE PLAY
--------------------------------------------------------

RISK PREMIUM MECHANICS:
  - BTN 60BB covering 15-20BB blinds: open/jam wider.
  - Exploit: minraise more — most players won't defend enough at FTs.

3-BETTING AS BIG STACK:
  - Can't go wrong 3-betting most offsuit Ax vs CO open.
  - vs wide open (26%): ATo-AQo = pure CALL.
  - vs tight open (16%): ATo-AQo = 3-BET.

BIG STACK vs BIG STACK:
  - Risk premiums MASSIVE. Avoid collision.
  - 3-bet ranges polarized. FLAT most good suited hands IP.

POSTFLOP AS BIG STACK IP vs BB:
  - C-bet at HIGH frequency. Small bets accomplish the job.
  - Low/connected boards (876): c-bet MORE than CEV.
  - Two broadway boards (KJ4): check MORE (~59%).

GEM INTEGRATION — 3-BET POT C-BETTING + BIG STACK FT:
  1. Check board category + position matchup + depth.
  2. MP vs EP in 3-bet pots: ALWAYS bet range on A/K-high.
  3. BU vs CO at 60BB on connected A-high (A87, A54): ~40% check OK.
  4. BU vs CO at 30BB on K-high: more checking is correct.
  5. Low straight boards no gaps: 30%+ check is correct.
  6. 10% sizing: only valid when IP has >60% equity advantage.
  7. At FTs as big stack: higher c-bet freq on low/connected,
     lower on two-broadway boards.

========================================================
END OF APPENDIX E
========================================================


========================================================
APPENDIX F — BB 3-BET POT POSTFLOP STRATEGY (OOP)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-03 (v6.4)
Source: JAKA Coaching (Postflop Play After 3-Betting from BB)

--------------------------------------------------------
F1. BB 3-BET RANGE CONSTRUCTION BY DEPTH
--------------------------------------------------------

BB is the most under-bluffed 3-bet spot in poker.

  Sub-40BB: Use blocker hands as bluffs (Kx, Ax, Qx offsuit).
  50BB+: Start including suited hands (65s, 87s).
  100BB+: Don't 3-bet suited GAPPERS. Start 3-betting broadways
  for VALUE: KQs, KJs, AJo.


--------------------------------------------------------
F2. OOP C-BET SIZING IN BB 3-BET POTS
--------------------------------------------------------

DEFAULT: 25-30% pot c-bet is fine on most boards.

WHEN TO USE BIG (60%) C-BETS:
  - Dynamic boards with lots of equity shifts on turn.
  - Low RAINBOW boards: fold out hands like KQs, QJs, QTs, ATs.
  - Low PAIRED boards (442r): fold out backdoor FDs + overcards.
  - Big bet BLUFF selection: K9o, A9o (one-and-done hands).
  - Big bet VALUE: Vulnerable value (TT-QQ, A8 on low boards).

WHEN TO USE SMALL (25-30%) C-BETS:
  - A mid/low boards. Big paired boards (AAx, KKx, TTx).
  - AA/KK as value. Bottom set. At 30BB generally.


--------------------------------------------------------
F3. OOP CHECKING STRATEGY BY BOARD TYPE AND DEPTH
--------------------------------------------------------

50BB: T-HIGH = check most. J-HIGH = similar but have more Jx.
  K-HIGH = mostly bet range. A-HIGH = AKx checks more than expected.
  FLUSH DRAW = add ~10% to check frequency vs rainbow.

100BB: CHECK A LOT on middle cards with straights possible.
  BET RANGE: 2 broadway boards, K-high boards.


--------------------------------------------------------
F4. IP RESPONSE TO BB'S OOP C-BET
--------------------------------------------------------

When IP faces BB's 60% c-bet: IP must be PATIENT. CALL with sets,
  QT-type hands, A-high flush draws. Don't raise immediately.
When IP faces BB's small c-bet on low board: Big bet from IP
  forces folds from overs + BDFD.

GEM INTEGRATION — BB 3-BET POTS:
  1. Evaluate c-bet sizing by board type per F2.
  2. Flag checks on boards where Hero should be betting range.
  3. Track BB 3-bet pot c-bet rate separately from SRP.
  4. Flatting sets at low SPR is correct, not a slowplay error.

========================================================
END OF APPENDIX F
========================================================


========================================================
APPENDIX G — HU 3-BET POT STRATEGY:
             AGGRESSOR + DEFENDER FRAMEWORKS
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-03 (v6.5)
Source: Jeremy Menard / JAKA Coaching (Postflop Play in
        HU 3-Bet Pots)

--------------------------------------------------------
G1. CORE PRINCIPLES
--------------------------------------------------------

- Ranges are EVERYTHING in 3-bet pots.
- 3-bettor (aggressor) has strongest range on MOST flops.

--------------------------------------------------------
G2. AGGRESSOR STRATEGY
--------------------------------------------------------

COMMON MISTAKES (flag in GEM):
  1. C-betting 100% of flops (ignoring board texture).
  2. Checking A-high boards with QQ+ too often.
  3. Playing too passively with strong hands postflop.
  4. Betting flop then giving up on turn.
  5. Giving up too much on river.

BOARDS TO C-BET: Ace-high, one/two broadway, low disconnected,
  connected high when IP, disconnected monotone, high/low paired.
DEFAULT SIZING: Small (25-35% pot) on flop.

BOARDS TO CHECK: Connected middling (567, 89T), high connected
  favoring defender (Q8T, J9T), middling paired (77T, 88J),
  connected monotone (6h7h9h).

BOARDS FOR BIG BETS: Dynamic boards OOP with range advantage.
  Low SPR on dynamic flops. Example: T93 at 20-30BB.

--------------------------------------------------------
G3. DEFENDER STRATEGY
--------------------------------------------------------

COMMON MISTAKES:
  1. Calling too wide preflop/flop.
  2. Not check-raising enough on dynamic boards.
  3. Not FLOATING enough vs small bets.
  4. Playing strong hands face-up on dry boards.
  5. Leading into aggressor on boards good for aggressor.
  6. Folding too often on turn/river.

CHECK-RAISE: Mix with strong hands AND draws on DYNAMIC boards.
  On DRY boards: DO NOT check-raise. Let opponents continue bluffing.

--------------------------------------------------------
G4. GEM INTEGRATION — HU 3-BET POTS
--------------------------------------------------------

  1. Flag 100% c-bet frequency in 3-bet pots.
  2. Flag checks on A-high with QQ+ as passivity errors.
  3. Flag one-and-done in 3-bet pots.
  4. Track river give-up rate in 3-bet pots.
  5. Flag big c-bets where small sizing is correct.
  6. Flag donk bets into 3-bettor on A/K-high boards.
  7. Flag check-raises on dry boards in 3-bet pots.
  8. Flag folds to small c-bets with medium-strength draws.
  9. When aggressor checks turn: evaluate river attack.
  10. Track defender's "float → bluff" rate.

========================================================
END OF APPENDIX G
========================================================


========================================================
APPENDIX H — SHORT STACK CRASH COURSE:
             15BB LIMP/ISO/RESHOVE FRAMEWORK
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-03 (v6.6)
Source: JAKA Coaching (Maneuvering a Short Stack)

--------------------------------------------------------
H1. RFI RANGE CONSTRUCTION AT SHALLOW STACKS (15-20BB)
--------------------------------------------------------

CORE SHIFT: Range COMPOSITION changes dramatically at 20BB.
  DROP suited connectors (76s, 87s, 98s). ADD blocker hands
  (Ax offsuit, Kx offsuit). Suited broadways and pocket pairs
  remain. Shallow stacks = blocker-oriented range construction.


--------------------------------------------------------
H2. OPEN LIMPING AT 15BB — PREFLOP FRAMEWORK
--------------------------------------------------------

Limping is GTO-approved at 15BB. NOT a weakness tell.

LIMP RANGE STRUCTURE BY POSITION:
  - RED (All-in on ISO): Premiums + strong hands trapping.
  - GREEN (Call ISO): Medium-strength with postflop playability.
  - BLUE (Fold to ISO): Bottom of limp range.
  - ORANGE (Raise — limp-raise small): Trapping hands.

EP limp: Tightest. Mostly pairs, suited broadways, suited Ax.
BTN limp: Widest limp range. Many speculative hands.
SB limp (vs BB only): Very wide. Almost any two cards can limp.


--------------------------------------------------------
H3. ISO STRATEGY VS LIMPS AT 15BB
--------------------------------------------------------

ISO range tightness depends on: limper position, ISO position,
remaining players behind.

KEY: BB ISO vs EP limp = extremely tight (near-premium only).
BB ISO vs BTN limp = wide. BB ISO vs SB limp = very wide.
ISO SIZING: 3x limp (~3BB at 15BB). DO NOT min-ISO.


--------------------------------------------------------
H4. RESPONSE VS ISO AFTER LIMPING AT 15BB
--------------------------------------------------------

ALL-IN: Hands that were trapping.
CALL: Hands with postflop playability at committed SPR.
FOLD: Bottom of limp range (should be SMALL at 15BB).


--------------------------------------------------------
H5. RESHOVE MASTERY AT SHORT STACKS
--------------------------------------------------------

Most important short-stack skill. Use range charts.
SB reshove vs EP/MP: FLAT more often rather than reshove.
SB reshove vs CO/BTN: reshove is standard.


--------------------------------------------------------
H6. SHALLOW STACK C-BETTING & CHECK-RAISING (15-20BB)
--------------------------------------------------------

C-BET: Use 1BB sizing at shallow stacks. Standard sizing.
CHECK-RAISING: Only with hands willing to get all-in.
DO NOT check-raise bluff at 15BB unless remaining stack
after CR is too small for villain to re-raise.


--------------------------------------------------------
H7-H8. LIMPING EXPLOITS & GEM INTEGRATION
--------------------------------------------------------

1. When Hero limps at ≤20BB, do NOT flag as a leak.
2. Verify limp-jams with proper hand tier.
3. Flag limp-folds with hands that should continue.
4. Verify ISO ranges per H3.
5. BB checks vs EP limps are NOT "missed ISOs."
6. C-bet sizing in limped pots: verify 1BB per H6.
7. Check-raise at 15BB: verify commitment.
8. Track "SB flat vs EP open at 15BB" per H5.

========================================================
END OF APPENDIX H
========================================================


========================================================
APPENDIX I — GTO SIMPLIFIED FRAMEWORK:
            BOARD TYPES, RANGE SHAPES, SIZING,
            AND EXPLOITATION PATTERNS
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-03 (v6.7)
Source: Dara O'Kearney & Barry Carter, "GTO Poker
        Simplified" (2022). Solver-based heuristics.

--------------------------------------------------------
I1. CORE PRINCIPLE: VALUE BETS DRIVE EVERYTHING
--------------------------------------------------------

| Value Density | Strategy |
| Lots of value, few bluffs | Bet SMALL with whole range |
| Few value hands, many bluffs | Bet BIG with polar range, check middle |
| Almost no value | Play passive, let villain bet, bluff-catch |

VALUE TARGET: Weakest hand you hope gets called.
BLUFF TARGET: Strongest hand you hope folds.
RULE: Big bet = value + bluffs. Small bet = mostly value.


--------------------------------------------------------
I2. STATIC VS DYNAMIC BOARDS (replaces wet/dry)
--------------------------------------------------------

STATIC: Most turn/river cards do NOT change who is ahead.
  Examples: A♠9♠6♠, K♠7♥2♦.
DYNAMIC: Many turn/river cards CAN flip range advantage.
  Examples: 9♣6♦4♠, 8♥7♣5♦.

KEY INSIGHT: The old "wet vs dry" gets this backwards.
  A♠9♠6♠ LOOKS wet but is static. 9♣6♦4♠ LOOKS dry but is dynamic.

THE RULE: How dynamic depends more on how HIGH the top card is.
  High top card (A, K) = more static. Low top card (9-) = more dynamic.

| Board Type | Bet Size | Why |
| Static, range adv | Small (25-33%), range bet | Lots of value, only way to get paid is small |
| Dynamic, range adv | Big (66-100%), selective | Need equity denial |
| Static, no range adv | Check most, small bet some | Can't support big bets |
| Dynamic, no range adv | Check 100% | Let villain bet, bluff-catch |


--------------------------------------------------------
I3. RANGE SHAPE TAXONOMY
--------------------------------------------------------

LINEAR: Strongest hands sequential from top. No gaps.
POLARIZED: Very strong AND very weak. No middle.
CONDENSED: Mostly middle-strength. No monsters, no trash.
CAPPED: Medium and weak, missing the strongest.

CRITICAL: Capping your range by betting ALL strong hands is
an exploitable leak. Keep some strong hands in check/call range.


--------------------------------------------------------
I4. HOW RANGES TRANSFORM BY STREET
--------------------------------------------------------

| Flop Action | OOP Range Becomes | IP Range Becomes |
| Check / Check | Stays same | CONDENSED (would have bet strong) |
| Check / Bet / Call | LINEAR/CONDENSED | Stays roughly same |
| Check / Bet / Raise / Call | POLARIZED | Stronger but CONDENSED |

KEY RULES:
1. After check/check: IP CONDENSED. OOP can attack turn aggressively.
2. After bet/call: Villain's range is STRONGER. Don't auto-barrel bricks.
3. After check/raise: Raiser POLARIZED. Caller CONDENSED.


--------------------------------------------------------
I5. BLOCKER BET (OOP RIVER TOOL)
--------------------------------------------------------

Small OOP river bet (25-33% pot) designed to:
1. Get value from marginal hands that would check back.
2. Lose less when beaten (fold cheaply to a raise).
3. Induce bluff-raises from aggressive opponents.

WHEN TO USE: Strong-but-not-nutted hand on scary runout.
WHEN NOT: Nuts (bet big), Air (check to give up), Safe/dry board.


--------------------------------------------------------
I6. BOARD COVERAGE (OPENING RANGE CONSTRUCTION)
--------------------------------------------------------

Ranges need to hit strong hands on EVERY possible flop.
Adding A2s-A5s, small pairs, low suited connectors provides
board coverage on low boards. Replacing one broadway offsuit
combo (12 combos) buys two pocket pairs or three suited hands.


--------------------------------------------------------
I7. OVERBET TRIGGER RULES
--------------------------------------------------------

Frequency: River > Turn > Flop.

REQUIREMENTS:
1. Hero must have nutted hands in range.
2. Villain's range must be capped or condensed.
3. Hero does NOT need overall range advantage.

IP OVERBET TURN TRIGGER: Dry static flop → small range bet →
villain called → turn brick → overbet with nutted + blocker bluffs.

OOP OVERBET TURN TRIGGER: Wet dynamic flop → check/check →
turn any card → lead overbet with nutted + best bluffs.

SPR AND OVERBETTING:
  SPR 2-3: No overbet needed. SPR 4-6: Need one overbet street.
  SPR 7+: Need overbets on multiple streets.


--------------------------------------------------------
I8. EXPLOITATION PATTERNS (VILLAIN ARCHETYPES)
--------------------------------------------------------

BETTING STATION: Don't donk. Let them bet. Raise as bluff.
  River: NOW raise for value.

TRAPPER: Don't value bet thinly. Don't bluff river after
  they call turn. BUT: bluff strong draws big on turn.

PROTECTION OBSESSED: If no check-raise by river, range is
  capped. Shove river as bluff. Value bet SMALL.

AUTO-CBET 100%: Check-raise more on dynamic boards. Float
  flop IP wider, attack when they check turn.


--------------------------------------------------------
I9. RIVER DECISION TREES (QUICK REFERENCE)
--------------------------------------------------------

IN POSITION, CHECKED TO:
  Worse calls? → Value bet. SDV? → Check back. No SDV? → Best bluffs.

IN POSITION, FACING BET:
  Raise gets called by worse? → Raise. Wins often enough? → Call.
  No SDV + bluffs? → Best bluffs by blockers.

OUT OF POSITION:
  Same + RANGE PROTECTION (keep strong hands in check range).
  BLOCKER BET option on scary boards.

BLOCKERS MATTER MOST ON THE RIVER: Ranges narrow enough for
blocker effects to be significant.


--------------------------------------------------------
I10. GEM REPORT INTEGRATION RULES
--------------------------------------------------------

1. Tag every flop as STATIC or DYNAMIC per I2.
2. Identify range shapes (Linear/Polar/Condensed/Capped) after each action.
3. Apply transformation table from I4 for turn/river decisions.
4. Cross-reference bet sizing with board type per I2.
5. Verify overbet trigger conditions from I7.
6. Apply I8 villain archetypes when evaluating exploitation spots.
7. Track OOP river blocker bet opportunities per I5.
8. Ask "What is the value target? What is the bluff target?" for sizing.

========================================================
END OF APPENDIX I
========================================================

========================================================
APPENDIX J — DAVE COACHING NOTES (Apr 3-5, 2026)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-04 (v6.8), updated 2026-04-05 (v7.0)
Source: Live session review with Dave (14 takeaways)
Note: These rules take PRECEDENCE over Jaka/GTO framework
for punt evaluation when there's a conflict.

Also update the file header to include:
For Dave coaching rules (Apr 3-6), see: APPENDIX J

--------------------------------------------------------
J1. MIDDLING A-HIGH C-BET ADJUSTMENTS
--------------------------------------------------------

On middling A-high flops (A-9-x, A-8-x type), sometimes
CHECK to keep weaker Aces in the pot.

If Hero has Ax with backdoor nut flush draw, MORE checks
to maximize equity realization for monsters.

GEM RULE: When evaluating A-high c-bets, check if Hero
has backdoor nut FD. If yes, checking is more correct
(protect equity realization for the draw).


--------------------------------------------------------
J2. MIDDLE POCKET PAIR OOP vs RAISE
--------------------------------------------------------

As PFR with middle pocket pair (99-JJ), if Hero checks
flop OOP and villain raises:
- CALL once to any reasonable bet if Hero also has
  backdoor draws.
- OVERFOLD to big bets (>66% pot).

GEM RULE: Don't auto-fold middle pairs OOP to flop
raises when Hero has backdoor equity. Call small/medium,
fold big.


--------------------------------------------------------
J3. ICM BB DEFENSE — DON'T OVERDEFEND
--------------------------------------------------------

Don't overdefend BB with bottom-of-range offsuit hands
in ICM/bubble spots, ESPECIALLY multiway.

GEM RULE: In ICM/bubble spots, tighten BB defense
significantly. Bottom offsuit hands (T7o, J3o) = fold
MW near bubble.


--------------------------------------------------------
J4. DISCONNECTED A-HIGH = RANGE BET
--------------------------------------------------------

A92 duotone is very disconnected = RANGE BET with
everything.

GEM RULE: A-high + 2 low + disconnected (no straight
draws) + duotone = range bet. This is MORE aggressive
than standard A-high Jaka rule. Overrides Appendix A
for this specific board type.


--------------------------------------------------------
J5. EQUITY SHIFT TURN SIZING
--------------------------------------------------------

On turns that create significant equity shifts (flush
draw arrives, straight draw arrives, overcard):
- MAX sizing is 50% pot.
- Use 33%/55% strategy.
- Don't overbet equity-shift turns.

GEM RULE: When turn card significantly shifts equity,
cap sizing at 50% pot. Flag turns where Hero bets >50%
pot on equity-shift cards as sizing errors.


--------------------------------------------------------
J6. SHALLOW STACK OOP LEADING
--------------------------------------------------------

The shallower the depth, the LESS EV in checking OOP.
Increase frequency of LEADING (donk betting) when
shallow.

GEM RULE: At shallow stacks (<25BB), leading OOP is
more correct than at deep stacks. Don't auto-check
OOP when short. Overrides the general "BB checks to
PFR" default at shallow stacks.


--------------------------------------------------------
J7. MW SQUEEZE BLUFF EXPLOITATION
--------------------------------------------------------

Over-aggress in spots that population UNDERBLUFFS.

Example: On J42r as BB with QTs vs CO small cbet +
BU call: can squeeze-bluff with combos connecting to
board (44, 22, 35) and BDFD + BDSD + one overcard.

When facing a small MW cbet, look to bluff-raise if
at reasonable depth and have blockers/backdoors.

GEM RULE: Flag MW small c-bet situations where BB can
squeeze-bluff. Don't just call/fold MW — raising is an
option with the right combo (backdoors + board connection
+ underbluffed spot).


--------------------------------------------------------
J8. SHALLOW MW C-BET (<20BB)
--------------------------------------------------------

When shallow (<20BB), maximize equity realization.
C-bet frequency goes DOWN. Be more selective.

GEM RULE: At <20BB in MW pots, reduce c-bet frequency.
Only bet with hands that benefit from fold equity or
strong value. Cross-reference with Appendix D2
(multiway strategy) — shallow stacks add another reason
to check MW.


--------------------------------------------------------
J9. BOUNTY RIVER OVERBET
--------------------------------------------------------

Don't be afraid to shove 2x-3x pot when covering a
bounty and IP needs to bluff-catch Hero's top of range.

GEM RULE: In bounty spots covering villain, river
overbets/jams are correct when Hero has top of range
and villain must decide between calling for their
tournament life vs the bounty. Flag missed bounty
overbets as "Too Much River Respect."


--------------------------------------------------------
J10. OOP DYNAMIC BOARD VALUE — 2 STREETS MAX
--------------------------------------------------------

OOP on ultra-dynamic boards (connected, draws
everywhere), aim for 2 STREETS of value, not 3.

GEM RULE: On dynamic/connected boards OOP, plan for
2 streets of value maximum. 3 barrels OOP on dynamic
boards = over-committing. This overrides the general
"barrel aggressively" default for OOP dynamic textures.


--------------------------------------------------------
J11. 3-BET FOLD AT <50BB
--------------------------------------------------------

Don't 3-bet fold with good equity at <50BB with
polarized 3-bets. Extends Amit's <35BB rule from
memory #9 to <50BB.

GEM RULE: If Hero 3-bets at <50BB and gets 4-bet,
can't fold hands with good equity (pairs, suited
connectors). Either flat the original raise or don't
3-bet at all. 3-bet/fold with a pair at <50BB is a
confirmed error.


--------------------------------------------------------
J12. BvB JAM RANGE
--------------------------------------------------------

<21BB in BvB: A2-AJ = open JAM (not raise).

GEM RULE: BvB at <21BB, all Ax hands A2 through AJ
are open jams, not min-raises. This ensures fold
equity + avoids playing Ax OOP postflop at shallow
depths. At 21BB+, standard raise-sizing applies.


--------------------------------------------------------
J13. BB vs UTG DEFENSE
--------------------------------------------------------

Want 60% equity advantage to defend BB vs UTG.

GEM RULE: BB defense vs UTG requires premium hands.
Don't defend light vs UTG — need strong equity edge.
This is tighter than the general 40-55% BB defense
target which applies vs LP opens.


--------------------------------------------------------
J14. MONOTONE BOARD IP C-BET (Dave Coaching, Apr 5)
--------------------------------------------------------

When Hero is IP as PFR or 3-bettor on monotone boards,
c-bet OFTEN. Do NOT require made hand / two pair / set /
strong draw to c-bet.

This overrides the Jaka monotone rule ("check air, bet
made hands") specifically when Hero is IN POSITION as
the preflop aggressor.

OOP on monotone: Jaka rule still applies (check air,
bet made hands).

GEM RULE: On monotone flops IP as PFR/3-bettor, c-bet
at high frequency regardless of hand strength. Position
advantage + range advantage justifies frequent small
c-bets even with air. Only check back with hands that
specifically want a free card (e.g., one card of the
suit for backdoor runner-runner).

IMPORTANT: This rule applies ONLY to IP PFR/3-bettor.
Does NOT apply to:
  - BB or SB (OOP — use Jaka framework)
  - Non-PFR (caller — different range dynamics)
  - Multiway pots (tighten c-bet per Appendix D2)


--------------------------------------------------------
J14 SUB-CLAUSE: 0-OF-SUIT GIVE-UP-FRIENDLY C-BET
(Amit refinement, v7.29 / 2026-05-02)
--------------------------------------------------------

Source: Amit, Day 11 review of H23 (KQo HJ open vs BB call,
A32sss monotone flop, Hero no spade — Hero x-back, lost to
8s flush). Ron clarification: the rule is "cbet when you're
*willing to give up* to a CR (because you have no equity to
defend)" — not "always cbet."

REFINED RULE:

  When Hero is IP PFR on a monotone flop AND holds 0 cards
  of the suit AND has no equity worth defending: c-bet small
  (~25-33% pot) for fold equity against medium-suit floats
  (54s / 65s / 76s / 87s) that must fold but cannot
  credibly check-raise.

WHY THE GIVE-UP POSTURE IS A FEATURE, NOT A BUG:

  - Holding 0-of-suit means Hero loses NO equity to give up
    later. Folding to a CR or barrel costs only the c-bet.
  - Medium-suit floats (54s / 65s / 76s / 87s) make up a
    meaningful slice of OOP defense range on monotone but
    cannot credibly CR — they need turn equity, not fold
    equity. They fold to a small c-bet.
  - The CR-friendly portion of villain's range (Ax-of-suit,
    sets) crushes Hero with or without the c-bet — Hero
    folds either way.

CONTRAST: when Hero holds 1-of-suit (Ksss-blocker, Khxh
on Asss board, etc.), the calculus shifts — Hero has BDFD
equity to defend and can call CRs profitably. Then the
"check or bet selectively" framing returns.

GEM RULE: when reviewing IP PFR x-back on monotone flops
with 0-of-suit Hero hands at SRP, treat the x-back as a
candidate mistake. C-bet small for fold equity against the
medium-suit-float bucket. This is a drill-mode refinement
of J14 — not auto-detected (no parser flag for "Hero
holds 0-of-suit" yet).

ECHOES: Aligns with M16 (multiway vs station — value bet
wider+bigger; the give-up-friendly c-bet is the bluff
analog) and Jaka K5 (range adv → wide+small).


========================================================
END OF APPENDIX J
========================================================


========================================================
APPENDIX J CONTINUED — DAVE COACHING NOTES (Apr 6, 2026)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-06 (v7.2)
Source: Dave session review (14 hands, 7 new rules)


--------------------------------------------------------
J15. MW FLOAT REQUIRES DOUBLE BACKDOOR
--------------------------------------------------------

Don't float multiway with just overcards or a single
backdoor draw. Need BOTH backdoor straight + backdoor
flush draw to justify a MW float.

GEM RULE: MW float hands must have 2+ backdoor draws
(BDFD + BDSD). Single backdoor or just overcards = fold
MW. Overrides general "call with draws" in MW spots.


--------------------------------------------------------
J16. SHOVE INSURANCE — BACKDOOR REQUIRED
--------------------------------------------------------

When shoving (especially overbet/jam), need backdoor to
nuts (BDFD or BDSD) as insurance in case villain has a
set or strong hand. No naked overbets without backup
equity.

GEM RULE: Before jamming, check for backdoor equity.
Naked shoves with no backdoor = higher risk.


--------------------------------------------------------
J17. FD + OVERCARDS OOP = CHECK-CALL
--------------------------------------------------------

When Hero is OOP with flush draw + overcards, always
CHECK-CALL. Don't check-raise. Let the draw develop
and maximize equity realization.

GEM RULE: FD + overcards OOP = check-call for equity
realization. CR is incorrect here — it turns a drawing
hand into a bluff that can't realize equity if raised.


--------------------------------------------------------
J18. POPULATION UNDER-3BETS (LOW STAKES)
--------------------------------------------------------

At these stakes ($10-$88 buy-in), population under-3bets.
When they DO 3-bet, their range is strong. Hands like 88
can fold to a 3-bet without it being a Dave J11 violation.

GEM RULE: Population-adjusted fold-to-3bet should be
HIGHER than GTO (target 55-65%). 88 type hands = fold
to 3-bet at population. This does NOT conflict with
"don't 3-bet-fold pairs <50BB" (J11) — that applies when
Hero 3-bet and faces a 4-bet. This population fold-to-3bet
rule (J18) applies when Hero opened and faces a 3-bet.


--------------------------------------------------------
J19. POPULATION UNDER-BLUFFS TURNS
--------------------------------------------------------

At these stakes, most villains who check flop then
check-raise turn are NOT bluffing. Their range is Q+
for value. Can fold medium hands to turn check-raises.

No bluffs on the turn that didn't bet the flop = if
villain checks flop and bets/raises turn, it's real.

GEM RULE: Turn check-raise after villain checked flop =
strong hand (Q+ type). Can fold medium pairs, weak TP.
This is a population exploit, not GTO.


--------------------------------------------------------
J20. OOP — DON'T LEAD ON VILLAIN CARDS
--------------------------------------------------------

When OOP, don't lead or check-raise on turn cards that
improve villain's range more than Hero's.

GEM RULE: OOP turn card analysis — if the card is better
for villain (e.g., overcard that connects with their
opening range), check. Don't lead into strength. Let
villain bet and evaluate.


--------------------------------------------------------
J21. SB RANGE BOARDS — LOWER C-BET FREQUENCY
--------------------------------------------------------

When the board connects to SB's calling range more than
the raiser's range, c-bet frequency should be lower.
Use 66% sizing when betting on these boards.

GEM RULE: On boards that favor the caller's range
(especially SB), reduce c-bet freq and use 66% sizing.
Don't auto-bet range on boards like 876, 543, JT9 vs
SB caller.


J22. 3-WAY EQUITY TRAP — REJAM OVER SHORT STACK
--------------------------------------------------------

When facing a rejam over a short stack's all-in, calculate
equity 3-WAY, not heads-up vs the rejammer. The short
stack's wide range cannibalizes Hero's outs (shared Aces,
broadways, Tens, etc.), causing ~8-15% equity drop vs
the HU calculation.

Hands like ATo/KQo that appear to be coinflips HU vs the
rejammer's range become clear folds 3-way. Even with the
most favorable rejammer range assumptions, ATo only reaches
~32% equity 3-way — below the typical ~33% pot odds
threshold.

Bounty on the short stack can close a small gap but does
NOT compensate for 8%+ equity shortfalls.

GEM RULE: When facing a rejam over a short stack jam,
always run 3-way equity, not HU. Flag calls with unsuited
broadways (ATo, KQo, KJo) in these spots as mistakes
unless Hero has a specific exploitative read AND the
3-way math still clears pot odds. Source: $108 HEATER
AhTc hand analysis (Apr 2026).


J23. SB vs UTG 3-BET CONSTRUCTION BY DEPTH
--------------------------------------------------------

<60BB: Only 3-bet hands willing to play for stacks, OR
hands with easy fold on raise + easy playability (suited
connectors, A5s).

100BB: Mainly nut-potential hands only. A5s, ATs+, QQ+,
T9s, 98s, 87s, JTs.

GEM RULE: When evaluating SB 3-bets vs EP, check stack
depth. At <60BB, suited connectors and A5s are acceptable
3-bets. At 100BB, tighten to nut-potential hands only.
Flag non-nut-potential 3-bets from SB vs EP at 100BB+.


J24. OOP 3-BETTOR MONOTONE FLOP STRATEGY
--------------------------------------------------------

70% betting frequency, 20-25% sizing.

The 30% checking range = some made-hand equity that is
NOT nuts potential, OR complete give-ups.

GEM RULE: When Hero 3-bet OOP and faces a monotone flop,
default is to bet 70% of range at 20-25% pot. Only check
with non-nut made equity or pure give-ups. This overrides
the general "check more OOP" default on monotone boards
specifically for the 3-bettor.


J25. OOP 3-BETTOR MONOTONE TURN — TWO SIZINGS
--------------------------------------------------------

Turn strategy splits into two sizings based on depth:

POT CONTROL (small): Pocket aces without the flush suit.
  Goal: extract value from weak draws without bloating pot.

GEOMETRIC (large): Strong hands, air, nuts-like hands, or
