  hands that will shove river anyway (e.g., Aces with the
  suited ace for that board's flush).

CHECK RANGE: Baby flushes or strong made hands like sets
  that don't want to see a river card (check-RAISE line).

GEM RULE: On monotone turn as OOP 3-bettor, classify
Hero's hand into pot-control (small bet), geometric
(large bet), or check (baby flush / set for CR). Flag
mismatches — e.g., geometric sizing with a pot-control
hand, or betting when check-raise is correct.


J26. OOP 3-BETTOR FLOP GIVE-UP RULE
--------------------------------------------------------

If Hero 3-bet OOP and has NO playability on any street
(no pair, no draw, no backdoors, no runner-runner), the
correct play is check/fold. Do NOT c-bet without
playability.

GEM RULE: Flag OOP 3-bet pot c-bets where Hero has
zero playability (no pair, no draw, no backdoors) as
mistakes. The c-bet needs a plan for at least one future
street.


J27. OOP 3-BETTOR FLOP SIZING BY BLOCKER
--------------------------------------------------------

Strong hand that DOESN'T block the draws = BET BIG.
Strong hand that BLOCKS the draws = BET SMALL.

Example: K65dd.
  AKd (blocks diamond draws) → small bet.
  AK no diamond (doesn't block draws) → big bet.

Logic: When you block draws, fewer combos will call a
big bet. When you don't block draws, more combos call
and you want to charge them.

GEM RULE: In OOP 3-bet pots, check if Hero's hand
blocks the primary draw on board. If yes → small sizing
is correct. If no → big sizing. Flag sizing mismatches.


J28. OOP 3-BETTOR — UNPROTECTABLE MADE HANDS CHECK
--------------------------------------------------------

When OOP as 3-bettor with a made hand that doesn't need
protection (e.g., full house, nut flush on static board),
check. Don't bet hands that are already invulnerable.

GEM RULE: Flag bets with hands that don't need protection
OOP in 3-bet pots. These should be in the check range to
trap or induce.


J29. BvB SB PREFLOP STRATEGY (GTO WIZARD)
--------------------------------------------------------

GTO Wizard BvB from SB when folded to: limp 80%, raise
10%, fold 10% (at 30-40BB depth). As depth increases,
fold share increases.

SB steal targets must incorporate this:
  - At 30-40BB deep: fold ~10-15% of hands from SB BvB.
  - Limp is the DEFAULT action (~80%), not raise.
  - Raise with strong hands for value + some bluffs.
  - Increase raise share and decrease limp share as
    stacks get shallower.

GEM RULE: Track SB BvB preflop action: limp vs raise vs
fold frequency when folded to SB. Target: ~80% limp,
~10% raise, ~10% fold at 30-40BB. Adjust for depth.


J30. BB 3-BET SIZING — 5X
--------------------------------------------------------

When 3-betting from BB, increase sizing to 5x the open
(compared to standard 3x from other positions). The extra
size compensates for being OOP and builds a pot where
Hero can leverage range advantage postflop.

GEM RULE: Track BB 3-bet sizing. Flag BB 3-bets at <4x
as undersized. Target: 5x from BB.


J31. VILLAIN MIN-RAISE = STRENGTH
--------------------------------------------------------

When villain min-raises Hero on the flop or turn, treat
as a strength signal. Villain is trying to maximize
without Hero folding.

GEM RULE: When facing a min-raise on flop/turn, tighten
calling/continuing range. Don't treat min-raises as
"cheap" — they indicate strength. Exception: known
maniacs who min-raise bluffs.


J32. SB LIMP-RAISE TO DECREASE SPR
--------------------------------------------------------

From SB OOP, decrease positional disadvantage by:
  - Limp-raising with strong hands (e.g., KK).
  - Decreasing SPR so that postflop decisions are
    simpler (fewer streets, easier all-in decisions).

GEM RULE: Track SB limp-raise frequency. When Hero has
a premium from SB, limp-raise is a valid line to trap
and reduce SPR. Don't flag SB limp-raises with premiums
as passive play — it's a deliberate SPR manipulation.


========================================================
APPENDIX J CONTINUED — DAVE COACHING NOTES (Apr 19, 2026)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-19 (v7.14)
Source: Dave session review (19 hands, 8 new rules)
Hands reviewed: KJs jam, K5s BvB, JTs 30BB jam, J8o BvB,
73s BvB, A3s/ATo ICM MP, A8o SB call, K4o 3bet, KQo/QTo
reshove, 99 ICM jam, A8s stab, 99 dual sizing, 64s bluff
sel. Source file: Dave_Ron_hands_to_go_over.xlsx (rows 27-45).


--------------------------------------------------------
J33. JAM BLOCKER PREFERENCE (2x+ Pot Value Jams)
--------------------------------------------------------

When Hero jams 2x+ pot for value on a draw-completing
runout (flush/straight arrived), prefer the hand that
blocks villain's nut-continue range. Without the nut
blocker, the jam is thinner — villain's strongest value
combos still get there and call.

Rule of thumb: with Kx of the flush suit on a 3-flush
runout, the jam is marginal; with Ax of the flush suit,
the jam is clearly correct. Prefer more outs (backup
equity) when draws are live.

GEM RULE: When Hero jams >=2x pot on a flush-completing
or straight-completing runout, check blocker profile.
Flag "weak-blocker jam" when Hero holds a non-nut flush
card (Kx/Qx of flush suit) or a non-nut straight card
on 2+ pot jams. Target: nut-blocker present on >=70%
of overbet jams. Tracks under Del 4B mistakes when
n>=3 in a session.


--------------------------------------------------------
J34. ICM SHORT-STACK RAISE-OR-3BET (MP vs EP / MP vs MP)
--------------------------------------------------------

Deep in ICM (bubble_zone+) at <=30BB effective, MP's
line vs an EP open AND vs an MP open collapses into
raise-or-3bet-fold. Hands that would normally flat
an EP open (AQo, AJs, ATs, AJo) become 3-bets instead.

Only 99 and AQs remain as flat exceptions. Everything
weaker folds; everything stronger 3-bets.

Rationale: ICM penalizes playing OOP multiway — SB/BB
can 3-bet and force Hero off marginal stacks. Flatting
compresses Hero's range while giving PFR position.
3-betting folds out the blinds and puts fold equity
to work.

GEM RULE: At <=30BB eff in ICM phases (bubble_zone,
post_bubble, ft_zone), flag flats of EP opens from MP
with hands AQo/AJs/ATs/AJo as mistakes. 99 and AQs
flats excluded. Extends J23 (SB vs UTG by depth) by
covering MP-as-caller at short ICM stacks.


--------------------------------------------------------
J35. RESHOVE CEILING — NO RESHOVE OVER 7BB SHOVE (<30BB)
--------------------------------------------------------

When villain jams ~7BB and Hero has <30BB effective
behind, deep in a tournament, Hero's decision is binary:
CALL with a calling-range hand, or FOLD. There is no
reshove/isolation range that sits above a small villain
jam at this stack depth.

KQo = bottom of the call threshold.
QTo = below the call threshold (fold unless in BB,
      where ICM math allows a call).

Rationale: at <30BB, Hero doesn't have enough to "use"
a reshove — can't meaningfully fold out players behind
with a stack that's only 3-4x villain's jam, and the
pot odds of calling are already compelling enough that
most marginal hands should just call.

GEM RULE: When villain jams ~5-8BB and Hero has <30BB
behind, Hero's only actions are call or fold. Flag
Hero reshoves over villain jams <8BB when Hero is at
<30BB as mistakes. Applies mid-late tournament only
(not late_reg with both players deep).


--------------------------------------------------------
J36. ICM JAM-THRESHOLD COMPRESSION
--------------------------------------------------------

The non-ICM "jam if stack <=30% of pot" or "jam at
<30BB eff" rule of thumb BREAKS in ICM.

In ICM, 3-bet sizing compresses (opens smaller,
squeezes smaller), so the ratio of pot-to-stack at
which a jam becomes correct shifts DOWN. 34BB eff
is clearly jammable in non-ICM vs a 2.5BB open; in
ICM, the same hand at 37BB is borderline — because
ICM bust-tax is higher AND because villain's open is
smaller, so Hero's "% of stack invested" threshold
drops.

Practical: at 30-37BB eff in ICM, prefer standard
3-bet sizings. Jam only when <25-28BB eff.

GEM RULE: In ICM phases, flag jams at 30-37BB eff
as potentially oversized. Review rather than auto-flag
as mistake — confirm that standard 3-bet sizing
wouldn't have captured same EV. Standard 3-bet
preferred when Hero is 30BB+ in ICM unless specific
stack pressure or table dynamics force the jam.
Ties to v7.13 "Draw Overbet Jam" tracking.


--------------------------------------------------------
J37. SHALLOW BvB BB JAM RANGE CONSTRUCTION
--------------------------------------------------------

Shallow BvB (<21BB) from the BB, Hero's jam range is
small pairs + offsuit aces. NOT middling broadways.

Reason: jamming profits when either (a) fold equity
plus equity-when-called combine favorably, or (b)
Hero has clear value vs villain's calling range.

Middling hands (KJo, QJo, JTo-type) don't gain enough
fold equity — villain folds worse and calls better.
Small pairs + offsuit aces work because:
  - Pairs have showdown value and equity vs most calls
  - Offsuit aces block villain's Ax calling range

Extends J12 (BvB <21BB: A2-AJ = jam) by adding pair
construction AND explicitly excluding middling broadways
from the jam range.

GEM RULE: In BvB at <21BB where Hero is in the BB,
the jam range is 22-99, A2-AJ (per J12), and
blocker-aware broadways only (KQo on occasion).
Flag Hero jams from BB BvB with middling broadways
(KJo/QJo/JTo/JTs) as shallow jam mistakes.


--------------------------------------------------------
J38. 30BB EFFECTIVE = 2 STREETS, NOT 3
--------------------------------------------------------

At 30BB effective or less (in bounty/ICM formats),
postflop plan is "get it in by turn" — 2 streets of
value/aggression, not 3.

Implications:
  - C-bet size goes UP (pot-sized or near-pot), not
    standard 33-55%. We want SPR to collapse.
  - Preflop shoves widen where SPR would otherwise be
    awkward. Example: BB vs BTN open at 30BB eff in
    ICM — JTs, T9s, AQo, J9s all preflop shoves.
  - Don't c-bet marginal made hands linearly at these
    depths — they bloat the pot into a 2-street plan
    Hero can't continue on.
  - Plan the hand like you have the nuts: "how do I
    get all-in by the turn?" not "what's my river?"

Distinct from J10 (OOP dynamic board = 2 streets):
J10 is board-driven, J38 is stack-depth-driven. Both
can apply simultaneously.

GEM RULE: At Hero eff stack <=30BB, postflop sizing
should be geometric across 2 streets, not 3. Flag
small c-bets (33-40%) at <=30BB where pot-sized
would achieve all-in by turn. Also flag small-small-
jam lines as geometric-sizing violations — ties to
v7.13 Small->Small->JAM tracking. Couples with J37
(shallow preflop jam range) for <21BB decisions.


--------------------------------------------------------
J39. BLUFF COMBO SELECTION — BLOCK OR REPRESENT
--------------------------------------------------------

A bluff combo must do at least one of two things:
  1. BLOCK villain's continues (removes a key card
     from villain's calling/value range), OR
  2. REPRESENT a specific river runout (so Hero's
     story is believable when the runout arrives).

Bluff combos that do NEITHER are mistakes, even if
the overall line looks balanced.

Example (from 64s hand, 4/19): 64s on a board with
no 6 or 4 has no blocker to villain's continuing
range AND no natural draw that represents a river.
Villain calls more often than he should because
Hero's combo has no story.

Counter-example: 64o when both board suits are in
Hero's hand. Blocks both flush draws AND represents
the flush runouts AND has a gutter for equity.
Three things at once — strong bluff combo.

GEM RULE: When flagging Hero bluff combos, check
(a) does the combo block any value card in villain's
range, and (b) does it represent at least one clear
river runout? Flag bluffs that do neither as "combo
selection mistakes" under Del 4B. Target: >=80% of
Hero's flagged bluff combos have >=1 blocker OR
>=1 runout rep.


--------------------------------------------------------
J40. DUAL-SIZING BOARD HAND SORTING
--------------------------------------------------------

On boards where GTO solves for two distinct sizes
(typically 1/3 pot AND pot, or 1/3 pot AND overbet),
Hero's hand categories sort as follows:

  BIG size (pot or near-pot):
    - Strong made hands (sets, two pair, overpairs,
      strong top pair with kicker)
    - Pure bluffs (air with blocker, backdoor-only
      hands that fit J39 selection criteria)
    These are the polar range — value or bluff.

  SMALL size (1/3 pot):
    - Medium-strength made hands (middle pair, weak
      top pair, underpairs to TP)
    - Strong draws that aren't nut-level (combo draws,
      non-nut FD with backups)
    These are the merged range — moderate equity,
    want to bet small for protection/thin value.

  CHECK:
    - Marginal made hands that don't want to inflate
      the pot (pocket pairs below TP with no draw)
    - Pure give-ups

Medium made hands in the BIG bucket = over-bloating
(value bets turn into bluffs when villain raises).
Bluffs in the SMALL bucket = giving correct price,
villain flats everything.

GEM RULE: On boards flagged as dual-sizing textures
(Hero used two distinct bet sizes across similar
spots, or GTO Wizard indicates dual-sizing solve),
check Hero's hand-to-size mapping. Flag:
  - BIG bet with medium-strength made hand = mismatch
  - SMALL bet with pure air/bluff = mismatch
Track "hand-size misalignment" as a leak when n>=5
in a session.


========================================================
APPENDIX J CONTINUED — DAVE COACHING NOTES (Apr 29, 2026)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-29 (v7.24)
Source: Dave session (ICM range dynamics + preflop sizing)


--------------------------------------------------------
J41. ICM RANGE ASYMMETRY (AGGRESSOR vs RESPONDER)
--------------------------------------------------------

In ICM, range adjustments are ASYMMETRIC and DEPEND ON
DIRECTION OF AGGRESSION. The two rules are inverses,
not duplicates.

WHEN BIG STACK OPENS / IS THE AGGRESSOR:
  - Big stack EXPANDS opening / 3-bet ranges significantly.
  - Short stack RESPONDS by NARROWING (>50% range
    contraction in some scenarios — Dave's observed
    range-shrinkage at FT bubble can be more than half
    a normal continue range).
  - Mechanism: short stack pays full ICM bust-tax;
    big stack pays minimal tax → asymmetric risk premium.

WHEN SHORT STACK JAMS / IS THE AGGRESSOR:
  - Short stack still constructs a tight jam range
    (their own bust-tax remains high).
  - Big stack RESPONDER also NARROWS — counterintuitive
    on first read, but correct: villain has already
    committed to going to showdown, so big stack's
    fold-equity-when-aggressor advantage doesn't apply
    here. Big stack only gets the equity-when-called
    side, and ICM penalizes them for losing flips even
    though they survive bust.
  - The big-stack-expands rule from above does NOT
    apply when short stack is the aggressor.

PRACTICAL SUMMARY:
  Big stack OPENS → big expands, short narrows.
  Short stack JAMS → short stays tight, big also narrows.
  Both sides narrow when the short is the aggressor.

GEM RULE: When evaluating preflop ICM spots, classify
who initiated aggression FIRST:
  - If big stack opened: apply big-stack-splashy logic
    (M10) + flag short-stack flat-calls as too wide
    (J34 / J43).
  - If short stack jammed: apply tight calling chart
    to the big stack responder (do NOT widen by the
    chip_leader_cover_jam tag automatically — that
    tag is for big-stack-AS-jammer, not big-stack-as-
    responder).

Detector implication: existing chip_leader_cover_jam
tag in v7.20 widens call ranges 15-20pp when villain
covers Hero by 3x+. That widening is for cases where
HERO is the short stack calling a covering jam. It
should NOT be inverted to widen Hero's call when Hero
is the big stack responding to a short jam — Hero's
range stays at base chart in that direction. This is
already implemented correctly in the analyzer; J41
codifies the underlying principle so it's not lost.

Auto-detector: existing tags handle this; no new
detector needed. Drill mode: review every ICM jam-
or-call spot through the J41 directional lens.
Depth: 🟡 ICM phases only (bubble_zone, post_bubble,
ft_zone).


--------------------------------------------------------
J42. ICM LADDER HEURISTIC — EVERY PAY JUMP ≈ 2X BUY-IN
--------------------------------------------------------

Quick mental model for ICM risk premium estimation
without an ICMizer at the table:

  Each ladder step (pay jump) is worth approximately
  2x the buy-in.

USAGE:
  - Hero's stack at bubble: weigh "take this spot now"
    vs "fold and ladder one spot" using 2x-BI as the
    EV-of-laddering proxy.
  - Marginal spots near pay jumps: if EV(call) is
    close to zero in chips but there's a clear ladder
    1-2 spots away, the chip-EV needs to clear at
    least the 2x-BI ladder value before the call is
    +EV in $.
  - At deeper FT (3-4 ladder spots above current),
    cumulative ladder value can exceed remaining stack
    in $ terms — explains why FT play is so much
    tighter than chip-EV would suggest.

WORKED EXAMPLE:
  Bubble of $25 hyper, Hero has 12BB, villain jams
  18BB from BTN covering. Hero has KQo in SB.
  - Chip-EV call may be marginal (~+0.5BB).
  - If 1 spot above gets +$50 (2x BI), 2 spots gets
    +$100 (4x BI), 3 spots +$150 (6x BI).
  - Folding preserves a real shot at all three ladders;
    calling busts ~55% of the time = forfeit ~$50-100
    in expected ladder value.
  - Result: KQo fold beats KQo call here, even though
    chip-EV is positive.

GEM RULE: When evaluating ICM mistake/punt classification
in Del 4B, apply the 2x-BI heuristic as a sanity check.
A "borderline" call that's chip-EV positive but loses
clear ladder value (≥1 jump within reach) gets weighted
toward MISTAKE not MARGINAL. Conversely, a "punt-looking"
fold of a marginal hand near a pay jump can be CORRECT
even if chip-EV says call.

No detector needed. Mental model only — tag in narrative
when relevant.
Depth: 🟡 ICM phases only.


--------------------------------------------------------
J43. ICM RAISE-OR-FOLD (GENERALIZED FROM J34)
--------------------------------------------------------

GENERAL PRINCIPLE: In ICM, when Hero's hand is NOT
strong enough to call a raise, the correct line is
RAISE or FOLD — not flat-call.

This is the broader version of J34 (MP at <=30BB ICM:
raise-or-3bet-fold, no flat). Dave's expansion: the
principle applies across positions and depths in ICM
contexts, not just MP at <=30BB.

WHY FLATTING IS DISPROPORTIONATELY BAD IN ICM:
  - Flat-calling commits chips without claiming fold
    equity (no chance to win pot uncontested).
  - Hero's continuing range is capped (premiums would
    3-bet); villain's range is uncapped on subsequent
    streets.
  - Multiway risk: flatting OOP invites squeezes from
    behind. Squeezes in ICM are devastating because
    Hero must fold or commit a tournament-life-risking
    stack with a hand that wasn't strong enough to
    3-bet to begin with.
  - Postflop OOP realization is poor at low-mid SPR;
    ICM amplifies this (can't realize equity through
    multi-street pressure).

WHEN THE PRINCIPLE BINDS HARDEST:
  - Hero is short or mid stack (not big covering).
  - Hero is OOP relative to the opener.
  - There are players left to act (squeeze risk).
  - Tournament phase is bubble_zone or later.

WHEN THE PRINCIPLE RELAXES:
  - Hero is on the BTN closing action.
  - Hero is the BB (closing action; getting good pot
    odds; flatting range natural).
  - Big stack vs big stack (chip-EV dominates ICM).
  - Late_reg / post_reg (no ICM pressure).

EXISTING DETECTOR (J34): MP at <=30BB ICM, flag flats
of EP opens with AQo/AJs/ATs/AJo. That stays.

GENERALIZED FRAMING (J43): apply same lens to other
positions/depths in ICM — but DO NOT auto-flag
beyond J34's specific case until per-position thresholds
are validated. Drill-mode review: when a flat-call
appears in bubble_zone+ from any position other than
BTN/BB, ask "is this a J43 spot? Should it have been
3-bet or fold?"

GEM RULE: Cross-reference J43 in narrative when reviewing
ICM flat-calls outside J34's scope. Flag as MARGINAL
review candidate if the hand profile doesn't fit a
natural flatting range (e.g., suited connectors are
fine flats from BTN; offsuit broadways from CO/HJ in
bubble are J43 candidates). Do not auto-promote to
CLEAR mistake without hand-by-hand validation per the
Leak Validation Gate.

Auto-detector: J34 only (existing). J43 generalization
is review-time framing.
Depth: 🟡 ICM phases only.


--------------------------------------------------------
J44. IP 3-BET SIZING BY DEPTH
--------------------------------------------------------

When 3-betting IN POSITION (BTN/CO/HJ), sizing scales
with effective stack depth:

  <25BB eff:    2.5x the open
  25-40BB eff:  ~3.0x the open (linear scale)
  >40BB eff:    3.5x the open

COMPANION TO J30 (BB 3-bet = 5x, OOP).

RATIONALE:
  - Shallow (<25BB): smaller sizing because Hero's
    stack-to-pot ratio post-3-bet is already low; over-
    sizing commits Hero to the pot without flexibility.
    2.5x leaves room for fold-to-4bet at very short
    stacks (J38: 30BB = 2 streets framework applies).
  - Deep (>40BB): larger sizing (3.5x) because IP
    means Hero realizes equity better postflop and
    bigger pots leverage that positional advantage.
    Smaller sizing at depth invites too many flats and
    squeezes from behind.
  - Mid (25-40BB): linear scale; 3x is a reasonable
    default unless specific stack pressures exist.

OOP COMPARISON:
  - BB 3-bet = 5x always (J30) — the OOP penalty
    requires bigger sizing to deny realization.
  - SB 3-bet vs IP open = closer to BB sizing (4-5x)
    than to IP sizing.

CONFLICT CHECK:
  - J36 (ICM jam-threshold compression): in ICM at
    30-37BB, prefer 3-bet over jam. J44 specifies
    THE SIZING when J36 says "use 3-bet." 30-37BB
    in ICM: 3.0-3.5x is correct.
  - J38 (30BB = 2 streets): pot-sized cbets, plan
    all-in by turn. J44's 25-40BB range bridges
    J38's framework. At the lower end (~25-30BB),
    smaller 3-bet sizing (2.5-3.0x) gives Hero room
    to execute the 2-street plan; at the upper end
    (~35-40BB), larger sizing builds the pot to
    geometric streets.

GEM RULE (DOCUMENTED — DETECTOR PENDING):
  Track Hero IP 3-bet sizing by stack depth bucket.
  Flag deviations:
    - At <25BB: 3.5x+ sizing = oversized, commits
      Hero unnecessarily.
    - At >40BB: 2.5x or smaller = undersized, fails
      to leverage position.
    - In any bucket: |actual - target| > 0.5x = flag
      for review.
  Output: position-bucketed sizing distribution table
  in Del 2I+ (sizing consistency). Append IP 3-bet
  sizing as new sub-category alongside flop/turn/river
  geometric tracking.

DETECTOR IMPLEMENTATION (PENDING — v7.24.1):
  Parser work required:
    - Extract Hero's preflop 3-bet amount in BB from
      pf_sequence.
    - Extract opener's raise amount in BB.
    - Compute ratio = hero_3bet_bb / opener_raise_bb.
    - Add field `hero_3bet_size_x` (float) to hand
      record.
  Analyzer work required:
    - New tracker `ip_3bet_sizing` analogous to
      `bb_3bet_sizing` but bucketed by:
        position ∈ {CO, BTN, HJ}
        stack_bucket ∈ {<25, 25-40, 40+}
    - Flag hands where actual sizing deviates >0.5x
      from target.
  Tests required:
    - Add fixtures to test_hands_detectors.txt for
      each position/depth/sizing combination.
    - Verify all 54+ assertions still pass.

Auto-detector: PENDING (spec above).
Depth: 🟢 All depths, but sizing target shifts by depth.


========================================================
END OF APPENDIX J (UPDATED Apr 29)
========================================================


========================================================
APPENDIX K — JAKA ADVANCED FLOP PLAY
(Raising C-Bets IP, OOP Construction, IP Caller Stab,
 SRP vs SB, Flop Leading)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-18 (v7.13)
Source: Jaka "Mastering Advanced Flop Play" curriculum
Instructors: Thomas Boivin, Jeremy Menard
Sessions logged: April 12–16, 2026

Note: Same precedence rules as Appendices A-J. Dave rules
take precedence over Jaka where they conflict. Jaka is
the baseline framework.


--------------------------------------------------------
K1. RAISING C-BETS IN POSITION (CALLER IP FLOP X/R)
--------------------------------------------------------

GENERAL RULES:
- Main value raises: overpairs+, sometimes TP best kickers.
- Main bluffs: FDs > SDs > occasional backdoors & middle/
  bottom pairs.
- At <30BB: STOP raising draws that can't call a jam.
- At 30BB: TP best kickers played more statically (call
  more, raise less).
- Vs EP opener: need STRONGER threshold to raise.
- Turn after c-bet raise: blank turns → BIG or CHECK
  (not medium).
- Multiway: NO raising, OR max 5% if board doesn't nail
  BB range.

FREQUENCY TABLE — CO (caller) vs BU / CO vs EP (opener):
  Hand           | CO v BU 60BB | CO v BU 30BB | CO v EP 60BB | CO v EP 30BB
  Straight       | 75-100%      | 75-100%      | 75-100%      | 75-100%
  Top/Med Trips  | 50%*         | 50%*         | 30%*         | 30%*
  Bottom Trips   | 75-100%      | 75-100%      | 75-100%      | 75-100%
  2-Pair         | 50%          | 0-50%        | 50%          | 0-50%
  Overpair       | 75%          | 75%          | 25-50%       | 25-50%
  TP best kickers| 50%**        | 25%          | 25%**        | 25%
  Mid/Bottom Pair| 5-20%***     | 0-5%         | 0-5%         | 0-5%
  Flush Draw     | 50%          | 15%          | 15%          | 15%
  Open-ender     | 25%****      | 0-15%        | 15-25%       | 0-15%
  Gutshot        | 25%****      | 0-15%        | 10-20%       | 0-15%
  2OC+BDFD       | 25%          | 0-15%        | 15-25%       | 0-15%
  Ax/Kx 1OC+BDFD | 10%          | 0-10%        | 0-10%        | 0-10%

HIGH CARD DRY BOARDS:
  2 high + 1 low (KJ3r type):
    - Hits OOP range especially vs EP.
    - At 30BB: don't raise TP often; don't raise OE.
    - Value: bottom trips, TPTK up to 20%.
    - Call 2-pair (don't raise).
    - Bluff: ~10% — SDs + 2-card BDFD with Ax low kicker;
      FD 20-30% at 60BB, 10-20% at 30BB.

  1 high + 2 low (Q72r type):
    - Value: bottom & mid trips, TPTK up to 30%.
    - At 30BB: CALL bottom/mid trips — don't need to
      build pot.
    - Bluff: backdoor draws ~10%; FD 20-30% at 60BB,
      10-20% at 30BB.

PAIRED BOARDS:
  High pair (KK3 type):
    - Value: trips 20-30% — lower stack = lower raise freq.
    - No difference between high/low kicker.
    - Bluff: draws/backdoor 10-20% — lower stack = lower
      raise freq.

  Low pair (223 type):
    - Value: trips 50-70%, TPTK 10-20% — lower stack =
      lower raise freq.
    - No difference between high/low kicker.
    - Bluff: draws/backdoor 10-20% — lower stack = lower
      raise freq.

KEY THEME: Stack depth is the primary dial — shallower =
raise less across the board.

EXPLOITS:
  - If OOP NEVER 3-bets flop: INCREASE raise frequency —
    get to river easily OR buy free card.
  - If OOP c-bets TOO MUCH: DON'T raise more — widen
    CALL range slightly. Most EV from calling. Over-c-
    betting OOP → high turn x/f stat.

GEM INTEGRATION — K1:
  1. Track IP caller flop raise frequency. Separate from
     "stab when checked to" (see K3).
  2. At <30BB, flag raises with draws that can't call a
     jam (FD alone, OE alone) as errors.
  3. At 30BB, flag IP raises with TP best kicker as
     over-aggression (should mostly call).
  4. In multiway pots, flag IP flop raises unless board
     strongly doesn't hit BB (and even then cap at 5%).
  5. CO vs EP: require stronger threshold than CO vs BU.
     Flag marginal IP raises vs EP opens as errors.
  6. Against persistent over-cbetters: note that widening
     CALL range is higher-EV than widening raise range.
  7. Add to Del 2M sub-table: "IP Flop x/r Frequency" with
     target varying by opener position + stack depth.


--------------------------------------------------------
K2. PLAYING OOP AS PFR — "MAKE THEM FEAR YOUR CHECKS"
--------------------------------------------------------

CORE PHILOSOPHY: Checking OOP is NOT passive — it's a
weapon. When you check at a high frequency, your range
is strong and protected:
  - x/raise: overpairs, TPTK, strong draws + some
    backdoor bluffs.
  - x/call: most top pairs, 2nd/3rd pairs, PPs, weak
    draws, high cards.
  - x/fold: pure air.

If it goes check-check: ATTACK the turn aggressively.
IP caps themselves when they check back → bet turn
aggressively.

DEFAULT IS CHECKING OOP:
  In most formations (LP vs LP, MP vs MP), checking OOP
  is the default play.

WHEN TO BET MORE:
  - When significantly earlier than the flatter (MP vs
    LP, EP vs LP).
  - High cards + rainbow → bet more.
  - Mid-low + 2-tone/monotone → check more.
  - Deep (50BB+): who has the most nuts (2P+)? Is pot
    control important?
  - Shallow (40BB-): who makes/has the most pairs?

GENTLEMEN AND WARRIORS (position archetype):
  MP vs MP ("Gentlemen"): Lots of checking both sides,
    small bets, some trapping — RESPECT the x/r.
  MP vs LP / LP vs LP ("Warriors"): More aggression —
    more big c-bets, more x/raising, more x/calling.
  If c-betting vs LP: size UP on mid-low boards (esp.
    rainbow) to challenge suited hands and PPs.

KEY PRINCIPLES:
  - Play TOUGHER vs LP (from any position).
  - Play SOFTER vs EP/MP.
  - Size UP on mid/low semi-connected boards ("dynamic
    boards").
  - Always adapt to the specific villain (range, mood,
    your image).

OOP PFR DECISION FRAMEWORK (in-game):
  1. POSITIONS: Are we in heavy check territory?
     (MP vs MP, LP vs LP = yes; EP vs LP = less so)
  2. TEXTURE: Unsure = heavy check.
  3. VILLAIN'S RANGE: Too loose → bet more. Too tight
     → check more.
  4. HOW WILL HE REACT IF I...
     - CHECK → "check happy" (bet good hands!) or "bet
       happy" (x/raise A LOT)?
     - BET → sticky (pot control) or tight/fit-or-fold
       (bet more bluffs)?
  5. SIZING: Size UP when small doesn't challenge IP
     (e.g., 952, T93, T22, 554).

GEM INTEGRATION — K2:
  1. Classify every HU SRP flop by opener position
     matchup: EP/MP vs LP (Warrior), MP vs MP (Gentleman),
     LP vs LP (Warrior).
  2. In Gentleman spots, flag over-aggression (big c-bets,
     barrel-barrel-barrel lines without nuts) — respect
     villain's x/r range.
  3. In Warrior spots, flag under-aggression (all-checking
     lines as PFR) — range advantage should be exploited.
  4. When Hero checks OOP as PFR and it goes check-check,
     flag turn passivity. "When checked to turn, OOP PFR
     should bet much higher freq than IP would stab."
  5. Add to Del 2D sub-note: "OOP SRP c-bet% by opener
     matchup (Gentleman vs Warrior)".
  6. When Hero c-bets OOP on a mid-low rainbow vs LP
     flatter at small size, flag as potential sizing miss
     (should size UP to challenge suited/PPs).


--------------------------------------------------------
K3. PLAYING IP AS CALLER VS PFR (STAB + FLOAT)
--------------------------------------------------------

WHY IT MATTERS:
  - Frequent spot → big long-run impact.
  - Unintuitive → vastly misplayed by population → big
    edge available.
  - Goal: become VERY STICKY, especially vs over-cbetting
    villains.

STEP 1 — KNOW OOP's CORRECT STRATEGY:
  - Helps you play well OOP AND exploit when IP.
  - If OOP OVER-cbets → be sticky/aggro.
  - If OOP OVER-checks (rare) → be passive.
  - Punish mistakes on flop, turn, AND river.
  - "HU is a 0-sum game — don't let them get away."

GENTLEMEN AND WARRIORS (IP version):
  MP vs MP: Lots of checking both sides, small bets,
    some trapping — RESPECT the x/r.
  MP vs LP / LP vs LP: More aggression — get STICKIER
    vs over-cbetting, STAB more vs LP checks — be
    stickier vs x/r.

*** IP STABBING FREQUENCY VS CHECK IS STABLE ACROSS
    ALL TEXTURES IN THEORY: 40-60%. ***

This is the core metric. When OOP PFR checks to IP
caller, IP should bet ~40-60% of the time regardless
of board.

VILLAIN ARCHETYPES:
  vs OVER-CBETTING villain:
    - Don't fold! Float & raise aggressively.
    - vs check → attack (they're capped).
  vs OVER-PASSIVE villain:
    - If OOP defaults to checking most textures → be
      passive IP too. Their checks mean something.

SIZING GUIDE — STABBING IP VS CHECK:
  DEFAULT: Small & wide.
  2 HIGH-CARD BOARDS (AKx, ATx, KTx, QJx etc.) where IP
  doesn't need to bet for protection:
    → BIG & SELECTIVE.

IP CALLER DECISION FRAMEWORK (in-game):
  1. POSITIONS: Should OOP mostly check or bet?
  2. TEXTURE: Unsure = OOP mostly checks.
  3. Is OOP cbetting too much or not enough?
     - Too much (common) → Don't fold! Float & raise
       aggressively.
     - Not enough (rare) → Be passive, check back a lot.
  4. SIZING vs FREQUENCY:
     - Small & wide by default.
     - Big & polar on 2 high-card boards.

"The more capped OOP is, the more we attack flop+turn+
river."

GEM INTEGRATION — K3:
  1. NEW METRIC — IP Caller Stab Rate:
     - Definition: Hero IP as caller, OOP PFR checks
       flop to Hero, Hero's bet frequency.
     - Target: 40-60% stable across textures.
     - Flag <40% as "too passive when checked to."
     - Flag >70% as "stabbing too wide" (unless vs
       confirmed over-cbetter, which can't be checked
       from HH — so flag the raw rate).
  2. Split IP stab rate by board type:
     - 2 high-card (AKx, ATx, KTx, QJx): sizing should
       trend BIG.
     - Other boards: sizing should trend SMALL.
     - Flag sizing/board mismatches.
  3. Add to Del 2M as new row: "IP Stab Rate (checked to)"
     with count, %, target, color.
  4. When Hero IP faces OOP PFR c-bet and folds, track
     fold rate by sizing bucket. Flag fold% >55% to
     small c-bets as "over-folding vs over-cbetters"
     (population exploit miss).
  5. Track "Float → Turn Attack" rate: Hero calls flop
     IP, OOP checks turn, Hero bets turn. Target >70%.
     Flag <50% as missed capped-range exploitation.


--------------------------------------------------------
K4. C-BETTING AS RFI VS SB DEFEND (SRP, HU)
--------------------------------------------------------

KEY TAKEAWAYS:
  - Betting frequencies vs SB DECREASE from EP to BTN:
    your range expands, SB's stays condensed.
  - Betting frequencies INCREASE as stacks get shallower
    (less hand strength needed to stack off).
  - Stack size + opening position + board texture +
    villain tendencies = sizing decision.
  - Caution on MONOTONE and MIDDLING CONNECTED boards
    across all positions/depths.
  - PAIRED boards = best boards to attack on flop.
  - B55 (55% pot) is often the LARGEST size used in this
    dynamic.

BTN vs SB — 60BB (overall check 52%):
  - T-high through A-high: highest check frequencies;
    bet b30 or b55 when betting.
  - 8-high most favorable → high bet frequency mixing
    b30/b55, slightly favoring b55.
  - Low high cards (7-high and below): more favorable,
    often bet LARGER (b55).
  - Monotone + connected: high check frequency.
  - Paired boards: slightly higher bet frequency, mix
    b30/b55.

BTN vs SB — 30BB (overall check 47%):
  - T-high through A-high: still highest check; K-high
    least favorable; bet mix b20/b30.
  - 6-high through 3-high: bet at higher freq using
    b30/b55.
  - Monotone: 55% check. Middling connected: 48% check.
  - Paired: higher bet freq favoring b30.

CO vs SB — 60BB (overall check 44%):
  - A-high through T-high: LEAST favorable (50% check!);
    bet mix b30/b55 favoring b30.
  - 9-high most favorable, followed by 8-high: bet high
    freq mix b30/b55.
  - 7-high through 4-high: checked high freq; b55 slightly
    favored when betting.
  - Monotone: 55% check. Middling connected: 45% check.

CO vs SB — 30BB (overall check 39%):
  - Q-high most favorable, followed by 7-high through
    4-high; Q-high = small sizes, 7→4-high mix b30/b55.
  - T-high least favorable, followed by A-high, K-high,
    J-high; small sizes still favored.
  - Paired: high bet freq using small sizes.
  - Monotone + connected: similar caution.

MP vs SB — 30BB (overall check 30%):
  - Q-high most favorable, followed by A-high and J-high
    through 9-high; often b30 with some b20.
  - K-high far less valuable; 8-high through 5-high also
    less favorable; some b55 on lower high cards.
  - Monotone + middling connected: similar caution.
  - Paired: high bet frequencies.

CROSS-POSITION CHECK% SUMMARY:
  Position     | Check% 60BB | Check% 30BB | Best Boards       | Worst Boards
  MP vs SB     | —           | 30%         | Q-high, A/J-9 high| K-high, 8-5 high
  CO vs SB     | 44%         | 39%         | 9-8 high          | A-T high
  BTN vs SB    | 52%         | 47%         | 8-3 high          | T-A high

CORE RULE: Earlier position = more betting (tighter
range = more equity advantage). Shallower = more betting.
Monotone + connected = always caution. Paired = always
attack.

GEM INTEGRATION — K4:
  1. Track HU SRP c-bet frequency split by:
     - Hero's position (MP/CO/BTN, when SB is the defender)
     - Stack depth (60BB+, 30-60BB, <30BB)
     - Board type (paired, monotone, connected-mid, high
       card, low card)
  2. Apply position × depth targets:
     - MP vs SB @ 30BB: ~70% bet (30% check)
     - CO vs SB @ 60BB: ~56% bet (44% check)
     - CO vs SB @ 30BB: ~61% bet (39% check)
     - BTN vs SB @ 60BB: ~48% bet (52% check)
     - BTN vs SB @ 30BB: ~53% bet (47% check)
  3. Flag outliers >15pts from target.
  4. On paired boards vs SB: flag CHECKS as errors (should
     attack).
  5. On monotone vs SB: flag BIG c-bets as sizing errors
     (should be small or check).
  6. Add to Del 2E sub-table: "SRP HU C-Bet by Position
     vs SB Defend (K4 targets)".


--------------------------------------------------------
K5. C-BETTING OOP (CONSTRUCTION + X/R) — Jeremy Menard
--------------------------------------------------------

COMMON MISTAKES:
  1. C-betting too often.
  2. Choosing suboptimal hands when c-betting.
  3. Using improper sizings.
  4. No balance (c-betting all good hands, checking
     all bad hands).
  5. Not check-raising enough.

HAND SELECTION & SIZING RULES:
  Choose hands with: reasonable potential to improve,
  strong blockers to villain's strong hands, draws, OR
  strong bluffing ability based on board texture and
  nutted hand advantage.

  STRONG RANGE ADV + STRONG NUTTED ADV:
    → C-bet WIDE, SMALL (20-30%), with some 60% sizings.

  NO RANGE ADV but STRONG NUTTED ADV:
    → C-bet NARROW, LARGE (60-80%).

  MONOTONE BOARDS:
    → C-bet NARROW, SMALL (20-30%).

  PAIRED BOARD — paired card NOT in our favor:
    → C-bet FREQUENTLY, SMALL size.

  PAIRED BOARD — paired card IN our favor (strong equity
  + nutted advantage):
    → C-bet VERY FREQUENTLY, MIX small and large.

*** KEY SIZING PRINCIPLE ***
  Range advantage → WIDE + SMALL.
  Nutted advantage only → NARROW + BIG.
  Monotone → NARROW + SMALL.

CHECK RAISING OOP AS OPEN RAISER:
  - Mix in x/r FREQUENTLY to balance checking range.
  - X/R hands: strongest parts of range + strongest
    draws + strong draw blockers + some strong backdoor
    draws with overcards.
  - X/R sizing = function of effective stack size AND
    villain's bet size.

BvB OOP C-BETS (SB as PFR vs BB):
  - BB range very wide, SB raising range condensed →
    SB has equity advantage on certain boards.
  - SB has STRONG equity + nut advantage → c-bet large
    part of range for SMALL size.
  - Equities run closer but SB has strong nut advantage
    → LARGER sizes favored including some OVERBETTING.

GEM INTEGRATION — K5:
  1. When Hero c-bets OOP as PFR:
     - Classify range adv (yes/no) from position matchup.
     - Classify nut adv (yes/no) from board × range.
     - Flag sizing/frequency mismatches per the 3-rule
       principle above.
  2. Track Hero's OOP x/r frequency as PFR:
     - Flop: target 8-15% (not all checks are x/fold).
     - Turn: target 10-20% (Hero checked flop OOP,
       villain bet, Hero raised turn after calling flop).
     - Flag "never x/raises" as construction error —
       check range becomes exploitable.
  3. For BvB SB-as-PFR c-bets:
     - Wide-small on strong equity+nut boards.
     - Flag narrow/big as construction error on these
       boards (should be wide-small).
     - On closer-equity boards with nut adv, allow
       overbet sizing.
  4. Cross-reference with Appendix F (BB 3-bet pots OOP)
     — K5 applies to SRP OOP only. 3BP OOP uses F.


--------------------------------------------------------
K6. FLOP LEADING + CONTINUING TURNS & RIVERS — T. Boivin
--------------------------------------------------------

WHAT A FLOP LEAD IS AND WHY IT MATTERS:
  - Capitalize on range & nut advantage when BB vs IP.
  - Deny IP's equity:
    - They don't get to check back (free card).
    - They don't get to c-bet-call and see turn/river
      with initiative.
  - Take initiative WITHOUT inflating the pot (cheaper
    than x/r).

WHEN TO HAVE A LEADING RANGE — BASELINE:
  Leading is RARE by default. Solver data BB vs BTN:
  - Overall: 97.5% check, 2.5% lead.
  - Leading range is extremely narrow in most spots.

BOARDS WHERE BB LEADS AT MEANINGFUL FREQUENCY:
  LOW PAIRED BOARDS vs BTN (664, 663, 644, 665 type):
    - Leading frequency jumps to 35-48% at 33% pot.
    - This is the primary exception to the "always check"
      default.

FULL SUMMARY — WHEN TO LEAD (range smashes the flop):

  BB vs IP (SRP):
    - LOW STRAIGHTS (765, 643): ANY depth.
    - Best paired boards for BB (665, 553, 77A): 60BB+.

  3-BET POTS:
    - LOW STRAIGHTS: 60BB+.
    - MID-HIGH SEMI-CONNECTED (JT7, T96): 30BB-.

  BvB LIMP/CALL:
    - MID-HIGH SEMI-CONNECTED (JT7, T96): 40BB-.

LEADING SIZING:

  MERGED LEAD (wide range, value/protection) → SMALL
  (20-33%):
    - BB vs IP straights: L20-33%.
    - 3BP straights: L20-33%.

  POLAR LEAD (very good hands + bluffs only) → BIG:
    - BB vs IP 80BB+ paired flops: L67-100%.
    - IsoR 40BB- mid connected: L67-100%.
    - 3BP shallow (30BB-) mid-connected: L67-all-in!

IMPLEMENTING FLOP LEADS — THEORY vs PRACTICE:
  THEORY: Mix everything except 0 EQ hands.
  PRACTICE: Check available exploits FIRST — maximise
  villain's mistakes.

  If IP will over-cbet when you check:
    - X/R value and strong bluffs.
    - Lead weak backdoors (exploit).

  If IP will over-check back:
    - Lead vulnerable value hands.

  If IP will under or over-raise vs your lead:
    - Skew range toward bluff or value accordingly.

EXPLOITS:
  - Lead MORE vs passive IP.
  - Check back MORE vs passive OOP.
  - EXPLOIT: if BB never leads → IP should check more
    (BB range is uncapped/stronger when they check).

TURN AFTER FLOP LEAD:
  MERGED lead on low board, low turn:
    - Small, or small + big (if many nuts available).
  MERGED lead, low board, K+ turn:
    - Polar → BIG only (to stack off).

RIVER AFTER LEAD TURN:
  After SMALL turn bet:
    - Small (thin value) + big (traps & rivered nuts).
  After BIG turn bet:
    - Nuts doesn't change → BIG only (range very polar).
    - Nuts changes → SMALL (turn nuts) + BIG (new river
      nuts).

GEM INTEGRATION — K6:
  1. NEW METRIC — Hero Flop Lead Rate (as BB or BvB caller
     vs PFR):
     - Denominator: Hero in BB or SB, called PF, saw flop.
     - Numerator: Hero bet first on flop (donk/lead).
     - Baseline target: ~2-5% overall.
     - Split by board type:
       * Low paired boards: can be 35-48% (acceptable).
       * Low straight boards (765, 643): 20-40% (acceptable).
       * Mid-high semi-connected in 3BP (30BB-): 20-40%.
       * All others: should be <5%.
     - Flag leads on non-favored boards as errors.
  2. When Hero leads flop, check sizing vs board:
     - Straights/merged → small (20-33%). Flag big as error.
     - 80BB+ paired / shallow mid-connected → big
       (67-100%). Flag small as error (underbetting polar
       range).
  3. When Hero checks BB on a low paired board vs BTN as
     opener (60BB+), flag as "missed lead opportunity"
     for coaching review. Do NOT auto-flag as mistake
     — default is still check; this is exploit territory.
  4. When Hero leads and faces a raise:
     - Evaluate raise frequency and response.
     - Strong hands continue; thin leads face-up.
  5. Turn continuation after lead:
     - If Hero led flop small and checked turn → flag as
       missed turn barrel on favorable turns.
     - If Hero led flop big and sized down on blank turn
       → flag as sizing error (polar range = stay big).
  6. Add to Del 2M or new Del 2M+: "Flop Lead Profile"
     (rate, by board, sizing compliance).

========================================================
END OF APPENDIX K
========================================================



========================================================
NET_BB CALCULATION FIX (Session 18 — v7.4)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-06

CRITICAL BUG FIXED: net_bb was calculated as
  (collected - hero_start_stack) / bb
which made every winning hand show massive losses.
A hero with 100BB who won a 5BB pot showed -95BB.

CORRECT FORMULA:
  Won:    net_bb = (collected - hero_committed) / bb
  Lost:   net_bb = -hero_committed / bb
  Folded: net_bb = -hero_committed / bb

hero_committed = sum of all chips Hero put in (antes,
blinds, calls, bets, raises across all streets).

Parser now tracks hero_committed_bb per hand.


========================================================
DATA-DRIVEN FINDINGS (Session 18 — corrected net_bb)
========================================================

With correct net_bb, the session picture changes completely.
Previous analysis based on broken numbers was misleading.

CORRECT FINDINGS:
  1. PFR OOP is the #1 drain (-3.97 BB/hand HU OOP vs
     -1.81 IP). OOP is 2.2x more expensive than IP.
  2. 88 is the worst single hand (-8.0 BB/h, 5/7 SD losses).
     Paying off on high boards with underpair.
  3. Ax offsuit loses mainly at showdown (outkicked).
     ATo worst at -7.4/hand.
  4. Caller play is near breakeven (-0.62/hand). The
     "convert calls to 3-bets" advice was WRONG.
  5. Multiway is profitable (+2.26/hand 4+way).
     HU is where the bleeding happens (-2.47/hand).

REPORT FORMAT NOTES (Ron feedback):
  - TLDR must be structured (bullets/table, not blob)
  - All stats must include comparison: "2.8% (-40% vs expected)"
  - Aggression tables: consolidate flop+turn in one row
    per draw type, show "26.1% vs 55% GTO" with color coding
  - Fewer tables, more density per table



========================================================
SELF-UPDATE RULE (Session 18 — v7.5)
========================================================

CRITICAL: Whenever analysis discovers a finding that changes
how future sessions should be parsed, reported, or evaluated,
Claude MUST immediately update the parser and/or instructions
file. Do NOT defer fixes to "next session." The cycle is:

  1. Discover finding (e.g., net_bb is broken)
  2. Fix parser/instructions IMMEDIATELY
  3. Re-run analysis with fix
  4. Present corrected files to Ron

This prevents the same bug from corrupting multiple sessions.
If Ron identifies a misclassification, rule change, or format
issue, treat it as a P0 fix — update files before continuing.


========================================================
POSITION NORMALIZATION (Session 18 — v7.5)
========================================================

Parser now computes eff_pos (effective position) based on
distance from BTN, adjusted for table size:

  Table    UTG    UTG+1   MP    HJ    CO    BTN
  9-ring   EP     EP2     MP    LJ    HJ    CO    BTN
  8-ring   EP     MP      LJ    HJ    CO    BTN
  7-ring   MP     LJ      HJ    CO    BTN
  6-ring   LJ     HJ      CO    BTN

IMPORTANT: Range charts (Poker_Ranges_Text.txt) assume 9-ring.
When looking up ranges, use eff_pos not raw position.
Example: UTG+1 in 8-ring = MP. Look up MP ranges, not UTG+1.

All reports should show eff_pos alongside raw position when
relevant (e.g., "UTG+1 (eff: MP, 8-ring)").

Blinds (SB, BB) are always SB, BB regardless of table size.


========================================================
SESSION 18 CONFIRMED FINDINGS (v7.5)
========================================================

These are DATA-CONFIRMED findings, not hypotheses:

1. CHECK-FOLD OOP MORE (biggest single finding)
   26 SD losses after check→call→call→SD OOP = -496 BB
   When PFR OOP and you check flop, villain bets:
   - STOP calling 3 streets with TP weak kicker, 2nd pair
   - Check-call ONE street, then re-evaluate
   - Check-fold weak hands immediately

2. CALLER PLAY IS NEAR BREAKEVEN (-0.62/hand)
   Do NOT "convert calls to 3-bets" wholesale.
   GTO confirms flats are correct in most spots.
   Flatting from BTN (+4.11/h) and HJ (+2.92/h) is profitable.

3. OFFSUIT BROADWAYS FROM LP: FLAT > 3-BET
   3-bet = -3.42/hand, Flat = +0.57/hand (session data)
   AJo specifically: Open +21.5, 3-bet -64.5, Flat +7.7
   Keep flatting until 3-bet pot postflop play improves.

4. CALLER IP MADE HAND LEAK IS SMALLER THAN THOUGHT
   10 of 17 checked hands were correct (underpairs, MW).
   Only 2 clear HU misses (ATo on Ad2c8c, A6s on 9sTcAc).
   Don't overweight this leak.

5. 88 LOSSES ARE MOSTLY COOLERS (5/7 SD losses)
   Not a rule change — monitor but don't overreact to
   small sample. QQ over 88, JJ over 88, set over pair.



========================================================
LINE-BASED ANALYSIS (v8.0 — Session 18)
========================================================

CONCEPT: "Lines, not stats." The complete action sequence from
preflop through river is the atomic unit of analysis. Aggregate
stats are symptoms. Lines are the disease.

PARSER NOW TRACKS per hand:
  hand['line']             = "SRP_PFR_OOP_cbet-xc-fold_SD_lost"
  hand['line_actions']     = "cbet-xc-fold"
  hand['pot_type']         = "SRP" | "3BP" | "4BP"
  hand['hero_street_actions'] = {flop: 'cbet', turn: 'xc', river: 'fold'}

LINE FORMAT:
  {PotType}_{Role}_{Position}_{flop_action}-{turn_action}-{river_action}_{SD?}_{outcome}

  Actions per street:
    cbet  = PFR bet first on flop
    bet   = non-PFR bet or later street bet
    raise = raised villain's bet
    call  = called villain's bet
    xr    = check-raised
    xc    = check-called
    xf    = check-folded
    x     = checked through (no villain bet)
    fold  = folded to villain's bet (not after check)
    jam   = went all-in

  Examples:
    SRP_PFR_OOP_cbet-x-xf_lost     = c-bet flop, checked turn, check-folded river
    SRP_Caller_IP_call-bet-bet_won  = called flop, bet turn+river
    3BP_PFR_IP_cbet-bet-bet_SD_won = 3-bet pot, c-bet + barrel + barrel → SD win

REPORT DELIVERABLE 9 — TOP LOSING LINES:
  Sort all lines by TOTAL NET BB (frequency × magnitude).
  Report top 10 losing lines with:
    1. Line description
    2. Count + total BB + avg BB/hand
    3. Confidence indicator (LOW <30, MED 30-100, HIGH 100+)
    4. Top 3 example hand IDs
    5. Suggested fix

KNOWN ISSUE (v7.6): Some preflop-only hands are misclassified
when postflop streets exist but actions aren't captured. Fix
in progress for v7.7 — verify street text parsing for edge cases.

CROSS-SESSION AGGREGATION (planned):
  Parser will support --aggregate mode to load all sessions.
  Minimum 10k hands before trusting line-level stats.
  50k hands target for high-confidence leak finding.

SRP vs 3BP SPLIT:
  All postflop stats must separate by pot type:
  - SRP (Single Raised Pot): pf_raise_count <= 1
  - 3BP (3-Bet Pot): pf_raise_count == 2
  - 4BP+: pf_raise_count >= 3
  Different SPR → different strategy → must not mix.

REPORT FORMAT UPDATES (v8):
  TLDR: Structured bullets, not blob text.
  All stats: Include comparison vs expected.
    Example: "2.8% premiums (-40% vs 4.7% expected)"
  Aggression tables: Consolidated (flop+turn in one row per draw type).
  New section: Top Losing Lines (Deliverable 9).



========================================================
APPENDIX L — HUNGRY HORSE RULES (HH1-HH18)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-19 (v7.15)
Source: Hungry Horse Poker YouTube channel (coach Mark/Maron).
18 strategy videos distilled; ~1.46MB transcript corpus.
Channel is 200BB live cash-focused — rules tagged with
depth applicability for MTT translation.

Priority relative to other coaching rules:
  - Dave (J1-J40) takes precedence over H rules when they conflict.
  - Jaka (K1-K6) and Amit rules take precedence when they conflict.
  - Ron's own data (session_history + GEM leak tracker) takes
    precedence over all coaching rules when they conflict.
  - H rules mostly COMPLEMENT rather than conflict — they fill
    gaps in sizing framework, underbluff catalog, and opponent
    selection.

Depth tags:
  🟢 = All depths (applies wherever postflop exists)
  🟡 = SPR ≥3 (typical MTT postflop above ~25BB eff)
  🔴 = Deep only (≥80BB eff — cash-adjacent geometry required)

At <15BB effective, H rules are overridden by push/fold / ICM /
Dave J33-J40.

Unifying philosophy (three ideas that drive every H rule):
  1. Put opponents in nodes where they make the biggest mistakes.
  2. Live/rec populations share three universal IP-caller mistakes:
     (a) overstab when checked to, (b) telegraph hand strength
     with sizing (big=strong, small=weak on dynamic boards),
     (c) don't protect checkback range with strong hands.
  3. Fear and greed drive rec decisions. Fear → size DOWN with
     strong-but-vulnerable hands (inverse of GTO). Greed → size
     UP on rivers with nuts, DOWN with bluffs (inverse of GTO).


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 1 — SIZING FRAMEWORKS (HH1-HH4)
--------------------------------------------------------

HH1. FLOP SIZING QUESTION — "biggest size where villain raises
    strong stuff AND calls weak stuff" 🟡
    
    One question drives flop sizing. Biggest bet where villain
    still raises their strong hands (2P+, sets, big combo draws)
    AND still calls with their weak hands (weak TP, medium
    draws, underpairs).
    
    Defaults:
      Single-raise pot heads-up: ~50% pot
      3-bet pot heads-up:        ~30-40% pot (absolute pot is
                                  larger, so relative sizing
                                  shrinks)
      Multiway:                  ~30-40% pot
    
    EXCEPTION — static/dry boards (A72r, AJ4r, K84 rainbow):
    villains do NOT raise-strong-call-weak on these boards
    because they don't fear the turn. Use OVERBET or CHECK
    strategy instead — skip HH1 on dry boards (see HH8).
    
    Applies: single-raise pots and 3-bet pots when SPR permits
    a 3-street game. Rule of thumb: SPR ≥3 on flop.

HH2. TURN SIZING QUESTION — "is villain CAPPED?" 🟡
    
    One question drives turn sizing:
      YES capped  → go BIG (overbet OK when truly capped).
                    Villain's TP and draws are inelastic; extract
                    max from the hands that won't fold.
      NO uncapped → go SMALL. Let strong hands raise and put
                    more money in for us; keep draws in.
    
    CAPPED means: villain has already had the opportunity to
    raise their strongest hands on the flop, didn't, so their
    turn range is weighted toward medium strength.
    UNCAPPED means: villain still has sets/flushes/2P in range.
    
    Applies: most turn decisions when Hero has position or the
    betting lead. SPR ≥2 for sizing to matter.

HH3. RIVER SIZING QUESTION — "what size would I bet with the
    OPPOSITE hand?" 🟢
    
    One question drives river sizing:
      Value-betting?  Ask "what size would I bet as a bluff?"
      Bluffing?       Ask "what size would I bet for value?"
    
    Value and bluff sizing often DIVERGE on rivers — this is
    fine. Example: blank river in 3BP, pot 450, stack 850.
      Value with trips: bet 450 (want AJ to call)
      Bluff with busted draw: jam 850 (want AJ to fold)
    When the river CHANGES the nuts (flush completes), usually
    value wants small (target TP that hasn't shriveled) and
    bluff wants small too (fold draws, don't need to fold TP).
    
    Applies: every river decision with value-bluff mix.

HH4. ELIMINATE MEDIUM BET SIZES 🟡
    
    Medium bets (40-70% pot on turn and river) are usually the
    worst option. Either go very small (keep villain wide +
    weak, let them over-fold later) or very big (target
    inelastic hands that won't fold regardless). Medium gets
    neither goal.
    
    EXCEPTIONS where medium IS correct:
      - Single-raise pot flop c-bet (~50% pot is fine; absolute
        pot is small)
      - 4-bet pot on low boards (KK vs 964r — medium ~2/3 pot,
        JJ/QQ never folds, AK/AQ isn't committed anyway)
      - Value-bet when bluff sizing wants both very big AND
        very small (medium becomes the only shared size)
    
    Applies: all turn and river decisions where sizing is a
    choice. Cross-check against HH2 (turn) and HH3 (river) before
    defaulting to ~half-pot out of habit.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2 — THE KEY DEPTH ADJUSTMENT (HH5)
--------------------------------------------------------

HH5. DO NOT TRY TO FOLD TOP PAIR AT ≤100BB EFFECTIVE 🟢
    
    SINGLE MOST IMPORTANT RULE IN APPENDIX L. Covers ~95% of
    Ron's MTT postflop volume.
    
    At 200BB+ deep: villain is elastic on rivers; empty-clip
    targeting TP folds works. TP at 200BB is willing to fold
    to overbet jams.
    
    At ≤100BB: villain is INELASTIC with TP on rivers — they
    are NOT folding top pair to any size. Empty-clipping at
    100BB eff on a dry-ish board against someone who can have
    AJ is lighting money on fire.
    
    RULE: Empty-clip at ≤100BB eff ONLY when villain's range
    CANNOT contain top pair (e.g., they checked back an A-high
    flop → they don't have Ax → TP folds fine).
    
    Pair with HH2: the "go big when capped" direction only
    generates value when TP folds. At shallow depths the
    capped-range doesn't fold TP, so "big" means ~pot, not
    1.5x pot.
    
    Applies: every postflop bluff-size decision at effective
    stacks ≤100BB. Always-check at <60BB unless you've ruled
    out TP from villain's range.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 3 — BLUFF / VALUE SELECTION (HH6, HH7, HH14)
--------------------------------------------------------

HH6. FOLD-EQUITY EQUATION 🟢
    
    Heuristic for deciding which draws to barrel and which to
    give up:
      MORE fold equity (villain capped + Hero deep)
        → need LESS hand equity to bluff profitably
      LESS fold equity (villain uncapped or Hero shallow)
        → need MORE hand equity (stick to combo draws,
           nut flush draws, 8+ out draws)
    
    Concrete application:
      Gutshot on capped turn at 150BB eff → fire (low hand
        equity is fine because high fold equity makes up for it)
      Gutshot on uncapped turn at 40BB eff → give up (low
        hand equity + low fold equity = torch)
      Combo draw on any turn → fire at almost any depth (hand
        equity carries the bluff)
    
    Applies: every turn/river semi-bluff decision. Especially
    useful for drill mode — forces Hero to ask which factor is
    dominant before pulling the trigger.

HH7. BLUFF THE LOOSE/AGGRESSIVE VILLAIN, NOT THE TIGHT/PASSIVE 🟢
    
    Counterintuitive. Loose villains reach rivers with a much
    WEAKER distribution (Mark's example: 41% TP+ for loose vs
    55% for nit). Aggressive villains arrive at turn/river
    with too much air because they bet wider ranges postflop.
    Tight/passive villains are supposed to fold 57% in GTO but
    will UNDERFOLD because their range is actually strong.
    
    Most profitable bluff targets: loose/aggro players.
    Least profitable bluff targets: tight/passive players
    (value-bet thin against these, don't bluff).
    
    FOLD-BUTTON OVERRIDE (Ron-specific):
    Against pure calling stations at low-buy-in bounty MTTs,
    HH7 inverts — loose-passive fish often lack a fold button
    for the weak portion of their river range. Flag villain
    type before acting: "Does this loose villain actually fold
    top pair on a scary river? Or does he call any size?" If
    no fold button, value-bet thin and skip the bluff.
    
    Applies: opponent-selection decisions in any spot where
    Hero has a non-trivial bluff choice. Especially relevant
    for MTT squeeze / 3-bet bluff targeting.

HH14. DOUBLE-CHECK INDUCES OVERBLUFF FROM OOP 🔴
    
    On blank turns after Hero checks range OOP as PFR (HH8)
    and villain checks back the flop: CHECK AGAIN on the turn.
    
    Why this works:
    - Villain's showdown-value hands (small pairs, A-high)
      that checked back the flop now stab to protect against
      our "Ace King" or take control.
    - Villain's air that checked back the flop now stabs
      because we twice showed weakness.
    - Both halves of villain's range fire, then Hero
      check-raises HUGE with value, combo draws, and selected
      air — maximizing fold equity across two streets.
    
    Applies: OOP as PFR on single-raise pots at SPR ≥3 against
    non-passive villains. Deep only — needs geometry to support
    check-raise + river jam.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 4 — OOP AS PFR DEFAULTS (HH8, HH9)
--------------------------------------------------------

HH8. CHECK RANGE OOP ON DYNAMIC/WET BOARDS WHERE VILLAIN
    WILL OVERSTAB 🔴
    
    Default framework for OOP-as-PFR postflop:
    
    Is the board likely to get stabbed if we check?
      YES (dynamic + wet + villain not a passive nit)
        → check ENTIRE range
      NO (static + dry, or passive villain)
        → bet thick value, check the rest
    
    Facing the stab (board likely to be stabbed, villain stabs):
      Stab BIG on any board:
        CR with CPFS + combo draws only
        Call thick value, thin value, high-equity draws
        Fold SDV + low-equity draws
      Stab SMALL on dynamic/wet board (villain overbluffs):
        CR wide — CPFS, combo draws, thick value, high-eq
          draws, low-eq draws
        Call thin value + SDV
        Fold air
      Stab SMALL on static/dry board (villain does NOT telegraph):
        CR narrow — CPFS + combo draws only (same as stab-big)
        Villain can still have strong hands in the small size
          on dry boards because they don't fear turns
    
    Check-raise sizing: 6-10x when check-raising at depth
    (SPR ≥5+). Smaller = lets villain get away too cheaply
    on lines they've never seen; they play worst against
    unfamiliar large sizes.
    
    Ron-specific note: this directly addresses Ron's #1
    confirmed leak (check-call-call-showdown OOP as PFR).
    The "check range" instinct is correct. What's been missing
    is the CR-aggressively-when-they-stab-small leg.
    
    Depth: 🔴 Deep only. At <50BB eff the multi-street follow-
    through breaks — default to bet-bet-bet instead when you
    can get the money in by river. Dave's equity-shift turn
    rules (max 50% sizing on dynamic boards) still apply and
    take precedence.

HH9. "BEST LINE IN POKER" — SMALL C-BET FLOP + CHECK TURN
    (WITH SDV) + BLUFF-CATCH RIVER 🟡
    
    As IP PFR in single-raise or 3-bet pots on wet/dynamic
    boards, when Hero has a showdown-value hand:
    
    Flop:  c-bet small (33-50% pot). HH1 framework.
    Turn:  CHECK BACK when Hero has SDV (middle pair, A-high,
           thin value). Do not keep barreling.
    River: bluff-catch medium sizes; fold to pot+; value-bet
           thinly when villain checks to you.
    
    Why this is profitable:
    - Villains call too wide pre-flop
    - Villains raise too much strong stuff + call too much
      weak stuff on small c-bet (HH1 at work)
    - Range that reaches river is wider + weaker + air-heavy
    - Villains let fear+greed drive sizing: strong hands
      overbet river, bluffs use small sizes → face-up
    
    Standard response pattern on river:
      Villain bets half-pot  → CALL (overbluffed)
      Villain bets pot+      → FOLD (underbluffed)
      Villain checks         → VALUE-BET small
    
    Ron-specific note: pairs with HH8 as the IP-side of the
    same population-exploit framework. HH8 covers OOP-as-PFR,
    HH9 covers IP-as-PFR with SDV.
    
    Depth: 🟡 SPR ≥3. At <25BB eff the 3-street geometry
    breaks and the turn check becomes a trap that leaves us
    unable to fold-win-enough on river.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 5 — UNDERBLUFF AND OVERBLUFF CATALOGS (HH10, HH11)
--------------------------------------------------------

HH10. UNDERBLUFFED-LINES CATALOG (9 lines where Hero folds
     everything that can't beat value) 🟢
     
     Live and low-stakes online populations almost never bluff
     these lines. Fold medium hands; do not hero-call; do not
     turn bluff-catchers into bluffs:
     
     1. CHECK-BACK FLOP + RAISE TURN as PFR. Trap range. Pocket
        queens / big pairs that slow-played flop and now
        want to protect against bad cards. Fold TP or weaker;
        continue 2P+ only.
     
     2. TRIPLE-BARREL ACE-HIGH BOARD small size IP as PFR. Thin
        value (JJ-TT, occasional 2P). Bluffs don't exist — no
        natural semi-bluff candidates on A72 boards. Fold TP.
     
     3. TRIPLE-BARREL MULTI-BROADWAY / STRAIGHT-HEAVY BOARD
        from EP. Natural bluffs don't exist — hands like AK/AQ
        arrive as SDV not bluffs. Fold anything less than
        straight.
     
     4. BB or CLOSING-SEAT 3-BET vs EP OPEN. Strong range —
        players tempted to call instead of 3-bet close the
        action. Pairs with Dave J18 (population under-3-bets).
        88 is a fold; KK proceed cautiously but not an auto
        5-bet.
     
     5. CHECK-CALL / CHECK-CALL + BIG RIVER DONK after Hero
        showed aggression (PFR → c-bet → overbet turn → donk
        river). Nuts range — usually flushes. NOTE: small
        river donk (25-33% pot) in same line is different and
        may be thin-value bluff-catch attempt.
     
     6. MULTIWAY DONK from pre-flop caller on flop. Strong-
        but-vulnerable hands (TP+ protecting equity). Bluffs
        don't exist multiway. Fold medium, raise only premiums.
     
     7. 3-BET POT DONK from cold-caller. Very strong —
        QQ+/AK-type hands. Cold-caller 3BP flats are already
        narrow; donking them is max strength. Fold all but
        AA/KK+set of top card.
     
     8. TURN CHECK-RAISE when Hero has shown only aggression
        (PFR + c-bet + turn barrel big, villain CRs). Nuts
        range — KJ, sets, 2P+. Fold TP and overpairs.
     
     9. LARGE C-BET SIZE (pot-sized flop bet). Range too strong,
        not enough bluffs in the large size. Matches Dave J19
        pattern. Fold medium, continue only 2P+.
     
     Applies: all depths, but especially 60-100BB where Hero
     actually has decisions vs. just calling for pot odds.
     At <30BB, pot odds math often overrides HH10 — call down
     with TP+.

HH11. OVERBLUFFED-LINES CATALOG (7 lines where Hero calls wider
     or turns bluff-catchers into bluffs) 🟢
     
     Live populations bluff too often in these spots. Call
     down; consider bluff-raising if villain is capable:
     
     1. HEADS-UP SMALL DONK FLOP from pre-flop caller. Garbage
        range — mostly weak pairs, draws, random floats.
        Call both value and bluffs; don't raise (want villain
        to keep bluffing later streets).
     
     2. WIDE-vs-WIDE RANGE C-BET IP AS 3-BETTOR on A-high flop
        (e.g., we 3-bet cutoff from BTN, flop A-Q-8). Villain
        should c-bet 35-45% in GTO; live population c-bets
        90%+. CR aggressively with air.
     
     3. VILLAIN C-BETS + WE CHECK-BACK TURN WITH SDV + VILLAIN
        BETS RIVER. HH9 line but inverted (we're the villain
        target). On medium river size (33-66% pot) this is
        heavily bluff-weighted. Call TP and thin value.
     
     4. VILLAIN STABS SMALL TURN after flop-check-check. Having
        shown weakness twice, villain gets cart blanche to
        bluff. Call down linear (pair+, not king-high
        attempt to bluff-catch).
     
     5. ACE-X TURN DOUBLE-BARREL as PFR in SRP wide-vs-wide.
        Villain sees "good card for my range" and over-
        barrels. Call turn wide; most villains give up river
        when they don't have it. Pairs with "fifth street
        chicken" — let villain keep bluffing.
     
     6. DOUBLE-CHECK FROM HERO AS PFR OOP → VILLAIN BETS RIVER.
        Villain induced to overbluff after Hero shows weakness
        twice. See HH14 for the offensive version of this line.
     
     7. THE "BEST LINE IN POKER" NODE (HH9) from villain's side.
        When villain c-bets small, checks back turn, and we
        bet river — villain overbluffs this exact sequence
        when they're in our shoes. From Hero's side as the
        caller of that line, call medium river sizes.
     
     Applies: all depths, but most profitable at 50-100BB
     where villains have room to overbet and Hero has stack
     to call.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 6 — CONCRETE BLUFF AND VALUE SPOTS (HH12, HH13)
--------------------------------------------------------

HH12. TOP-5 HUGE-VALUE SPOTS (go bigger than standard here) 🔴
     
     1. BLANK TURN when villain is capped. AJ isn't folding to
        any size; pot-size or overbet to maximize.
     
     2. BOTTOM-CARD PAIRS TURN OR RIVER. Villains get stickier
        with TP when board pairs (think their hand "improved"
        to 2P+). Treat as blank turn; go big. Bonus: their
        draws get more elastic on paired boards (fear of "not
        knowing if I win when I get there") — go small if
        targeting draws, big if targeting TP.
     
     3. VILLAIN TAKES BET-BET-CHECK LINE on river. River check
        signals intent to check-call (rec players rarely check
        to bluff-raise). Overbet for thin value when Hero has
        TP-or-better — they put us on busted draws.
     
     4. VILLAIN CHECK-RAISES FLOP + CHECKS TURN when nuts
        change (flush completes turn after flop CR from
        villain). Villain's range is sets + 2P, NOT flushes
        (aggressive-type villains would keep betting flushes).
        Overbet turn to set up low river SPR; sets/2P don't
        fold to any size on turn.
     
     5. BIG CHECK-RAISE ON FLOP OOP AS CALLER. 6-10x sizing
        instead of standard 3-4x. Matches HH8 sizing logic —
        villain plays worst against unfamiliar huge sizes.
        Targets the inelastic top of their stabbing range.
     
     Applies: SPR ≥3 for geometry. At shallow depths, "go
     bigger than standard" = pot-size, not overbet.

HH13. TOP-5 BLUFF SPOTS (cleanest spots to empty the clip) 🟡
     
     1. WIDE-vs-WIDE RANGE-C-BET FACE. We 3-bet linear on
        BTN vs CO, villain flat-calls wide, flops A-high,
        range-bets 35%. CR small size — high FE from their
        marginal floats. If called, give up unless we pick up
        equity.
     
     2. WET/DYNAMIC FLOP + CLEAN RUNOUT. Villain capped after
        flop check-call. Jam river on blank to fold AJ/KJ.
        (Combine with HH5 at ≤100BB — only jam if you're sure
        villain capped BELOW top pair, otherwise empty-clip
        torches.)
     
     3. FLUSH COMPLETES TURN + VILLAIN CHECK-CALLS small bet.
        Small river overbet (don't need massive size — flush
        being out already scares villain's TP).
     
     4. FLOP CHECKS THROUGH + TURN IS ACE. From Hero as
        pre-flop caller OOP: check-raise the turn (induce
        villain to bet Ax), jam river. Villain's Ace-X range
        folds to turn CR + river jam.
     
     5. VILLAIN DONKS FLOP HEADS-UP SMALL. Float flop + turn;
        bluff when villain checks river. Their range is mostly
        weak + shows up weak by river after passive float.
     
     Applies: SPR ≥3. Sizing scales to depth — at MTT depths
     <100BB, "jam river" often = 1.2-1.5x pot remaining, not
     2-3x pot.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 7 — REINFORCING RULES (HH15-HH18)
--------------------------------------------------------

These rules echo Dave / Jaka / Amit's existing coaching —
listed here for completeness and to unify the H-series.

HH15. 4-BET CONSTRUCTION: OOP = LINEAR, IP = POLARIZED 🟡
     
     OOP as 4-bettor: go LINEAR (top of range) because IP
     caller continues wide. Want hands that out-flip their
     calling range (QQ+, AK, AQs, KQs).
     
     IP as 4-bettor: POLARIZE (top of range + polar bluffs
     with A-blockers — A5s, A4s, A6s). OOP 3-bettor will
     5-bet-jam or fold, not flat-call. Bluff 4-bets have
     blocker value.
     
     Echoes: Amit rule "<35BB can't fold to 4-bet unless 3-bet
     was pure bluff"; Dave shallow 4BP construction.

HH16. PREFLOP RED-FLAG CATALOG (7 rec-villain tells) 🟢
     
     When facing a recreational player, these actions reliably
     indicate a strong range:
     
     1. Rec 5-bet jam over Hero's 4-bet = AA (KK sometimes
        becomes a fold depending on dynamics)
     2. Rec 4-bet to >33% of stack size = AA/KK (committing
        preflop with anything less is too loose for rec)
     3. Rec COLD 4-bet (no prior action from rec) = AA/KK.
        JJ/QQ/AK mostly flat-calls from recs. Extremely narrow.
     4. BB or closing-seat 3-bet vs EP open = strong
        (HH10#4 pattern)
     5. Abnormal large open size from rec (5bb+ when table
        standard is 2.5bb) = strong — 3-bet bigger than
        normal when you hold premium
     6. Rec has limping-first range AND opens = strong. Their
        open range is narrowed because weak hands go to limps.
     7. Rec LIMP-RAISES preflop = strong. Continue cautiously;
        don't auto-fold KK but don't 5-bet-jam it either.
     
     Echoes: Dave J31 (min-raise = strength signal). Extends
     catalog.

HH17. PLAYER TYPE > POSITIONAL CONFIGURATION for rec villains 🟢
     
     Most rec players open the same range UTG as BTN. Solver
     ranges assume position-based opponent ranges; reality is
     rec has ONE opening range and ONE 3-betting range.
     
     Adjust to the PLAYER, not the SEAT. When choosing whether
     to 3-bet/flat/fold, use the player profile first, then
     positional configuration as a secondary factor.
     
     Echoes: Dave/Amit general population-adaptation approach.

HH18. MULTIWAY JUDICIOUSNESS (c-bet value tightens with opponents) 🟢
     
     Base value-bet threshold scales with number of opponents:
       3-way:  minimum for value = TP good kicker
       4-way:  minimum for value = TP top kicker / overpair
       5-way+: minimum for value = overpair / 2P+
     
     C-bet frequency scales with opponents:
       HU:     range-c-bet OK on many board textures
       3-way:  c-bet selectively (value + nut-blocker/semi-bluff)
       5-way+: c-bet only nutted / nut-making equity
     
     Multiway donks from pre-flop callers are STRONG (HH10#6);
     multiway range-bets by pre-flop raiser should be TIGHT,
     not wide.
     
     Echoes: Dave shallow MW c-bet reduction rule.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 8 — RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RULES
--------------------------------------------------------

ELIMINATE LIMPING (general preflop hygiene)
  HH's "eliminate limping except in designated spots" ALIGNS
  with Dave at deep stacks. At deep-stack MTT play (60BB+) and
  all cash-style postflop ranges, limping is usually wrong.
  
  ONLY EXCEPTION: SB BvB full-ring at 30-40BB per Dave J29
  (limp 80% / raise 10% / fold 10%). This is a specific ICM
  structure that overrides the general rule.
  
  At short-handed tables (3-4 handed), J29 does NOT apply —
  wider opens are standard.

REJECTED FROM H-SERIES

  "3-bet-or-fold vs rec opens (except BTN/BB)" — NOT ADOPTED.
  Mark's logic is high-rake live cash specific. Ron's data
  confirms the opposite pattern for MTT populations:
    - Offsuit broadways from LP: flat > 3-bet (data-confirmed)
    - Historical biggest leak was 3-betting OOP from blinds
  Ron's session_history overrides HH here. Continue flatting
  more vs EP opens from LP.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 9 — ANALYZER AUTO-DETECTION (which H rules are wired
in vs manual-only for drill mode)
--------------------------------------------------------

AUTO-DETECTED in gem_analyzer.py (v7.15):
  HH5  — TP-fold attempt at ≤100BB eff (flagged MARGINAL when
        Hero river-overbets as aggressor on board where villain
        could have TP)
  HH10#1 — Continue wider than 2P+ vs villain check-back flop
        + raise turn line (flagged CLEAR when Hero calls with
        TP or weaker)

MANUAL-ONLY (drill mode prompts, not auto-flagged):
  HH1, HH2, HH3, HH4 — sizing heuristics (too context-dependent
                   for reliable automated classification)
  HH6, HH7         — opponent-selection heuristics (requires
                   villain type metadata not in hand history)
  HH8, HH9, HH14    — OOP protocols (already partially flagged
                   via existing caller-aggression detectors
                   and #1 leak tracker)
  HH10#2-9, HH11   — underbluff / overbluff catalogs (require
                   semantic understanding of opponent ranges
                   and betting intent, not reliable auto-flag)
  HH12, HH13       — value / bluff spot catalogs (concept-level
                   drill material, not pattern-matched)
  HH15-HH18        — reinforcing rules already partially covered
                   by existing J/K/Amit detectors
