========================================================
APPENDIX M — MECHANICSOFPOKER PODCAST RULES
(Probe/Delayed-Cbet Exploit, 3BP Double-FD Barrel Selection,
 Exploit-Tree Coherence, Plan-Every-Street, Population
 Tendency Catalog, Sizing Heuristics Table)
========================================================
Added: 2026-04-20 (v7.17)
Source: MechanicsOfPoker podcast (Poker Ambition / Rene + Adam)
        + affiliated Wakko lesson videos
Processed: 19 transcripts, ~1.6 MB raw material
Key speakers: Thomas Boivin, Uri Peleg, Pedro Garagnani,
              Patrick Leonard, Mateus Zinhao, Owen Prodigy,
              Nikita WWSF45, Johan Guilbert

Note: Same precedence rules as Appendices A-L. Dave rules
take precedence over M rules where they conflict. M rules
ordered by Ron-leak relevance, not by speaker or video order.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 1 — RULES DIRECTLY ADDRESSING RON'S CONFIRMED LEAKS
--------------------------------------------------------

M1. PROBE + DELAYED C-BET EXPLOIT (Pads Leonard) 🟢
    
    Population check-raise rate vs a delayed c-bet (turn bet
    after flop went check-check) is <2% across GGPoker MTT
    populations up through high-stakes.
    
    Therefore, after Hero (as PFR) checks back flop, Hero
    can minbet or small-bet TURN RANGE on the turn card
    without fearing a check-raise.
    
    Villain range after flop check-check is
    weak + passive + air-heavy (they would have probe-bet
    strong hands). Small turn bets extract value from
    bottom-pair-no-kicker and deny equity from overs.
    
    ADDRESSES RON LEAK #1 DIRECTLY: check-call-call-
    showdown OOP PFR is Ron's #1 confirmed drain (-496 BB
    across 26 hands at session-era scale). The fix is not
    "stop checking flop" — checking flop is often correct
    per Jaka A-series framework. The fix is "don't check
    TURN after flop check-check." Minbet turn range instead.
    
    GEM RULE: Flag Hero turn-checks in HU SRP spots where
    (a) Hero is PFR, (b) flop went check-check, (c) turn
    card does not fundamentally change villain's expected
    range, as MARGINAL missed-delayed-c-bet candidates.
    Do not flag when turn brings an obvious equity-shift
    card (flush completes, 3-straight, overcard pairing
    the board) — those spots require different analysis.
    
    Auto-detector: AUTO (v7.17). See analyzer plan below.
    Depth: 🟢 All depths above 25BB eff.


M2. CAN'T HOP OFF THE EXPLOIT TRAIN (Uri Peleg) 🟢
    
    Once Hero enters an exploitative branch on the flop
    ("I'm c-betting wider because population overfolds"),
    Hero CANNOT revert to GTO reasoning on later streets —
    the ranges have shifted because of the initial
    exploitative choice.
    
    Concrete failure mode (Uri's example): Hero c-bets wide
    on flop because population overfolds → villain calls
    with his weaker continue range → river arrives → Hero
    reasons "GTO calls here 40%" → BUT the villain's river
    range is no longer the GTO river range, because Hero's
    wider c-bet pulled different villain combos into the
    continue range.
    
    ADDRESSES RON LEAKS #1 + #3: Ron's drain is partly from
    mid-street reasoning drift. If Ron deviates preflop
    (e.g., flats 3-bet wide per M3 / Pads), Ron must stay
    deviated postflop too.
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): Every hand flagged as a preflop
    deviation should be reviewed for POSTFLOP COHERENCE.
    If the preflop was exploitative, the whole line should
    be exploitative. Flag hands where Hero deviates preflop
    and then defaults to GTO/frequency thinking on later
    streets as a special subcategory of Caller-line leaks.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M3. PLAN EVERY STREET BEFORE BETTING (Uri Peleg) 🟢
    
    Before any flop bet, Hero should have a concrete answer
    to three questions:
      (a) Which turns do I continue barreling?
      (b) Which turns do I give up?
      (c) What does the river plan look like on the
          continuing turns?
    
    If Hero cannot answer these before the flop bet, the
    flop bet is premature — either don't bet, or pick a
    different sizing that admits a clearer plan.
    
    ADDRESSES RON LEAK #3 (one-and-done) DIRECTLY: the
    one-and-done pattern is structurally the absence of
    (a). Hero bets flop, then reaches turn with no plan,
    and checks by default because "the turn didn't fit."
    The fix is to pick flop bets only when the turn plan
    already exists.
    
    COMPANION RULE: M4 below (float requires barrel plan),
    M5 (mixed turn bluff requires committed river).
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): When Hero one-and-dones, the
    drill question should NOT be "should you have fired
    turn" but "what was your flop plan for this turn
    card?" If Hero can't answer, the flop bet was the
    mistake, not the turn check.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M4. FLOAT REQUIRES BARREL PLAN (Uri Peleg) 🟢
    
    If Hero floats flop (IP caller, villain c-bets, Hero
    calls with no showdown value), Hero MUST have a clear
    turn-bluff plan for non-improving turns. No plan = no
    float.
    
    Floats without a follow-through plan = burn money.
    Float-and-then-check-fold-turn is the lowest-EV line
    in the tree.
    
    ADDRESSES RON LEAK #2 (Caller IP Flop Aggression)
    DIRECTLY: Ron's Caller IP flop aggression chronically
    sits below the 30-40% target. Part of that is
    under-raising; part is under-floating with no plan.
    Adding M4 as a drill prompt forces Ron to commit to
    barrel or skip the float.
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): Every Hero flop call as caller
    IP on a wet board should be cross-checked against "what
    is your turn attack plan?" Flag hands where Hero floats
    flop and then check-folds turn without a clear draw-
    improvement or scare-card trigger as caller-passivity
    candidates.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M5. MIXED TURN BLUFF REQUIRES COMMITTED RIVER (Uri Peleg) 🟢
    
    If Hero enters a turn bluff that is a 50% mixed strategy
    in the solver (i.e., half bluff, half give-up), Hero MUST
    triple-barrel the correct rivers. Mixing in the turn bluff
    and then chickening out on the river converts the whole
    line into -EV.
    
    Companion to M3 and M4. M3 says plan every street; M5
    says specifically: mixed turn bluffs have a conditional
    river commitment that Hero must honor.
    
    If Hero is tilted, tired, or not in the zone, DO NOT
    enter mixed turn bluffs on this session. Default to the
    fold branch of the mix.
    
    ADDRESSES RON LEAK #3: many of Ron's one-and-dones are
    probably turn bluffs that Hero would have continued on
    the "right" river but never reaches because turn is
    missed or check-folded.
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): When reviewing turn barrels that
    reached river and Hero checked, ask: "Was this a pre-
    determined triple-barrel turn, or a single-barrel turn?"
    If pre-determined triple, Hero must have betted river.
    Flag checks on pre-determined triple rivers as plan-
    coherence failures.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M6. 3BP DOUBLE-FD TURN: BARREL AIR, CHECK EQUITY (Wakko) 🟢
    
    In 3-bet pots (low SPR), on turn textures that bring a
    second flush draw OR complete one of two flush draws,
    population turn check-raise rate is the HIGHEST of any
    texture in the game (>8% in most pools).
    
    Hero's correct response when IP 3-bettor on these turns:
    - BET air / non-equity holdings (they lose nothing if
      check-raised; they're folding anyway)
    - CHECK medium-equity holdings (TP, OESD, combo draws,
      non-nut FDs) — because these hands are forced to fold
      to the check-raise and lose their equity
    
    Counter-intuitive. Runs against naive "barrel equity
    hands" heuristic. But the math works because:
      - Equity hand that barrels and folds to XR = equity lost
      - Air hand that barrels and folds to XR = nothing lost
      - Equity hand that checks behind = realizes equity free
    
    ADDRESSES RON LEAK #3 (one-and-done): Ron probably
    currently barrels equity hands on these turns and gets
    blown off by the CR spike — exactly the drain M6 fixes.
    
    GEM RULE: In 3BP HU, when Hero is PFR IP, on turn that
    completes or introduces a second flush draw, flag Hero
    barrels with medium-equity hands (TP, OESD, combo draws,
    non-nut FDs) as MARGINAL review candidates. Do NOT flag
    barrels with pure air (those are correct) or with sets/
    two-pair+ (also correct — bigger texture categories).
    
    Auto-detector: AUTO (v7.17). See analyzer plan below.
    Depth: 🟢 3BP specifically (SPR typically 3-6).


M7. TURN BARREL CARD SELECTION: ADDS EQUITY WITHOUT ADDING
    NUTS (Prodigy) 🟢
    
    When choosing which turn cards to continue barreling,
    prefer cards that:
    - ADD equity to Hero's perceived range (overcard pairs
      up, straight-draw card, backdoor-completing card)
    - Do NOT add new NUTS to villain's calling range
    
    Example (Prodigy's 543 flop, villain called):
    - 8 turn = BAD barrel card — adds two-pair nuts for
      villain's 87, 76 combos
    - 7 turn = GOOD barrel card — adds equity via gutters
      and straight draws but no new nuts
    - K turn = GOOD barrel card — Hero's range has many
      more Kx combos than villain's
    
    ADDRESSES RON LEAK #3: improves Hero's barrel-selection
    discipline. Fewer bad barrels = fewer one-and-done
    failures because Hero fires on the right turns and
    gives up (correctly) on the wrong ones.
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): For every turn barrel flagged
    as mistake or margin call, run the two-part test:
    "Does this turn card add equity to Hero's range? Does
    it add nuts to villain's range?" If Hero barrels a
    turn that adds nuts to villain without adding equity
    to Hero, flag as combo-selection/barrel-card error.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL (requires range-semantic
    classification not yet in analyzer).
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M8. ICM SHORT STACK ON EQUITY-SHIFTING TEXTURES (Boivin)
    🟡 ⚠️ MTT-ADAPT
    
    When Hero has significant ICM RISK PREMIUM (covered
    short stack, bubble/FT context), reduce c-bet
    frequency dramatically on textures where the NUTS
    CAN CHANGE on later streets — even with nut-level
    current holdings.
    
    Equity-shifting textures:
    - Flush draw boards (1-suited flops)
    - Straight draw boards with 2+ possible straights
    - K56 with FD, A45 with FD — boards where turn/river
      can transform the nuts
    
    Reason: Hero's risk premium makes future street losses
    catastrophic. Better to check back AK on K56fd than
    to c-bet, get raised on turn flush, and be forced into
    a tournament-life-risking decision.
    
    CONFLICT WITH J14 (Dave's monotone IP = bet often):
    RESOLVED BY PHASE CONDITION. J14 remains correct for
    chip-EV and all non-ICM contexts. M8 adds ICM-phase
    caveat: when Hero is covered short with risk premium,
    check back monotone IP more than J14 default.
    
    Detector interaction: J14 currently flags monotone IP
    check-backs as deviations. Add exception: do NOT flag
    as deviation when tournament_phase is bubble_zone or
    later AND Hero is covered AND Hero's stack is below
    stack-premium threshold (~20-25BB eff with large pay
    jumps imminent).
    
    GEM RULE: Drill-mode only for now. Future enhancement:
    add ICM-phase exception to J14 detector once Ron
    provides more bubble-phase sample hands.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL (pending sample).
    Depth: 🟡 ICM phases only.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2 — GENERAL STRATEGY RULES
--------------------------------------------------------

M9. CHECK-RAISE FREQUENCY IS ELASTIC TO VILLAIN'S 3BET-OVER-
    CR RATE (Boivin) 🟡
    
    Villain's 3-bet-over-check-raise frequency on flop is
    the single most sensitive parameter affecting Hero's
    correct check-raise rate.
    
    When villain under-3bets Hero's check-raise (standard
    populations do <8% vs a GTO ~12%), Hero can nearly
    DOUBLE check-raise frequency — Boivin's sim shows
    correct CR rate going from 18% to 36% with just a
    4-point shift in villain's 3bet-over-CR rate.
    
    Ron-applicable implication: BB defense check-raise
    rate should be HIGHER than Jaka K1-default in
    populations where regs rarely 3-bet flops.
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): For every Hero flop check-raise
    review, cross-check against villain's 3-bet-over-CR
    tendency from HUD/notes. If villain is known to rarely
    3-bet flops, Hero should be check-raising WIDER than
    the Jaka default. Conversely, vs aggressive 3-bettors,
    tighten.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL (requires villain-specific
    note data).
    Depth: 🟡 50BB+ primarily.


M10. BIG-STACK ICM SPLASHINESS (Boivin) 🟡 ⚠️ MTT-ADAPT
    
    When Hero is BIG STACK in ICM phases (bubble, FT, near
    pay jumps) and villain has significant risk premium,
    Hero can bet WIDER and BIGGER across nearly all
    textures than chip-EV default would suggest.
    
    Villain under-realizes equity due to risk premium:
    - Villain overfolds — Hero's bluffs print
    - Villain plays fit-or-fold — Hero's thin value prints
    - Villain rarely check-raises (afraid to get stacked
      below pay jump) — Hero can barrel with impunity
    
    Companion to M8. Same ICM framework, opposite side:
    - M8 = Hero is covered short → check back more on
      equity-shift textures
    - M10 = Hero is covering big → bet wider/bigger on
      all textures
    
    Ron-applicable: bounty-format amplifies M10 because
    covering = bounty collection opportunity on top of
    chip-EV and ICM pressure.
    
    GEM RULE: Already partially covered by Appendix D2
    (multiway) and J16. M10 extends to HU ICM with covered
    big stack. Drill-mode: flag Hero passive lines
    (checks/flat-calls) as big stack in bubble_zone as
    potential M10 missed-exploits.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟡 ICM phases only.


M11. POPULATION RIVER RAISES ARE VALUE-HEAVY (Wakko/Peleg) 🟢
    
    When Hero faces a river RAISE (not shove — a river raise
    that leaves behind room), population is value-heavy by
    ~60% vs GTO. Fold most bluff-catchers below two pair
    unless Hero has a specific strong blocker.
    
    Extends J19 (population under-bluffs turn CR) to rivers.
    Applies across cash and MTT formats.
    
    GEM RULE: Hero calls river raises with one-pair hands
    (TP or weaker) should be flagged as MARGINAL review
    candidates unless Hero has an explicit blocker rationale
    documented in the note field.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL (current analyzer doesn't
    distinguish river-raise vs river-shove cleanly enough
    for auto-flag confidence).
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M12. BLOCKER SIGNIFICANCE SCALES WITH VILLAIN VALUE-COMBO
    COUNT (Peleg) 🟢
    
    Blocker impact = (combos blocked) / (total value combos
    in villain's range). Blocking 4 of 20 value combos (20%)
    is meaningful. Blocking 4 of 200 (2%) is noise.
    
    Before applying blocker reasoning to a bluff-catch or
    thin-value decision, assess villain's value-combo count:
    - Narrow range (10-25 combos) → blockers matter a lot
    - Wide range (50+ combos) → blockers matter much less
    
    Refines J27 (blocker sizing). J27 is about sizing given
    blockers; M12 is about when to weight blockers at all.
    
    GEM RULE: In drill-mode review of blocker-based
    decisions, include villain's estimated value-combo
    count as a required context field. Flag blocker-based
    calls on wide-range villain as low-confidence decisions.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M13. BLUFF-CATCHER BEST-CASE / WORST-CASE FRAMEWORK (Peleg)
    🟢
    
    For any marginal river bluff-catch:
    
    Best case = villain plays GTO (reaches the bluff
    frequency GTO requires on this line)
    Worst case = villain never bluffs this spot
    
    Decision rule:
    - Best ≈ breakeven, worst ≈ stack loss → FOLD
    - Best ≈ clear value call, worst ≈ small loss → CALL
    - Best ≈ breakeven, worst ≈ small loss → CLOSE
      (use secondary factors: image, timing, sizing tell)
    
    Replaces naive "is this a GTO call?" with actual EV
    weighting across a range of villain strategies.
    
    GEM RULE: Add to Appendix I9 river decision tree as
    pre-step for any close bluff-catch.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL (requires villain range
    estimation).
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M14. SOLVER EV DIFFERENCES <2% OF POT ARE NOISE (Peleg) 🟢
    
    A +3bb EV call in a 200bb pot is CLOSE, not "always
    call." Solver outputs under ~2% of pot EV should be
    treated as genuinely indifferent, and the decision
    should be settled by exploitative context (villain
    tendency, table image, game flow), not by clicking
    the solver's recommended action.
    
    Practical application: when GTO Wizard shows a
    decision within ±2%-pot EV, Hero should:
    - Check population tendency data (MDA)
    - Check villain-specific notes
    - Check sizing/timing tells from the line
    
    Ron's own data shows many of these close GTO decisions
    are systematically exploitable in one direction or the
    other across the pool.
    
    GEM RULE: When flagging GTO deviations, apply a 2%-pot
    EV tolerance. Deviations within that window are not
    flagged as mistakes — they're flagged as "judgment
    spots" for review only.
    
    Auto-detector: IMPLICIT (already partially captured
    by MARGINAL vs CLEAR confidence tiers).
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M15. STREET STUDY PRIORITY: RIVER > TURN > FLOP (Peleg) 🟢
    
    River mistakes are pure EV loss — no future street to
    absorb them. Turn mistakes can be partially absorbed
    by solver's river play. Flop mistakes are almost
    entirely absorbed.
    
    Study-allocation implication: spend more review time
    on river decisions than flop decisions.
    
    Ron-applicable: Ron's #1 leak is a river-street drain
    (check-call-call-showdown OOP). This rule validates
    the GEM focus on river-reaching lines and suggests
    continued emphasis on river-phase review over flop-
    phase nitpicking.
    
    GEM RULE (meta / study-allocation): When generating
    GTO shortlist, weight river-mistake hands higher than
    flop-only mistake hands. Already partially implemented
    via EV-delta sorting (v7.14); M15 confirms direction.
    
    Auto-detector: META (affects GTO shortlist sort,
    already implemented).
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M16. MULTIWAY vs CALLING STATION: SKIP BLUFFS ENTIRELY,
    BET VALUE THICK (Peleg) 🟢
    
    In multiway pots with a known calling-station villain
    (VPIP very high, never folds postflop), the correct
    adjustment is:
    - Do NOT bluff at all (even in spots where GTO bluffs)
    - Value-bet WIDER and BIGGER than GTO default
    - Do NOT try to "balance" by checking value hands
    
    Balance is a non-concept when one villain range-calls.
    
    ADDRESSES J22 (3-way equity trap) INDIRECTLY: when
    the station is in the pot, equity calculations matter
    more (you'll see showdown) and bluffing combos are
    wasted.
    
    GEM RULE: Flag Hero multiway bluffs where one villain
    is a confirmed calling station as MARGINAL review
    candidates.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL (requires villain-type
    metadata).
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M17. BB DEFENSE vs AGGRESSIVE OPENER: TIGHTEN ~10-15%
    (Peleg/Boivin) 🟡
    
    Standard BB defense charts assume average villain
    equity realization. Vs a confirmed aggressive opener
    (wide RFI + wide c-bet + frequent barrel), Hero
    under-realizes equity.
    
    Correct adjustment: tighten BB defense by ~10-15%
    relative to baseline. Drop offsuit connectors first,
    then low suited gappers. Keep: pairs, suited aces,
    suited broadways (still realize equity via range).
    
    Extends J13 (BB vs UTG needs 60% equity advantage)
    to all aggressive openers, not just EP.
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): Ron's Postflop leak when BB
    defending against aggressive LP opens may be partially
    caused by too-wide defense. Review BB defense hands
    against aggressive villains separately from general
    BB defense stats.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟡 50BB+ (at <30BB equity realization matters
    less because jams dominate).


M18. FLAT 3-BETS WIDER vs MTT 4BET-OR-FOLD META (Pads
    Leonard) 🟡
    
    Tournament populations default to "4-bet-or-fold vs
    3-bet" meta. Vs that meta, flatting 3-bets wider than
    baseline with connected-offsuit and suited-gappers
    (T9s, 98s, 87s, J9s) puts villain into 3BPs where
    his range is capped at JJ-down + suited broadways
    (having 4-bet QQ+/AK).
    
    Ron-applicable: flatting 3-bets wider does NOT
    contradict Amit's "can't fold 3-bet to 4-bet <35BB"
    rule — M18 is a 50-100BB rule about what to do after
    FACING a 3-bet, not what to do after Hero 3-bets.
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): Review Hero's flat-or-fold
    decisions when facing 3-bets at 50BB+. Flats with
    middling suited-connectors vs non-premium 3-betting
    villains are generally correct in Ron's pool; flat-
    fold Hero decisions with those hands should be
    flagged as potentially tight.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟡 50-100BB (at <50BB Amit's 3-bet-can't-fold
    rule dominates; at >100BB deeper implied-odds logic
    applies).


M19. POPULATION OVERBLUFF vs UNDERBLUFF BY RUNOUT TYPE
    (Zinhao) 🟢
    
    Population bluff frequency on river varies SYSTEMATICALLY
    by runout type:
    
    OVER-BLUFFS (natural scare card lands, no SDV available
    to villain's bluff range):
    - Low-to-high runouts (3-5-9 → Q → A type)
    - Flush-completing rivers with multiple broadways
    - Three-broadway-hitting rivers
    
    UNDER-BLUFFS (brick rivers, no scare card, only natural
    bluffs — backdoor-missed, pair+draws that missed):
    - Brick rivers on boards where Hero had to air-barrel
    - Paired-board rivers (no boat reps)
    - Blank rivers on dry flops
    
    Reason: humans bluff when a "story" is available. No
    story = no bluff. Paired boards, blank rivers, and
    ace-high runouts without draws = no bluff story.
    
    GEM RULE: Tag every river in parser output with runout-
    type classification:
    - overbluff-favored (low-to-high, flush-completing,
      3-broadway)
    - underbluff-favored (brick, paired-rearranged)
    - neutral
    
    Then in river-facing-bet review, weight Hero's call/
    fold decision by the runout bias.
    
    Auto-detector: META (adds runout-type tag to parser;
    not a mistake detector itself).
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M20. MIDDLE-SIZING READ (Zinhao / Wakko final verdict) 🟡
    
    Bet sizes carry population-level information:
    - Very small (20-33% pot) = polar (value+bluff) OR
      range-bet (merged)
    - Middle (50-66% pot) = often merged middle-strength
    - Very big (>100%) = polar (value+big bluffs)
    
    Middle sizings rarely come from the top of villain's
    range (those want polar). When facing a middle sizing
    from a non-elite villain, widen call range.
    
    Standard sizing-tell application already captured in
    Appendix I; M20 adds the middle-sizing-specific
    implication.
    
    GEM RULE: Drill-mode cross-check — when Hero folds to
    middle sizings (50-66% pot), check whether Hero's hand
    beats villain's expected merged range. If yes, folds
    may be too tight.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟡 50BB+ primarily.


M21. VILLAIN RAISE-SHOWDOWN% = RAISE-CALL% TELL (Prodigy)
    🟢
    
    When a villain's raise-to-showdown% equals his
    raise-call% across a sample (meaning every raise that
    sees showdown is a value raise), villain is range-
    folding all flop/turn BLUFFS to Hero's raises.
    
    Correct exploit: raise WIDER for fold equity (his
    folds are more frequent than you thought); call DOWN
    TIGHTER (his raise-showdown range is 100% value, so
    bluff-catching is hopeless).
    
    Requires HUD data with reasonable sample (100+ hands
    minimum).
    
    GEM RULE (drill mode): Consider adding to villain-
    profile drill prompts when Ron's HUD captures this
    stat pair consistently.
    
    Auto-detector: MANUAL/DRILL.
    Depth: 🟢 All.


M22. AVOID TOUGHER REGS (Peleg / Boivin / Guilbert)
    🟢 ⚠️ MTT-ADAPT
    
    Table selection advice: VPIP LESS when a known-edge
    reg is in the hand. Six-max cash EV is path-dependent;
    avoiding tough regs = higher win rate.
    
    MTT-APPLICABILITY: limited — seats are fixed in MTTs,
    so Hero can't avoid regs at the same table. BUT rule
    applies when:
    - Ron has choice of table at SatelliteFT
    - Ron has choice of MTT to register
    
    Already reflected in Ron's own game-selection practice.
    
    GEM RULE: Meta / session-planning, not per-hand.
    No auto-detector.
    
    Auto-detector: N/A.
    Depth: 🟢 Session-planning level.


M23. MANDATORY SESSION BREAKS AS TILT CIRCUIT-BREAKER
    (Peleg) 🟡
    
    Session structure rule: build mandatory breaks (every
    90-120 minutes) so Hero literally cannot punt for 4
    hours straight. Session length as circuit-breaker.
    
    Indirect EV impact: prevents extended tilt-driven
    runs.
    
    GEM RULE: Meta / session-planning, not per-hand.
    Intra-session arc analysis (v7.14) already tracks tilt
    patterns; M23 provides the structural fix.
    
    Auto-detector: N/A.
    Depth: 🟢 Session-planning level.


M24. ADVERTISING VALUE OF WILD PLAYS (WWSF45) 🟡
    
    Running an obvious bluff early in a session that gets
    SHOWN to villains shifts their read toward "this
    player bluffs too much." Subsequent thin value plays
    and merge bets extract more for the next 2-3 hours
    vs the same villain pool.
    
    Calibrate: occasional high-variance bluffs with
    advertising value > individual-hand EV.
    
    Applies mainly in cash / deep-MTT-runs where Ron
    sees same villains across multiple hands.
    
    GEM RULE: Meta / strategic, not per-hand.
    No auto-detector.
    
    Auto-detector: N/A.
    Depth: 🟡 Cash + deep MTT runs.


M25. SINGLE-SIZING vs SPLIT-SIZING: USE WHATEVER FITS
    THE SESSION (Ron's own practice, reinforced by CGWC
    Ep 3) 🟢
    
    Both approaches are valid:
    
    SINGLE-SIZING (one size per street):
    - Easier to balance (one range per spot)
    - Harder for villain to get a sizing read
    - Works well when Hero's focus/execution isn't peak
    - Works well vs populations not searching for sizing
      tells
    
    SPLIT-SIZING (two sizes — typically small+big polar):
    - Higher theoretical EV vs GTO
    - Creates exploitation leverage (small-bet under-
      attacked by populations still on the old "33% range
      = strong" heuristic)
    - Requires strong execution to keep both ranges
      balanced
    - Works well on dynamic/connected boards where BB
      defense is active
    
    Ron uses both. Neither is flagged as an error; neither
    is systematically preferred. Context-driven.
    
    GEM RULE: When reviewing Hero's sizing choices, do NOT
    flag the choice between single-sizing and split-sizing
    as a leak. Only flag when the chosen sizing is
    mismatched to the hand category (J40-style mismatch)
    or to the population's response profile.
    
    Auto-detector: N/A (by design — no flag either way).
    Depth: 🟢 All.


--------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 3 — POPULATION TENDENCY CATALOG (LIVING)
--------------------------------------------------------

⚠️ LIVING SECTION — Ron appends to this every session when
   new pool patterns are identified. Initial entries seeded
   from podcast extractions (2026-04-20). Each entry should
   include: stake context, exploit direction, confidence.

**At mid-stakes MTT (GGPoker $100-$500 ABI, Ron's primary pool):**

- 4-BET-OR-FOLD vs 3-BETS (not flat). Rarely flats with
  KK/QQ, almost never with JJ.
  → Exploit: M18 — flat 3-bets wider with T9s/98s/J9s/87s
  to enter 3BPs where villain is capped at JJ-down +
  suited broadways (having 4-bet premiums).
  Confidence: HIGH.

- UNDER-CHECK-RAISES TURN vs DELAYED C-BET (<2%).
  → Exploit: M1 — minbet turn range after flop check-
  check. Primary fix for Ron's #1 leak.
  Confidence: HIGH.

- VALUE-WEIGHTED RIVER RAISES (~60% under-bluffed vs GTO).
  → Exploit: M11 — fold most bluff-catchers below 2-pair
  unless specific strong blocker.
  Confidence: HIGH.

- OVER-RAISES TURN ON DOUBLE-FD TEXTURES (>8% turn CR
  rate on these boards specifically).
  → Exploit: M6 — barrel air, check equity hands, in 3BP
  on these textures.
  Confidence: HIGH.

- POPULATION UNDER-3BETS FLOP CHECK-RAISES (<8%).
  → Exploit: M9 — Hero's own flop check-raise rate can
  be WIDER than Jaka default when opening-villains are
  known non-3-bettors.
  Confidence: MEDIUM (Boivin's data is from cash; MTT
  calibration pending).

**By runout type (from M19):**

- LOW-TO-HIGH runouts (low flop → mid turn → high river):
  population OVER-BLUFFS.
  → Exploit: widen river call range.

- FLUSH-COMPLETING + multi-broadway rivers:
  population OVER-BLUFFS (intuitive scare card rep).
  → Exploit: widen river call range.

- BRICK rivers on boards where Hero had to air-barrel:
  population UNDER-BLUFFS (no scare card = no story).
  → Exploit: tighten river call range; fold medium hands.

- PAIRED-BOARD rivers after flop check-back:
  population UNDER-BLUFFS check-back line (no boat reps).
  → Exploit: thin-shove top-pair+ for value expecting
  light calls.

**By villain archetype (Prodigy / Uri framework):**

- REG-FISH (default reg, not GTO, not a fish):
  → Standard play; maybe slight exploit of known leaks.

- AGGRO-REG-FISH (over-3-bets, over-c-bets, over-barrels):
  → Slow-play more; check-raise more with strong hands;
  expect thin bluffs, catch wider.

- NITTY-REG-FISH (under-attacks, under-3-bets, folds too
  much):
  → Probe more; small-c-bet wider; value bet thin; bluff
  less.

- CALLING STATION (VPIP high, never folds postflop):
  → M16: skip bluffs entirely, value bet wider and bigger.

SECTION 5 — ANALYZER AUTO-DETECTION (which M rules are
wired in vs manual-only for drill mode)
--------------------------------------------------------

AUTO-DETECTED in gem_analyzer.py (v7.17):
  M1  — Missed turn delayed c-bet. Flagged when:
        - Hero is PFR in HU SRP
        - Flop went check-check (Hero checked, villain checked)
        - Turn card is NOT equity-shift (no FD complete, no
          3-straight, no board-pair change)
        - Hero checks turn
        Classification: MARGINAL (missed-delayed-cbet).
        Rationale: population turn CR vs delayed cbet <2%.
  
  M6  — 3BP double-FD turn medium-equity barrel. Flagged when:
        - Pot type = 3BP
        - Hero is PFR (3-bettor) IP
        - Turn card introduces second flush draw OR completes
          one of two flush draws from the flop
        - Hero's hand category = medium equity (TP, OESD,
          non-nut FD, combo draw below nut combo)
        - Hero bets turn
        Classification: MARGINAL (wrong-bucket-on-equity-shift).
        Rationale: equity hands forced to fold to CR spike on
        these boards; barrel air instead.

MANUAL-ONLY (drill mode prompts, not auto-flagged):
  M2   — Exploit-tree coherence across streets (semantic)
  M3   — Plan every street before betting (meta)
  M4   — Float requires barrel plan (semantic)
  M5   — Mixed turn bluff requires committed river (meta)
  M7   — Turn barrel card selection: adds-equity-not-nuts
         (requires range-semantic board classification)
  M8   — ICM short stack on equity-shifting textures
         (pending more bubble-phase sample hands)
  M9   — CR elastic to villain 3bet-over-CR rate (requires
         villain-specific HUD data)
  M10  — Big-stack ICM splashiness (semantic; partial overlap
         with Appendix D2 multiway rules)
  M11  — River raise = value-heavy population tendency
         (analyzer distinguishes raise vs shove inadequately
         for high-confidence auto-flag)
  M12  — Blocker significance scales with value-combo count
         (requires range estimation)
  M13  — Best-case / worst-case bluff-catch framework (meta)
  M14  — <2% pot EV = noise (implicit in CLEAR/MARGINAL tiers)
  M15  — Street study priority (meta, affects GTO shortlist)
  M16  — Multiway vs station: skip bluffs (requires villain-
         type metadata)
  M17  — BB defense vs aggressive opener: tighten ~10-15%
         (requires villain-type metadata)
  M18  — Flat 3-bets wider vs MTT 4bet-or-fold meta (tension
         with Amit rule at shallow depths; drill review only)
  M19  — Population overbluff/underbluff by runout type
         (parser tag added in v7.17; mistake-detection uses
         this as context, not standalone detector)

  M21  — Villain raise-showdown% = raise-call% tell

========================================================
APPENDIX N — AMIT COACHING RULES
========================================================
Added: 2026-05-02 (v7.29)
Source: Amit (coaching collaborator with Dave) — rules
extracted from cross-session review and Day 11 live APT
consultation.

Conflict resolution hierarchy: Dave > Amit > Jaka.
When Amit and Dave conflict, Dave wins (per memory).
When Amit and Jaka conflict, Amit wins (Amit's rules
are MTT-pool-calibrated; Jaka's are GTO-baseline).


--------------------------------------------------------
N1. WEAK Ax FLAT vs 3BET / SQUEEZE — FOLD OR SHOVE, NEVER FLAT
--------------------------------------------------------

Source: Amit, Day 11 review of H7 (A2hh BU vs SB 3bet,
85BB) and H5 (A4dd MP vs BU squeeze, 85BB). Both played
as flat-calls; both confirmed leaks.

RULE STATEMENT:

  Weak Aces (A2-A8 × {o, s}) facing a 3-bet OR squeeze at
  >=30BB effective in chip-EV phases must FOLD or SHOVE.
  Flat-calling is a CLEAR mistake.

WHY FLAT IS THE WORST OF THREE OPTIONS:

  - Flat surrenders fold equity. The 3-bettor / squeezer
    has a strong, narrow range; pushing back gets folds
    from their bluff bucket and adds chips uncontested.
  - Equity realization OOP is poor at 3BP / 4BP SPRs.
    Weak Ax misses most flops, can't credibly bluff-catch
    rivers, can't credibly value-bet 2nd pair.
  - Multiway-OOP risk amplifies after flat: postflop
    runouts force tournament-life decisions with a hand
    that wasn't strong enough to 4-bet to begin with.
  - The "set-mining at deeper stacks" justification doesn't
    apply — weak Ax doesn't have set equity.

WHEN THE SHOVE BRANCH DOMINATES (below 30BB):
  Shove for fold equity + flip equity vs called range.
  At <30BB, the shove EV beats fold EV for A5s/A4s/A3s/A2s
  type combos vs typical 3-bet ranges. Above 30BB, the
  shove is too thin against a tighter 3-bet range that
  isn't folding to 5-bet jam — fold becomes the higher EV.

DEPTH BOUNDARY: 30BB.
  - <30BB: shove or fold (shove dominates with A5s/A4s/A3s)
  - >=30BB: fold (shove EV negative vs typical 3-bet
            calling range)

SQUEEZE STRICTER THAN 3BET:
  When facing a squeeze (vs facing a straight 3-bet), the
  multiway risk and OOP-postflop dynamic amplifies the leak.
  Squeeze case binds harder — even at 25-30BB, fold often
  beats shove for the squeeze flat case. (Detector currently
  uses single 30BB threshold for both; refine if Day 12+
  data shows squeeze-specific divergence.)

CROSS-REFERENCES:
  - J11: 3-bet-fold at <50BB with good equity = leak
         (Amit's <35BB rule extended to <50BB by Dave).
  - J43: ICM raise-or-fold (generalized). N1 is the
         chip-EV analog for the weak-Ax hand class.
  - V15a: 4BP flat-call non-premium at 40+BB. N1 fires
         in the 3BP case at 30+BB; V15a fires in the 4BP
         case at 40+BB. Different scenarios — both valid.

GEM RULE: Auto-detect Hero flat-call of 3bet/squeeze with
hand ∈ {A2-A8} × {o,s} at >=30BB eff in non-ICM phase.
Confidence: CLEAR. Fires under "Weak Ax Flat vs {3bet|
Squeeze} (Amit)" mistake type. Tournament-phase exclusion
prevents double-flagging with J43.

DETECTOR: ships in v7.29.
TESTS: TM91000008 (3bet positive), TM91000009 (squeeze
positive), TM91000010 (depth-floor negative).


--------------------------------------------------------
LEGACY AMIT RULES (already encoded — listed here for
discoverability, not new in v7.29)
--------------------------------------------------------

  - 3-bet at <35BB then face 4-bet: can't fold unless pure
    bluff 3-bet. Extended to <50BB by Dave (J11).
  - Don't bet OOP turns without asking "bluff or value?"
  - T9s: prefer flat over 3-bet (under 50BB; M18 covers
    deeper). Confirms reading hands as Amit's domain in
    sub-50BB range constructions.
  - Deep early SB folds with trash = correct; do not flag
    as missed steal.
  - Monotone IP PFR with 0-of-suit + willing-to-give-up:
    c-bet small for fold equity vs medium-suit floats
    (J14 sub-clause, v7.29).


--------------------------------------------------------
N2. SHOVE VERDICT PREFLIGHT (Amit hand review, v7.47)
    2026-05-12 — KTo CO 15BB squeeze-shove
--------------------------------------------------------

CONTEXT: Amit submitted a hand for review — Hero CO with KTo,
15.01 BB, PKO format, Hero bounty 22% (largest at table),
facing UTG-open (49.68 BB) + HJ-flat (57.31 BB), with BTN
(13.92 BB) yet-to-act behind Hero. Hero shoved.

INITIAL ANALYSIS GOT THE VERDICT RIGHT BUT THE REASONING WRONG
ON TWO COUNTS:

  Miss 1 — Effective stack: used Hero's 15.01 as eff stack
  because BTN "hadn't entered yet." The hard rule (Ron's user
  memories: "ALWAYS use effective stack (minimum of Hero,
  villain, or shortest active opponent) in all EV/SPR/sizing
  analysis") had been in place but allowed implicit reasoning.
  Correct eff was min(15.01, 13.92) = 13.92 BB. Hero COVERED
  BTN by 1.09 BB — a fact that materially changes the bounty
  matrix.

  Miss 2 — Bounty math direction: framed as "Hero has the
  biggest bounty so all callers are paid to bust Hero" — true
  vs UTG, HJ, SB, BB (all cover Hero), but FALSE vs BTN (Hero
  covers BTN). With BTN being the most likely caller at the
  price-in odds, the bounty matrix was directionally wrong vs
  the most relevant matchup. Didn't flip the verdict, but the
  framing was sloppy.

ROOT CAUSE:

Both misses share the same shape: a hard rule existed, but
allowed Claude to skip the explicit written step ("just keep
the rule in mind"). Smart reasoning failed where mechanical
discipline would have caught it. The pattern matches v7.21
MANUAL ADD PROTOCOL (created for a similar reason — flagging
hands as punts without running the checklist) and v7.25
INTAKE CHECKLIST (created because rules were getting documented
without being implemented).

RULE:

For ANY shove/all-in classification — Hero shoves, Hero called
all-in, Hero faces an all-in, conversational or report — Claude
must emit two preflight blocks BEFORE any verdict:

  PREFLIGHT-1: [Eff Stack] explicit one-line declaration
  PREFLIGHT-2: [Bounty Matrix] per-opponent table (PKO formats)

Full preflight specs + worked examples are in
GEM_Quick_Reference.txt (SHOVE VERDICT PREFLIGHT section).
Repeating only the framing here for discoverability.

GEM INTEGRATION:

  • DOC: This entry + Quick Ref section (v7.47).
  • CODE (v-NEXT): Detector nXX_squeeze_shove_non_blocker
    pairs with new range chart family SQUEEZE_SHOVE_12-20BB_*
    (sources pending Ron's decision: derive from PUSH +
    Amit/Dave input, or commission GTOW solve).
  • PARSER (v-NEXT): eff_stack_bb for pf_allin=True hands
    currently defaults to hand['stack_bb'] (full Hero stack)
    because the parser only computes when players_at_flop >= 2.
    Decision-point eff stack for preflop-all-in hands isn't
    stored. Either fix the existing field to compute at decision
    moment, or add eff_stack_at_hero_action_bb. Ask Ron.
  • PARSER (v-NEXT, paired with detector): hero_is_largest_bounty
    (bool), bounty_asymmetry (Hero% − mean_opp%) — needed for
    detector confidence demotion when bounty matrix is mixed.

NOT A BOUNTY-CHEAT-SHEET REPLACEMENT:

The existing BOUNTY COVER PREMIUM framework (Quick Ref
~line 2609) still applies and is correct for the HU case.
PREFLIGHT-2 EXTENDS that framework to multi-way pots where
cover direction varies by opponent. Use both: matrix first,
then apply the +3-10% EV premium per bounty-positive matchup
weighted by likelihood-to-call.


========================================================
APPENDIX N — AMIT SESSION 2026-05-12
                (N3 — N13, v7.48)
========================================================

Eleven rules from Amit coaching session 2026-05-12. Mixed
formats: principle-only (drill), detector-spec (code in
v7.48.1), and informational-pending-validation (N5).

Conflict resolution hierarchy unchanged: Dave > Amit > Jaka.


--------------------------------------------------------
N3. JTs BvB SB — DEPTH-SPECIFIC CONTINUE RULES (Amit)
--------------------------------------------------------

Two sub-rules at different depths.

SHALLOW (≤30BB BvB): JTs is in SB raise/continue range. Do
not fold JTs to a BB jam — the equity vs BB jam range plus
pot odds make this a clear continue. Sits alongside Jaka's
"any pair to 30BB BB vs CO/BTN reshove" and "KQs reshove not
flat" principles — JTs has comparable equity profile and the
same continue logic applies.

DEEP (60-100BB BvB): JTs is a standard SB open. When BB
3-bets, FLAT the 3-bet (don't fold, don't 4-bet). Has the
playability + implied odds to realize equity OOP postflop.

GEM RULE: Drill-mode only. No detector (existing OPEN charts
already cover the open frequency; the "don't fold to BB
jam/3bet with JTs" branch is read-dependent on BB sizing).
Flag manually in hand reviews where Hero folded JTs on either
branch.


--------------------------------------------------------
N4. VALUE SHOVE → BET-SMALL ALTERNATIVE (Amit)
--------------------------------------------------------

When a value spot tempts a shove, FIRST ask: would a smaller
bet extract more from villain's capped/calling range?

  - Shove gets called only by hands that already-have-it-or-
    close. Often you're stack-protecting against a beat range,
    not value-betting your TPGK.
  - A 50-66% bet gets called by all the pair-plus-kicker
    one-pair hands that fold to a shove.
  - Especially true: shallow (SPR<2), nut-blocker hands, when
    villain's range is capped without 2P+ combos.

GEM RULE: Drill-mode principle. Flag hand reviews where Hero
shoves value on the river/turn for SPR<2 and the result was a
fold or a snap-call by exactly the hand class that would have
called a 50% bet. Note: not a mistake, just a value-line
review item.


--------------------------------------------------------
N5. CBET SIZING ↔ TURN BARREL FREQUENCY (Amit, INFORMATIONAL)
--------------------------------------------------------

Hypothesis (Amit, unverified): the frequency at which villain
barrels the turn is correlated with Hero's flop cbet sizing.
Smaller flop cbets correlate with HIGHER turn-barrel frequency
from villain (villain reads small cbet as cap signal, attacks).
Larger flop cbets correlate with LOWER turn-barrel frequency
(villain reads strength, plays passive).

If validated: with marginal made hands, sometimes hero-fold the
flop cbet when Hero used a small size — anticipating heavy turn
aggression from villain.

VALIDATION GATE (v7.48 — INFORMATIONAL only):
  This rule does NOT fire as a detector or count as a confirmed
  leak. It runs as a drift-monitor stub:
    - For each Hero flop cbet that gets called, bucket by sizing
      tier (small/medium/large) and observe turn villain action
      (bet vs check vs raise)
    - Compute correlation: P(villain bets turn | Hero small cbet)
      vs P(villain bets turn | Hero large cbet)
    - Threshold for promotion to CLEAR: |Δ| ≥ 10 pp over n ≥ 200
      cbets per sizing tier
  Until threshold passes, N5 is INFORMATIONAL pending validation.
  Promote to detector in v-NEXT release once threshold passes.

CROSS-REFERENCES:
  - J19 (population under-bluffs turns): if N5 is true, J19
    becomes population-specific (small cbet pools may turn-
    barrel more).
  - M-rules: population-read framework.

GEM RULE: Drift-monitor stub in gem_drift_monitor.py to compute
correlation across batch sessions. No detector firing in
gem_analyzer.py until validation gate passes. Drill-mode hand
review may invoke the hypothesis for marginal flop-fold spots,
but mark as "Amit hypothesis pending validation" not as a
confirmed read.


--------------------------------------------------------
N6. FLOP CR FOR VALUE — SIZE UP (Amit)
--------------------------------------------------------

When Hero check-raises the flop FOR VALUE, size up.
Population calls a flop CR once for pot odds, then folds turn
to most barrels. To capture max EV from the one call you'll
get, the CR sizing should be larger than the standard CR-as-
mix size.

Suggested sizing:
  - Standard mix CR (value + bluff): 2.5x-3x villain cbet
  - Pure-value CR (this rule): 3.5x-4x villain cbet, or pot+

GEM RULE: Drill-mode principle. Flag hand reviews where Hero
flop-CRs with 2P+/sets/strong-overpairs and used standard mix
sizing (2.5-3x). No auto-detector — hand-strength tagging
requires showdown confirmation that's brittle for in-line
analysis. Sister to Jaka K1 (IP raises cbets framework) which
already differentiates value vs bluff CR; N6 adds the size-up
prescription for the value branch.


--------------------------------------------------------
N7. BLUFF SIZING — NAME THE FOLD TARGET (Amit)
--------------------------------------------------------

Mental-model checkpoint. Before any bluff bet, Hero must
explicitly name:
  1. Which villain hand class do I want to fold?
  2. How much do I need to bet to make THAT class indifferent
     or fold?

If Hero can't name the target class → the bluff has no
identified mechanism → it's a fire-and-hope bet, not a
strategic bluff.

Companion to J39 (bluff combo must block continues OR represent
river runout) — J39 covers WHICH hand to bluff with; N7 covers
WHAT size to bluff at.

GEM RULE: Drill-mode principle. In hand reviews of unclear
bluff sizing choices, ask "what was the target class?" If Hero
can't answer, flag as "Mechanism-Free Bluff" — not necessarily
a mistake but a process leak.


--------------------------------------------------------
N8. MISSED KXo OPEN-SHOVE AT ≤8BB CO/BTN (Amit) — DETECTOR
--------------------------------------------------------

Source: Amit, 2026-05-12 — Hero missed multiple open-shoves
with KXo (K2o-K9o) from CO/BTN at <8BB stacks. Existing
<8BB push/fold heuristic in Quick Ref includes "suited King"
and "broadway" at CO <5BB but does NOT include offsuit
non-broadway Kx (K2o-K9o). Amit's correction: at ≤8BB from
CO or BTN, all KXo should open-shove.

RULE STATEMENT:

  At stack ≤8BB from CO or BTN, first-in, Hero holding K2o-
  K9o, folding is a CLEAR mistake. Open-shove is the
  prescribed action. KTo+/KJo/KQo already covered by
  broadway clause; this rule adds the offsuit-Kx middle.

WHY:
  - Stack equity preservation is the dominant factor at ≤8BB
  - Kx blocks AKo combos, reduces villain's call range
  - Bigger blind ante structure at these depths boosts pickup EV
  - Folding K-high with ≤8BB cannot recover the missed BB/100

GEM RULE: Auto-detect Hero fold first-in with K2o-K9o at
stack < 8BB from CO or BTN. Fires under "Missed Push <8BB
(KXo Amit)" mistake type. CLEAR confidence.

DETECTOR SPEC:
  trigger:
    - h['position'] in ('CO', 'BTN')
    - h['first_in'] == True
    - h.get('pfr') == False
    - h.get('pf_action') == 'fold'
    - 0 < h.get('stack_bb', 0) < 8
    - hand ∈ {'K2o','K3o','K4o','K5o','K6o','K7o','K8o','K9o'}
  confidence: CLEAR
  EV estimate: -1.5 BB (matches existing Missed Push <8BB)
  type: 'Missed Push <8BB (KXo Amit)'

TESTS (TM91000018 positive, TM91000019 negative):
  TM91000018: K4o CO 6BB FI fold → should fire CLEAR
  TM91000019: 73o CO 6BB FI fold → should NOT fire (out of range)


--------------------------------------------------------
N9. MP ATo FLAT vs PFR — CHIP-EV (Amit) — DETECTOR
--------------------------------------------------------

Source: Amit, 2026-05-12 — "stop calling MP after PFR with
ATo". Ron confirmed scope (2026-05-12): ATo only, not AJo.

RULE STATEMENT:

  Hero in MP, facing a single open from UTG or UTG+1, at
  ≥25BB eff in chip-EV (late_reg) phase, with ATo, flatting
  is a CLEAR mistake. Correct lines: fold or 3-bet.

WHY ATo SPECIFICALLY:
  - Dominated by AK/AQ/AJ in UTG/UTG+1 open ranges
  - ATs (suited) plays better — flush draws, set+suited
    backdoor structure, included in MP flat ranges
  - ATo offsuit has no implied odds upside vs the dominator
    range; no flush+ace draws; no straight+ace structure
  - 3-bet captures FE vs marginal portion of opener's range
    (AJo/KQs/JJ-TT bluff-folds); fold realizes 0 chips lost
  - Flat realizes ~25-30% equity OOP multiway-risk, dominated

WHY ONLY ATo (not AJo/AQo):
  - AJo: dominated by AK/AQ but flips with TT-99, has more
    showdown value; defensible flat exists at some depths
  - AQo: blocks AK/AA more, has more equity vs continue
    range; 3-betting also defensible
  - Per Ron's confirmation (2026-05-12) — only ATo is the
    specific identified leak. Keep scope tight.

CROSS-REFERENCES:
  - J34: ICM MP flat AQo/AJs/ATs/AJo at ≤30BB = mistake.
         N9 covers the chip-EV ATo case where J34 doesn't fire.
  - N1: A2-A8 flat vs 3bet/squeeze at ≥30BB chip-EV.
         N9 covers MP-vs-PFR; N1 covers facing-3bet-or-squeeze.
         Disjoint scenarios.

DEPTH/PHASE SCOPE:
  - eff_stack >= 25 BB (below = push-fold regime, other rules)
  - tournament_phase == 'late_reg' (ICM phases owned by J34)
  - No upper depth bound (100BB ATo MP vs UTG = same logic)

GEM RULE: Auto-detect Hero MP + flat-call ATo facing single
open from UTG or UTG+1 + eff ≥25BB + late_reg phase. Fires
under "MP ATo Flat vs PFR (Amit)" mistake type. CLEAR.

DETECTOR SPEC:
  trigger:
    - h.get('position') == 'MP'
    - h.get('opener_position') in ('UTG', 'UTG+1')
    - h.get('pf_raise_count') == 1
    - h.get('vpip') == True
    - h.get('pfr') == False
    - h.get('hero_3bet') == False
    - h.get('pf_action') == 'call'
    - h.get('eff_stack_bb', 0) >= 25
    - h.get('tournament_phase') == 'late_reg'
    - normalize_hand(h.get('cards', [])) == 'ATo'
  confidence: CLEAR
  EV estimate: -2.0 BB (flat surrenders FE + poor equity realization)
  type: 'MP ATo Flat vs PFR (Amit)'

TESTS (TM91000020 positive, TM91000021 negative):
  TM91000020: ATo MP 40BB flat UTG 2.2x open, late_reg → fires CLEAR
  TM91000021: AJo MP 40BB flat UTG 2.2x open, late_reg → should NOT
              fire (AJo intentionally excluded; Ron confirmed)


--------------------------------------------------------
N10. SB LIMP+CBET FOR VALUE — SIZE UP BEYOND GEOMETRIC (Amit)
--------------------------------------------------------

When Hero limps SB BvB and c-bets a flop where Hero has TPGK+
for value, the sizing should exceed the geometric 2-street
sizing (~75% pot). Pot-sized to small overbet preferred.

Rationale:
  - SB-limp BvB pots are SMALL (2BB pot before flop)
  - TPGK+ on a static board is near-nut equity vs BB's range
  - BB's flat-call range vs SB limp is wide and contains many
    pair+kicker hands that call larger sizings
  - Geometric 2-street setup leaves chips behind for an
    overbet turn anyway — front-loading sizing collects more
    folds-for-value AND more thin-value calls when villain
    over-defends

Cross-references:
  - J29 (SB BvB framework): limp 80% at 30-40BB.
  - Jaka BvB SB c-bet by texture (Appendix C III): sizing
    varies by texture. N10 adds the hand-strength axis: for
    TPGK+ value bets specifically, size larger than the
    texture-default.
  - J38 (30BB = 2 streets not 3): geometric sizing baseline;
    N10 is "beyond geometric" for the value-hand subset.

GEM RULE: Drill-mode principle. No detector — distinguishing
"value bet" vs "mix bet" from line alone is brittle. In hand
reviews of SB-limp + flop-cbet spots, when Hero shows TPGK+ at
showdown or in the live narrative, flag as "Size-Up Review" if
the bet was ≤66% pot.


--------------------------------------------------------
N11. DEEP STACK VALUE MAXIMIZATION (Amit)
--------------------------------------------------------

Philosophy. At deep stacks (60BB+), with strong hands on
dynamic boards, prioritize VALUE EXTRACTION over bluff-catching
finesse.

Specifically:
  - Bluff-catching deep against unknown ranges is high-variance
    and EV ambiguous. Don't optimize the spot you don't have.
  - When Hero has the strong hand on a board where the next
    card could BLOCK Hero's next barrel (paired turn, flush
    completion, straight completion), SIZE UP NOW to lock in
    value before the scare card.
  - Don't slowplay sets/2P on coordinated boards just to "trap"
    — the EV of fast-playing exceeds the EV of trap-then-miss.

Example: Hero has top set on K94 two-tone. Pot is bloated.
Standard mix sizing is ~50-66% pot. N11 says: bet 75-pot to
pot, because if the turn brings a flush card, the next-street
EV collapses. Lock in value while the board allows max betting.

Cross-references:
  - Jaka deep-stack postflop framework (Appendices).
  - J38 (30BB=2 streets) is the shallow analog; N11 is the
    deep analog of the same impulse (don't be passive when
    the board threatens your value).

GEM RULE: Drill-mode philosophy. In hand reviews, flag any
deep-stack (eff ≥60BB) Hero passive-line (check or small bet)
on a dynamic board (two-flush, two-straight, paired) with
showdown 2P+ as "Missed Value (N11)". Not a detector — relies
on hand-strength + dynamic-board tagging that needs review.


--------------------------------------------------------
N12. KTs MP vs UTG — 3-BET NOT FLAT (Amit, DRILL-MODE)
--------------------------------------------------------

Source: Amit, 2026-05-12 — "KTs from MP vs UTG, it's a 3-bet
not a call."

DRILL-MODE ONLY. Depth scope intentionally unspecified at this
stage. Ron's response on scope: "not sure" — defer detector
until a concrete hand makes the depth boundaries explicit.

RULE STATEMENT (provisional):

  At mid-stack depths (likely 25-50BB), Hero MP facing a UTG
  open with KTs should 3-bet rather than flat. Deep (60BB+),
  flat may be acceptable (postflop playability + implied odds);
  shallow (<25BB), shove dominates. The 25-50BB middle is the
  3-bet zone per Amit.

WHY (provisional reasoning):
  - KTs has blocker value (KK, AK, KQ in UTG range)
  - 3-bet captures FE vs JJ-99 / AJ-AT bluff-fold portion
  - Flat invites BTN/CO 3-bet behind, putting Hero in a
    capped flat-OOP spot
  - At mid stacks, 3-bet sizing keeps Hero committed without
    over-stacking

CROSS-REFERENCES:
  - Amit T9s prefer flat (Appendix N LEGACY): DIFFERENT
    HAND. T9s has worse blocker profile and worse high-card
    equity vs UTG continue range. KTs and T9s split here.
  - 100BB OPEN charts include KTs in MP flat ranges at deep
    depth — N12 is shallower than that range applies.

GEM RULE: Drill-mode only. No detector. In hand reviews of MP
KTs facing UTG open at 25-50BB, flag flat as "Amit 3-bet
preferred (N12)". When Ron provides a concrete hand making the
depth scope precise, promote to detector spec in v-NEXT.


--------------------------------------------------------
N13. SB PAIR ≤30BB vs LP OPEN — SHOVE NOT 3-BET-FOLD (Amit) — DETECTOR
--------------------------------------------------------

Source: Amit, 2026-05-12 — "no 3-bet-fold with pair in hand
and less than 30BB. So with let's say 66 from SB vs BTN open,
can just shove with 30BB."

Sub-clause of J11 (3-bet-fold <50BB is a leak) narrowed to the
pair-class + shallow-stack case where the shove is the
specific corrective action.

RULE STATEMENT:

  Hero in SB, eff ≤30BB, facing a single CO or BTN open with a
  pocket pair. Hero should SHOVE, not 3-bet to a non-all-in
  size. If Hero 3-bets non-all-in and then folds to a 4-bet,
  it's a CLEAR mistake (J11 violation + missed shove).

WHY THE SHOVE DOMINATES:
  - Shove captures FE vs entire opener range below a calling
    threshold (typically TT+/AKs/AKo at 30BB)
  - 3-bet non-all-in lets villain 4-bet bluff-jam with hands
    that would fold to a shove → worse spot for Hero
  - Pair has ~50% equity vs called range (flips + edge); shove
    is +EV across realistic call ranges
  - 4-bet-fold gives up all chips committed in the 3-bet + FE
    + flip equity — strictly dominated

DEPTH BOUNDARY: 30BB.
  - ≤30BB: shove dominates (this rule fires)
  - 30-50BB: shove vs 3-bet is closer; both can be defensible
    depending on opener tendency; rule does NOT fire above 30BB
  - >50BB: standard 3-bet sizing is fine; J11 doesn't apply

CROSS-REFERENCES:
  - J11 (3-bet-fold <50BB = leak): N13 narrows to ≤30BB pair-
    class with the specific shove-corrective.
  - C2 (Jaka 3-bet construction): "NEVER 3-bet 76s type hands
    below 40BB" — different hand class but same depth-driven
    shove preference.
  - RESHOVE RANGES FROM BLINDS (Jaka): "any pair to 30BB
    vs CO/BTN reshove" — N13 covers the open-then-shove
    branch; that rule covers the open-then-jam-over-3bet
    branch. Same shove principle, different prior actions.

GEM RULE: Auto-detect Hero SB + eff ≤30BB + opener ∈ {CO, BTN}
+ Hero pair + Hero raised non-all-in + faced 4-bet + folded.
Fires under "SB Pair 3-bet-fold vs LP <=30BB (Amit N13)"
mistake type. CLEAR confidence.

DRILL-MODE: When Hero raises non-all-in (no 4-bet faced or
called), flag as "Suboptimal Sizing — Shove Preferred (N13)"
without escalating to confirmed mistake.

DETECTOR SPEC:
  trigger:
    - h.get('position') == 'SB'
    - h.get('eff_stack_bb', 0) <= 30
    - h.get('opener_position') in ('CO', 'BTN')
    - normalize_hand(h.get('cards', [])) is a pair (XX format)
    - h.get('hero_3bet') == True
    - h.get('pf_allin') == False (Hero's 3-bet was NOT all-in)
    - h.get('pf_action') == 'fold' (folded to 4-bet)
  confidence: CLEAR
  EV estimate: -4.0 BB (J11 violation magnitude + missed shove EV)
  type: 'SB Pair 3-bet-fold vs LP <=30BB (Amit N13)'

TESTS (TM91000022 positive, TM91000023 negative):
  TM91000022: 66 SB 28BB 3-bets to ~7.5BB vs BTN 2.2x, faces BTN 4-bet
              jam, folds → fires CLEAR
  TM91000023: 66 SB 28BB shoves directly over BTN 2.2x open → should
              NOT fire (Hero correctly shoved); negative control.
